when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她確實做了一些 , 但真正的事情是說未來會是遠遠勝過這一點 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個人出現了 , 艾倫.圖靈 , 1936年 , 又發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器完全是機械性的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	圖靈的機器是完全理論性的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩位都是從數學的角度來的 , 但turing告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不管你怎麼製造電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你電腦的機械 , 像是babbage的原本 , 或電子的 , 像是現在的電腦 , 或是未來的電腦 , 或者說 , 未來的細胞 , 或者 , 再一次的 , 機械性的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變得很小 。 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	這是一種計算機的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做教堂論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你得到了一個連結 , 你說這個東西是babbage建造的 , 真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們今天用電腦所做的一切 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓各位知道它有多慢 , 它有大約1k的記憶體 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用的是打孔卡 , 被餵進去 , 它跑的速度大約是第一個zx81的一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一個拉姆包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想的話 , 可以加上許多額外的記憶體 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天這會帶給我們哪些地方 ?
so there are plans .	所以有些計劃
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在辛頓大學 , 科學博物館的檔案庫 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴貝斯所寫 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是一組計劃我們稱之為 「 計畫28 」 的計劃 , 也是我從doronswaade開始的慈善團體的名字 , 他是科學博物館的管理者 , 也是驅動這個計劃的人 , 來建造一個不同引擎 , 我們的計劃就是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓這裡 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個項目有幾個部分可以用 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中一個是巴貝奇的檔案掃描 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二項是研究這些計畫 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是模擬那台機器的電腦 , 最後一部分就是在科學博物館實體建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能夠理解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為與其在你面前有一個小小的晶片 , 你必須看著這個龐然大物 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體操作 , 我看到cpu操作 , 我聽到它操作 , 我可能聞到它 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在兩者之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫道 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它肯定會引導未來的科學發展 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有建造過 , 因為他總是處在新的計畫中 , 但當它確實被建造出來時 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來稍微說明一下 , 用影片來呈現它的樣子 , 顯示cpu機制運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪 , 它會加上 。 這是在行動中增加的機制 , 所以你想像這台巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年時間 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們將擁有
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像填寫的演說中 , yanarsbertrand展示了他的三項近期關於人類的三項計畫 , 以及我們的棲息地 , 在他的系列《地球從上而來的》中 , 來自全球各地的個人訪談 , 在他的網頁中 , 《六十億人》 , 他很快就在出版了《人性》 , 《家園》 , 記錄了人類對環境的影響 , 透過拍攝影片 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人類、媒體、攝影、
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yannahusbertrand以寬角度捕捉脆弱的地球
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 以以飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談生態學 , 一年內我排放的二氧化碳和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我該怎麼做呢 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我回家時必須殺死一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來補充我的碳 , 就像我每次都一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上我的工作是展現我們對地球的影響 。

for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我一直密切地看著地球和它的居民 , 來自天空中的高處 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命被綁在我們星球的福祉上 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、養殖 , 仍然是世界上最不可能的人類佔據 。

we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都對地球的禮物有著同樣的需求 , 希望能在自己上升 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們卻要不斷地築起牆壁 , 才能讓我們分開 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	今天我們最偉大的戰役是要保護我們星球的自然提供 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	在不到50年的時間裡 , 我們已經徹底地改變了它 , 比起整個人類歷史上更為徹底 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源經營得很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在瀕臨絕種 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距卻越來越大 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們以比地球能維持更快的速度前進 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道 , 現今的解決方案是可以取得的 。

bf: thank you guys !	布:謝謝各位 !
dh: thank you very much !	非常謝謝你 !
in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的這個可取得的演講中 , 理查德•雷斯尼克指出 , 便宜且快速的基因組定序是如何將健康照護顛倒 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技、技術、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查.雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示了人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大x染色體的複製品 ; 男性有x , 當然 , 那份小的y複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩 , 但這只是一個小東西 , 讓你與眾不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 那麼你看到的 , 當然 , 就是這個雙股螺旋結構--生命的編碼--用這四個生化字母拼出來 , 或者我們稱之為基礎 , 對:a、c、g、t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少人 ? 三十億人 。
is that a big number ?	這是個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以在大數字附近丟棄 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把這1280-800個解析度螢幕上的每一個像素都放上一個基礎 , 我們需要3000個螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以這真的相當大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 有一群人 , 順便說一句 , y染色體就決定要將它定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 15年 , 實際上 , 大約40億美元後 , 基因組被定序並發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後一個版本被出版 , 他們繼續努力研究它 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	全部都是在這樣的一個機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個鹼基的成本大約是一美元--一個非常緩慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 沒有人知道它 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以 , 現在我們做的是 , 我們拿一個基因組 , 做成50本 , 把所有這些複本都切成50個鹼基讀本 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 大量平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	接著 , 我們將它帶入軟體 , 我們重新組合它 , 告訴你故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給各位看這是什麼樣子 , 人類基因組計劃:3gb , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	其中一台機器跑一台:一週內200gb 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天 , 那200人將會改變到600人 , 沒有這個步調緩慢的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 基地的價格 , 要定序一個基地 , 已經下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這相當於你在1998年用氣體填滿你的車子 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星 , 再回到兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc位置、所有醫學文獻的檔案、摩爾定律、舊式的定序方式 , 以下是所有新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是個木頭尺度 ; 通常不會看到像那樣的線 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界有能力將人類基因組定序 , 今年大約有五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們依據被安置的機器來了解這一點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這是預計在可預見的未來中 , 每年會增加一倍、三倍或四倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 特別有一間實驗室 , 代表了20%的能力 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因學研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對會贏得這場比賽 , 順便說一下 , 新月球 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學來說有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以 , 一個女人37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她用 「 階段2 」 的雌激素來呈現乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她帶著第三期卵巢癌回來 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她回到42歲時 , 有更多的卵巢癌 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性肺癌回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 8天後死去 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女士在短短的十年內對待的方式 , 看起來就像是血液 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	而是因為像我同事rickwilson , 在華盛頓大學的基因研究所 , 她決定要看這位女子後回 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	然後他做了序列 , 他拿了皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 和癌症的骨髓 , 他把兩者的全部基因組排序在幾個禮拜內 , 沒有什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他將這兩組基因組在軟體中比較 , 他發現 , 在其它情況中 , 是一種刪除 , 在一個叫做tp53的特定基因中 , 一個兩千個鹼基的刪除劑 , 一個叫做tp53的基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這種明確的突變 , 你一生中有90%的機率會得到癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女士沒有幫助 , 但它的確有嚴重、深刻的影響 , 影響到她的家人 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們會得到這種基因檢測 , 他們會了解 , 那麼他們就可以去取得普通的螢幕 , 他們可以早期抓到癌症 , 可能活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向各位介紹現在的啤酒雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的媽媽是一位非常勇敢的女性 , 她不相信症狀根本不符合 , 透過一些英勇的努力和很多網路搜尋 , 她得以說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的是分離性肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了dopa , 他們的症狀確實有改善 , 但他們沒有完全的異常性 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	照片裡的先生是一位叫joebeery的傢伙 , 他很幸運是一家叫做生命科技的公司 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是讓這些龐大基因組定序工具的兩家公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他做的是讓他的孩子做排序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現 , 一個叫做spr的基因中有一系列突變 , 負責製造血清素 , 其它東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在盧旺達的頂端 , 他們給這些孩子一種血清素先驅藥物 , 現在卻正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 若沒有完整的基因序列 , 這絕對不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	在幾年前 , 成本是10萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 。 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	在百元以後的那一年 , 給予或服用一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這樣移動的速度就是這麼快 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	小尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果 , 尼克出現在兒童醫院裡 , 帶著這種不良的肚子 , 就像是飢荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他不吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西時 , 他的腸道基本上會打開 , 排泄出他的腸子 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以 , 一百個手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽 , 說: 「 媽媽 , 請為我祈禱 。 我身在這麼痛苦之中 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓這個孩子的基因序列得到 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	而他們發現 , 一個基因中負責控制細胞死亡的基因突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是 , 他對食物本質上正在發生的事有一些免疫反應 , 那是天然的反應 , 會造成一些程式化的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但規範下降的基因是壞掉的 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這也說明了在其他方面 , 可以治療骨髓移植的治療方法 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的復原後 , 他現在用a1醬汁吃牛排 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	用基因組作為普遍診斷的前景 , 今天就在我們身邊 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 它就在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	對我們所有人而言 , 這房間裡的每個人都可以多活五、十年、二十年 , 只因為這一件事 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你考慮到人類在地球上的足跡 , 以及我們保持食物生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	所以 , 結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來培養玉米、小麥、黃豆 , 以及其他農作物 , 都是高度包容乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得繼續種植、吃掉基因改造的食物 , 這是我今天唯一要帶的位置 。
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非觀眾中有任何人願意自願停止吃飯 ?
none , not one .	沒有 , 沒有一個 。
this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是一台打字機 , 數十年來每台桌面的一台電腦 。
and in fact , the typewriter was essentially deleted by this thing .	事實上 , 打字機基本上被這個東西刪除了 。
and then more general versions of word processors came about .	接著 , 更多的文字處理器出現了 。
but ultimately , it was a disruption on top of a disruption .	但 , 最終 , 它是顛覆性的顛覆 。
it was bob metcalfe inventing the ethernet and the connection of all these computers that fundamentally changed everything .	它是鮑勃.米卡菲 , 發明了乙烯 , 以及所有這些電腦的連結 , 從根本上改變了一切 。
and suddenly we had netscape , and we had yahoo and we had , indeed , the entire dotcom bubble .	突然間 , 我們有了netscape , 我們有了ahoo , 我們有了整個網路泡沫 。
not to worry though , that was quickly rescued by the ipod , facebook and , indeed , angry birds .	不用擔心 , 這很快就被ipod、facebook和憤怒的鳥拯救了 。
look , this is where we are today .	看 , 這是我們今天所處的位置 。

so what i'd like you to consider is: what does it mean when these dots don't represent the individual bases of your genome , but they connect to genomes all across the planet ?	所以 , 我想請各位思考的是:當這些點並不代表你的基因組中的個別基礎 , 但它們會連接到地球各處的基因組 ?
so i just recently had to buy life insurance .	所以我最近只需購買生命保險

thankfully , i was able to answer a , and i say that honestly in case my life insurance agent is listening .	謝天謝地 , 我能夠回答a , 我說 , 老實說 , 我的生命保險經紀人在傾聽 。
but what would have happened if i had said c ?	但如果我說過c會發生什麼事 ?
consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	消費者應用在基因組學上 , 他們會蓬勃發展 。
do you want to see whether you're genetically compatible with your girlfriend ? sure .	你想看看你是否和你的女朋友在基因上是相容的嗎 ? 當然 。

there's already a lab today that tests for allele 334 of the avpr1 gene , the socalled cheating gene .	今天已經有一個實驗室 , 測試了avpr1基因的alle334 , 也就是所謂的 「 作弊基因 」 。
so anybody who's here today with your significant other , just turn over to them and swab their mouth , send it to the lab and you'll know for sure .	所以 , 今天任何跟你同在的人 , 只要轉向他們 , 再轉向他們的嘴巴 , 送到實驗室 , 你肯定會知道 。
do you really want to elect a president whose genome suggests cardiomyopathy ?	你真的想要選出一位總統 , 他們的基因組建議的是心臟病變嗎 ?
now think of it , it's 2016 and the leading candidate releases not only her four years of back tax returns , but also her personal genome .	現在想想 , 那是2016年 , 領先的候選人不但釋放了她四年後的稅收 , 還包括她個人的基因組 。
and it looks really good .	看起來真的很好 。
and then she challenges all of her competitors to do the same .	接著 , 她挑戰她所有的競爭者都要做同樣的事 。
do you think that's not going to happen ?	你認為這不會發生嗎 ?

how many people in the audience have the last name resnick like me ? raise your hand .	觀眾中有多少人有像我一樣的姓氏resnick ? 請舉手 。

so my father's father was one of 10 resnick brothers .	所以我父親的父親是十個resnick兄弟中的一個 。
they all hated each other .	他們都很討厭彼此 。

but imagine if my genome were deidentified , sitting in software , and a third cousin's genome was also sitting there , and there was software that could compare these two and make these associations .	但 , 想像一下 , 如果我的基因被拘留 , 坐在軟體中 , 第三位堂兄的基因組也坐在那裡 , 有軟體可以比較這兩個 , 做出這些聯想 。
not hard to imagine . my company has software that does this right now .	不難想像 。 我的公司現在有軟體 ,
and so imagine one more thing: that that software is able to ask both parties for mutual consents , " would you be willing to meet your third cousin ? "	所以 , 再想像一件事:那軟體能夠詢問兩黨的同意 , 「 你會願意見你的第三堂堂兄弟嗎 ? 」

okay , so experts think that one to three percent of you are not actually the father of your child .	好的 , 所以專家認為你們當中有1%到3%其實不是你們孩子的父親 。
look these genomes , these 23 chromosomes , they don't in any way represent the quality of our relationships or the nature of our society at least not yet .	看看這些基因組 , 這23條染色體 , 它們沒有以任何方式呈現我們關係的品質 , 或我們社會的本質 , 至少還沒有 。
and like any new technology , it's really in humanity's hands to wield it for the betterment of mankind , or not .	和任何新科技一樣 , 它真的是人類的手 , 讓它成為人類的好處 , 或不 。
and so i urge you all to wake up and to tune in and to influence the genomic revolution that's happening all around you .	所以 , 我鼓勵各位 , 醒來、調整、影響到你周遭發生的基因革命 。
daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾.克拉夫特示範他的骨髓採用一種新裝置 , 能快速收割骨髓 , 用最小的疼痛來治療捐贈者 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中發現的成體幹細胞 , 可以用來治療許多終端條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。
biology , biotech , health , health care , medicine , science , technology	生物學、生物科技、健康、醫療、醫學、科學、科技、技術、
daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	danielkraft發明了一個更好的方法來收集骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是一名兒科癌醫師和史丹佛大學的幹細胞研究員我的臨床焦點是骨髓移植 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	現在 , 去年jillboltetaylor的啟發我沒有帶一個人腦 , 但我確實帶來一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓就是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的性命 , 他們大多患有先進的惡性惡性 , 如白血病和淋巴瘤 , 以及其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做我的移植資產 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 。 我們這裡有bob , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 以拯救有白血病孩童的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 實際上 , 我們要如何收割這塊骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 總體麻醉 , 護士 , 另外一個醫生來自我 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃在桌子上 , 我們拿著這個小針 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們做這件事的方法基本上是把這東西放在軟組織裡 , 用針筒打穿硬骨 , 打入管子裡 , 用技術術語來啟發大約10m的骨髓 , 每次都用針筒打出去 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後將它交給護士 。 她把它壓縮成一條錫 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	將它交回給我 。 我們一而再 , 再而三地
about 200 times usually .	通常是200倍 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	我手臂的末端是索爾 , 我手上有一通電話 , 更不用說bob , 他的背部看起來像這樣 , 像是瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道 , 這個程序在大約40年沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	這樣做可能有更好的辦法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個最小的侵入方式 , 一個我們稱之為 「 骨髓礦物 」 的新設備 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓礦工 , 這裡的運作方式
our standard seethrough patient .	我們標準的透視患者
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨骼數十次 , 我們剛剛進入一次 , 進入髖部或臀部的前方 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、有力的導管 , 有一個特殊的電線管尖端 , 它會停留在骨髓中 , 跟著臀部的輪廓 , 當它四處移動時 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它能讓你很快的透過一個洞吸出豐富的骨髓 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以多次通過同樣的入口 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃只能得到一個穿刺 , 當地的麻醉 , 把這個收穫當成一對一的病人 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛得到了一個小小的贊助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	而我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到兩個大型動物 , 還有豬的研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們驚訝地發現 , 我們不僅有骨髓 , 還能得到骨髓中骨髓活動的十倍之多 , 相較於正常的裝置 , 骨髓中骨髓活動的十倍 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年才剛核准fda 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是現場的病人 。 你可以看到它跟著有彈性的曲線在周圍 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡會有兩個通過 , 在同一個病人身上 , 來自同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	在當地麻醉下進行 , 作為一名病人 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	再一次 , 我們得到了大約三到六倍的幹細胞 , 比同一個病人的標準方法還要多三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是成體幹細胞的一個非常豐富的來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很棒的潛力 , 但尚未進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們身體各處 , 包括我們骨髓中的血液幹細胞 , 我們用它作為幹細胞療法 , 已經超過四十年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年 , 已經有一場爆炸用骨髓幹細胞來治療病人其他疾病 , 例如心臟病、血管疾病、骨科醫學、組織工程 , 甚至在神經科醫學上用來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出場 , 正在商業化 , 今年 , 兩世代的骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這能得到更多幹細胞 , 轉化為更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人簽名 , 成為有潛在救命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能使你銀行你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你年輕、更健康 , 在未來你應該要用它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這是我們的骨髓移植手術倖存者的照片 , 他們每年在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者-格雷特.里西在宇宙中提出了爭議性的新模型 , 只能回答所有的大問題 。 如果沒有其他東西 , 它是你所見過最美麗的元素粒子和力量模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garrettlisssi在他對一切的理論上
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 。 甜 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我會盡我所能地描述粒子物理學的美妙之處 , 不用方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們能從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚頭都包含了數千個獨立的聚合物 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚苯丙胺酸不斷繁殖 , 變成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超智能珊瑚 , 我們可以單獨找到一個人 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問 , 他到底是如何處在這個特定的地點 , 相對於他的鄰居 , 如果只是機會 , 還是命運 , 又或者什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	現在 , 在我們把溫度調高到太高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以是相當的意思 , 你看 , 我有衝浪傷疤來證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個聚苯乙烯會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居是非常相同的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他的地點 , 但身為獨立的個體 , 體驗著他 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分支成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	與我們不同的是 , 一個超智能珊瑚可以獨一無二的準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是持續分支成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是件怪事 , 因為我們只能體驗一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子的怪異性最初由薛丁格和他的貓描述的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設定中 , 薛丁格在一個盒子中 , 有一個放射性樣本 , 由量子力學定律 , 分支成一個狀態 , 它被放射 , 和一個沒有的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本輻射的樹枝中 , 它會發出一種觸發器 , 釋放出毒素和薛丁格就死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些現實被每個個體分開的經驗分開 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	據此 , 另一種也不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很怪 , 因為我們每個人都只能體驗到一個個體的存在 , 而我們沒有機會看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	彷彿我們每一個人 , 像薛丁格這邊 , 是種珊瑚分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這個世界是如何在微小的尺度下運作的
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 做得到 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示每件事都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其他物理學的重點是描述可能發生什麼事 , 以及什麼不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 一切都來到幾何學 , 以及基本粒子的交互作用 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	而事情只能發生在這些互動完全平衡的情況下
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來描述一下我們如何知道這些粒子 , 它們是什麼 , 以及這個平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一束質子和反質子的光束會加速接近光速 , 並在碰撞中聚集 , 產生出一股純粹的能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴霧 , 有偵測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器--日內瓦的大型強子對撞機有一個十七英哩的環境 , 當它在運作時 , 畫出和蒙特利市一樣多的五倍力 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法明確預測哪些粒子會在任何個體的碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都意識到
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理的確告訴我們粒子可以產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量必須和質子和反質子一樣多 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量限制更大的粒子都沒有產生 , 而對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器這麼令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將把這個能量限制推到前七倍以上 , 超越過去所做過的事 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談論我們可能看到的前 , 讓我來描述我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整個亞原子粒子的動物園 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部份人都熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在座的許多人都做得很好 , 把他們推過來 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中性伴侶 , 叫做微中子 , 沒有電荷和很小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上方的夸克有非常大的質量 , 三者會結合成原子內的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都來到左邊和右邊 , 有反粒子的夥伴攜帶相反載荷 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也有較不熟悉的第二代和第三代相同的載荷和第一代相同但質量較高
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都和各種力粒子相互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力會透過稱為光子的粒子來接收物質 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	有一個很弱的力量 , 叫做 , 很不可想像地 , 很弱的力量 , 只會和左撇子相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用力帶有不同種類的載荷 , 叫做顏色載荷 , 再以三種不同品種出現:紅、綠和藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann這些名字--他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 還有引力 , 透過它的質量和旋轉來和物質相互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	這裡最重要的是 , 這裡有一種與每種力相關的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力相互作用 , 根據每個粒子所擁有的對應載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看過的粒子 , 但我們很確定的存在 , 是希格斯粒子 , 它給所有其他粒子的質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是要看到這個希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會不會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎團是其他我們可能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要給你們看一段美麗的可能性 , 來到這場演講的尾聲 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來計算所有這些不同的粒子 , 總共有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	那是很多粒子可以持續追蹤的 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	看起來很奇怪大自然會有這麼多的基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的載荷將它們繪製出來 , 有些美麗的圖案就會浮現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合成一個質子時 , 它的電荷就有加一的電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩個載荷的結合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們將超荷和弱荷分佈在這個二度載荷空間中粒子的載荷圖示 , 電荷就是這些粒子沿著垂直方向坐著的地方 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力的作用力 , 根據它們的超荷和弱荷 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 統一的電擊模型 」 , 它在1967年被放回一起 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以只熟悉電荷 , 而不是兩者皆是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯有很大的質量 , 打破了這個電子信號圖案的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它會使弱力非常弱 , 只要給予弱子一個很大的質量 ,
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	既然這個龐大的希格斯座落在這個圖形中的水平方向 , 電磁力的光子仍然沒有質量 , 並與電荷相互作用 , 沿著這個電荷空間的垂直方向進行 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以 , 電磁力和弱力被這種粒子在二維空間中載荷的模式所描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以將強力納入 , 通過它的兩個載荷方向 , 將力粒子的載荷以沿著這些方向繪製出來 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四維的載荷空間中被描繪出來 , 然後投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 讓我們能看到它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用時 , 大自然會把物體保持在一個完美的平衡 , 沿著這四個載荷方向 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子的碰撞 , 它會產生能量的爆炸 , 和所有四個載荷方向的總載荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都可以被創造出來 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 並且維持一個總負荷的零 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	舉例來說 , 這個弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷一定總是平衡的 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱粒子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中子 , 這三個粒子仍然會加到零總電荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持一個完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以 , 這些載荷的模式並不只是漂亮的 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們哪些互動是被允許發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中轉動這個載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察強相互作用 , 這種強烈的六角形對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的相互作用中 , 強力粒子 , 例如這一個 , 與有色夸克相互作用 , 例如這個綠色的 , 給一個夸克用不同的顏色來充電這個紅色的粒子 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的相互作用每秒鐘都在我們身體的每一個原子裡發生數百萬次 , 把原子核結合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四種載荷對應三種力量並不是故事的結局 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以將另外兩個載荷對應到重力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把這些都納入時 , 每個物質粒子有兩個不同的旋轉載荷、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間裡給一個不錯的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看它是相當漂亮的 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個圖案符合我們目前對大自然如何在這些基本粒子的微小尺度下建立的最佳知識 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們所知的肯定 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中有些粒子在實驗中所能達到的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案中 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙與這些微小尺度的運作方式是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些關於我們還不知道的事情的新和舊的想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要單單用數學來擴大這個模式 , 看看我們是否能把手放在整個enchilada上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想找到所有製造出我們宇宙的粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們希望用這張照片來預測我們將看到的新粒子 , 當實驗達到更高的能量時 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 在粒子物理學中有一個古老的想法 , 就是這種已知的載荷模式 , 不太對稱 , 可以從一個更完美的模式中浮現出來 , 類似希格斯粒子如何突破電子圖案 , 以提供電磁性圖案 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要用新的載荷方向引進新的力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們向一個新的方向介紹時 , 我們會猜測粒子在這個方向上有哪些載荷 , 然後我們可以和其他人一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們可以在六度載荷維度中建構出標準載荷 , 作為一個在七度載荷中較為完美的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這種特殊的選擇 , 應對於1973年由pati和salam引進的一大統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到幾個粒子似乎缺少的縫隙 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	一個物理學家會尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 將已建立的圖案包含為子集的圖案 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩個新力粒子的存在 , 這應該會很像弱力 , 只會比較弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中轉動這一組載荷 , 並考慮一個奇怪的事實 , 關於物質粒子:第二代和第三代物質在六度載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不是獨一無二的被它們的六種載荷所辨別出來的 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們在標準載荷空間中坐在彼此上面 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以將獨特的新載荷分配到每個粒子上 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以在八度空間中旋轉這些 , 看看整個模式會是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到第二代和第三代物質的相關性 , 由 「 試驗性 」 所產生的對稱性 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度空間中 , 這種特殊的載荷模式其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	是最大的例外謊言團體的模式 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是一個平滑、彎曲的形狀 , 有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案中的每一個點都對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的彎曲時空 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙在最小尺度上如何運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的模式生活在八度載荷空間中是精緻美麗的 , 它在這些元素間總結出數千種可能的相互作用 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的一面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們轉動它時 , 我們可以看到許多其他錯綜複雜的圖案包含在這個圖案中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉 , 我們可以透過八度空間向下俯瞰這個圖案 , 沿著一個對稱軸 , 同時看到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是一個非常美麗的物體 , 隨著任何統一 , 我們可以看到新的粒子被這個圖案所需要的孔洞 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	那裡有20個缺口 , 新的粒子應該是 , 其中兩個已經被派達拉姆粒子填滿了 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們在這個模式中的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣的稀有場地 , 但有顏色電荷 , 和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子 , 完成這個模式 , 給予我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有很深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的前景 , 偉大的數學美麗物體能夠描述粒子相互作用的真相 , 以想像的最小尺度來描述粒子互動的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這個想法 , 大自然被數學所描述的並不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的孫子書 , 它持續地開放到我們的眼睛 , 用數學的語言寫出來 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有它是人類無法理解的 ; 若沒有這些 , 它就不可能在黑暗的迷宮中遊蕩 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我曾試著遵循伽利略的指引來描述粒子物理的數學只用三角形、圓形和其他幾何人物來描述 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在研究這些東西時 , 數學可以像一個黑暗的迷宮一樣 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但讓人放心的是 , 這數學的核心是純粹、美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學相結合 , 這個數學將我們的宇宙描述成一個正在成長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在各個位置交互作用 , 根據美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的模式出現 , 使用像大型強子對撞機的新機器 , 我們也許可以看出大自然是否使用這種e8圖案或另一種圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程 , 是一場美好的探險 , 要參與其中 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合這個e8圖案的粒子 , 那將會非常非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc發現了新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那將會非常有趣 , 但對這個e8理論不利 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然對我個人來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會是多糟糕 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 挺糟糕的 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然的運作方式是非常冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論都是漫長的照片 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人很努力地知道這些想法大部分可能最後都不會對自然界的真實存在 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理學就是這樣:有很多的荒野 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	如同任何大型的投資 , 在沒有出去時 , 要放棄一行研究是很困難的 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果有東西行不通 , 你就得要丟掉它 , 再試點別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 在這種不確定性中 , 唯一能維持理智的方法 , 就是在人生中保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我竭盡所能地生活在平衡生活中 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的人生 , 平衡在物理、愛 , 以及衝浪我自己的三個載荷方向之間 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣一來 , 就算我研究的物理學都沒有 , 我仍然知道我過著良好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	在過去的10年裡 , 我大部分都住在茂伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在這是宇宙中最偉大的謎團之一 , 對我的父母來說 , 我如何能一直活下去 , 卻沒有參與任何類似全職工作的任何事 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我會讓你進入那個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊的家鄉辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的觀點相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選過非常不尋常的人生 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心租金讓我花時間做我所愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	過著遊牧民族的存在 , 曾經有時很難過 , 但它讓我能生活在美麗的地方 , 並在我的人生中保持平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我花很多時間和超智能珊瑚相處 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級智慧的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能邀請來這裡參加ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概明白其中的百分之二 , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以我會聽起來很傻 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你對所有事物的理論-garrettlisi:我很習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 它的原因至少有少數人興奮是因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是說我們應該想到宇宙 , 在它的核心中 , 最小的東西 , 是不是一個可能性的e8物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度上有沒有縮小尺度 ? 還是...
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	高爾:嗯 , 現在我給你們看的圖案 , 與我們所知的基本粒子物理相對應到一個非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	那就是我說的那個 , 我們肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這個形狀有著驚人的相似性 , 和它融入e8圖案的方式 , 可能是其餘的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點的圖案 , 實際上代表的是這個高維物體的對稱性 , 它會在我們所體驗的時空中扭曲、移動和跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們所見到的所有基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但是一個弦理論家 , 正如我所理解的 , 用較小的弦來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該怎麼看待電子在和e8的關係中 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	高爾:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當形狀在時空中移動時 , 它在扭轉 。 當它移動時 , 它會轉向我們看到的粒子 。 所以 , 它會是:e8形狀的大小 , 它和電子有何關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	變大了嗎 ? 變小了嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	高爾:嗯 , 據我們所知 , 電子是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 這些東西在量子場理論中被解釋的方式是 , 所有可能性都在同時擴張和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這也是為什麼我用珊瑚來做類比 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	這麼一來 , e8進來的方式是 , 它的形狀會是時空中每個時間點都附著的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說 , 形狀扭曲了形狀的方向 , 當它在曲面上移動時 , 形狀在扭曲的表面上 , 就是基本粒子本身的樣子 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 它們將自己呈現為點 , 並以此方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能再更清楚一點 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克里斯:這真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它正在喚起一種奇妙的感覺 , 我當然也想了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但 , 非常謝謝你 。 這真是太吸引人了 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇性黑猩猩研究者珍•古德曾談到關於tacare和其它社區項目 , 它協助非洲小鎮的人們 , 和受到威脅的動物一起生活 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍古德能協助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 果醬 , 果醬 , 天啊 , 天啊 , 天啊 , 天啊 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上睡前打來的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊傳到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一個 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上 , 我想談談我昨天離開的地方 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個神奇、三歲的澳洲孩童selam
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也曾聽說過人類的歷史、族譜 , 透過dna遺傳學來側寫 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	當時是古生物學家 , 已故的路易斯.李基 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的路徑 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	很不尋常 , 很不尋常 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在還蠻常見的 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石遺骸 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	各位可以很清楚這些人的樣子 , 從化石、從肌肉附著的形狀 , 關於他們從各式各樣的人造物身上生活的方式 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們行為如何呢 ? 這是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張──現在是個很常見的理論 , 如果我們發現行為模式類似 , 或在我們最接近的生命親戚、偉大的人猿 , 以及人類 , 那麼 , 也許那些行為在七百萬年前就出現了 , 人類的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們把那些特徵從古老的過去帶過來 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看今日在處理人類演化的教科書 , 你經常會發現有人在推測早期人類的行為 , 基於黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	比起其他生物 , 它們更像我們 , 我們在ted大會上也聽過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 它仍然讓我對黑猩猩的行為做出評論 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每一隻黑猩猩都有他或她自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們名字 。 他們可以活到60年以上 , 雖然我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲先生 。 雌性的寶寶在十一或十二歲時就有了她的第一個寶貝 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她只有一個嬰兒 , 每五、六年就有一段長期的童年依賴 , 當孩子在療養時 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 然後騎在她背上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這長久以來的童年對黑猩猩是很重要的 , 就像對我們來說 , 學習的關係一樣 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同形式的動物演化過程中變得更加複雜所以我們發現學習在一個個體的生命史上扮演著更重要的角色
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	而年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀看他們的長輩們所做的事 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道 , 他們有能力模仿他們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 它是以這種方式呈現現在在非洲所有不同黑猩猩族群中所看到的不同的工具工具行為 , 如何從一個世代傳到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 這樣我們才能將這些工具行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語的語言 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 其中許多都很相似 , 甚至相同的 , 以相同的情境形成 。 希臘的黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	牠們還親吻 , 手牽手 , 背部拍打 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	牠們會游泳 , 會扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現很多很多的例子都是同情心、愛和真正利他主義的先驅 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對他們的本質有黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極度殘酷 , 甚至類似原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常具攻擊性的行為 , 大部分的情況下 , 都是針對鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	牠們非常具有侵略性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信 , 黑猩猩 , 比起其它的生物 , 已經幫助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物界之間沒有一條尖銳的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 隨著我們做更多的觀察 , 不斷地變得更加模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究 , 至今仍持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 生活在野外複雜的社交生活 , 幫助了我們更加瞭解到我們是其中的一員 , 而不是與我們共享這個星球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 發現黑猩猩和世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 都在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是從空中拍攝的一張照片 , 它讓你看到戈姆貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時我在16年前飛過整個區域 , 才發現 , 在公園外 , 這片森林 , 在1960年 , 這片森林幾乎沒有破裂 , 沿著塔昆尼卡湖邊的東岸 , 也就是那個小小、30平方公園的所在地 , 一個問題來到我腦海 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們怎麼能試著拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 , 當居住在國家公園附近的人都在掙扎求生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比這片土地能支撐的人還多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民的數量從緬甸湧入 , 和來自剛果湖邊的數量增加 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	而非常貧窮的人他們負擔不起從別處買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個程式 , 我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	用一種非常全面的方式來改善那些住在公園附近村莊的人的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村莊開始 , 現在是24個 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探討它 , 但它包含了像樹木護士這種東西 , 最適合耕種的方法 , 這種方式現在已經非常退化 , 幾乎在這些山區幾乎是沙漠地帶 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤侵蝕的方式 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重獲過度使用的農地 , 讓兩年內 , 能再次有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力幫助村民從井中取得新鮮水源 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許蓋一些學校 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和一小群婦女合作 , 提供她們機會給小額貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同全世界的情況 , 我們有95%的貸款回來 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性力量 , 與教育合作 , 為女孩們提供獎學金 , 讓他們能完成中學 , 清楚了解到 , 全世界的女性教育都在改善 , 家庭規模下下下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供關於家庭計畫的資訊 , 以及關於愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果是 , 有些事發生在保育上 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	為了保育 , 農夫住在這24個村莊 , 而不是把我們看成是一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順便說一句 , 許多工作人員現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始做坦尚尼亞的工作時 , 卻是坦尚尼亞團隊進入村莊 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞團隊和村民談話 , 問他們感興趣的是什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育有興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 ; 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間的推移 , 當他們的情況開始改善時 , 他們開始更加了解對保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解到 , 隨著山丘的上層起伏不定的樹木 , 所以你會有這種糟糕的土壤侵蝕和泥巴 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展我們所謂的更大的gombe生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是國家公園之外的一個區域 , 伸展到這些非常退化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村莊有更好的生活水準時 , 他們其實同意把他們土地的10% ~ 20%的土地放在高地的一旁 , 所以當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩會透過它穿梭在國家公園以外的其他遺傳族群間的互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是一個成功的
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地方複製它 , 其它的荒野地區 , 都面臨著極端人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 如同我們剛才討論過的這幾天的ted , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很多貧窮問題 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	而當你有大量的人住在陸地上 , 並不是那麼肥沃 , 特別是當你砍掉樹木 , 離開土壤開放到風中 , 隨著絕望的人口砍伐越來越多的樹木 , 這樣他們就可以試著為自己和家人種植食物 , 接下來會發生什麼事 ? 一定要給他們什麼 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	而其他問題不只在非洲 , 還有其他開發中國家 , 的確 , 不論我們在哪裡對我們的星球有什麼影響 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家e.o.威爾森說 , 如果地球上每一個人都能維持平均歐洲或美國人的生活水準 , 我們需要三個新星 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說了四個 。 但我們沒有他們 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題來了 , 在這裡 , 我們可說是有史以來最聰明的生物 , 帶著這個非凡的大腦 , 能夠用這些ted大會來說明的科技 , 但我們卻在破壞我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決定之前 , 曾經坐在身邊 , 自問: 「 這個決定如何影響我們的人 , 領先七個世代 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決策和我不是特別在談論非洲 , 但已開發的世界重大決策包含了數百萬美金 , 以及數百萬人 , 經常是基於 「 這會如何影響下一個股東的會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響到非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始到非洲各地旅行 , 談論黑猩猩所面臨的問題 , 以及他們消失的森林 , 我了解到 , 這麼多非洲的問題 , 可能會落在之前殖民地剝削的門口 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	於是我開始到非洲境外旅行 , 在歐洲演講 , 在美國演講 , 前往亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些糟糕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	而且你知道我說的那種 , 我說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣經常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水可能是這個世紀我們會面臨最關鍵的議題之一 , 到處都有水被農業、工業和家庭化學品污染 , 這些化學品仍然被世界各地噴灑 , 似乎無法從過去經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林正在被砍伐 ; 像海嘯這種東西的影響會變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有輕率的燃燒化石燃料 , 和其他溫室氣體結合 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在世界各地 , 人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候有很大的問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混合在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是那些被影響較差的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	是已經受到影響的非洲 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 旱災嚴重多了 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來臨時 , 通常會導致洪水 , 加上苦惱 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而居住的土地的人數卻無法支援、貧窮到無法購買食物的人數 , 因為整片土地都被降解了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化的裂縫 , 令人毛骨悚然 , 當最後一棵樹被砍掉時 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	而這種東西並不只是在非洲 , 全世界都有 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到了好多年輕人似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為 , 是否可能有某種程度的差異存在於這種異於聰明的大腦 , 那種ted科技的表徵 , 人類的心臟 ? 以非科學的角度來談論它 , 以愛和同情的角度來看 。 是否有一些不切實際的差異呢 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上 , 他們不是憂鬱或冷漠 , 或痛苦 , 或多或少都說過同樣的話 , 「 我們會覺得這樣 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 沒有我們能做的事 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們 , 我想我們如何在我年紀的時候就已經傷害到這個美麗的星球 , 我就感到這種絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	導致了這個計畫 , 我們稱之為根與芽 , 它從坦桑尼亞這裡開始 , 現在已經擴散到全世界的97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 , 根基製造一個堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊似乎微不足道 ; 要抵達太陽 , 它們能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為地球上所有的問題 , 環境和社會的問題 。 這是個希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人都能突破 , 為所有生物創造更美好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息:我們每一個人每一天都會造成不同 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每一個人 , 我們都有選擇 , 選擇要做出什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	貧窮的人別無選擇 。 我們要改變窮人的選擇 , 讓窮人也能選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽團體全都選擇了三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們有多老 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論是在城市或鄉村 , 都取決於什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有來自幼兒園的計畫 , 透過大學 , 有越來越多的成人開始他們自己的根部和芽團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每一組都選擇了 , 在他們之間 , 三種不同的專案計畫 , 來讓這個更美好的世界 , 意識到所有這些不同的問題都互相連結 , 互相阻礙 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們其中一個計畫 , 就是要協助他們自己的人類社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能夠 , 他們可能會募到資金 , 來協助世界上其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項計畫是幫助動物 , 不僅僅是野生動物 , 家庭動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們其中的一個計畫是幫助我們共同的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	這一切都是一個訊息 , 傳達的是學習在我們內在的和平與和諧的生活 , 在我們的家庭中 , 在我們的社區中 , 在文化之間 , 宗教之間 , 和我們之間的關係 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能以我們現在的速度去破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有比這一個星球還多 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要挑選非洲這裡的一兩個項目 , 根部和槍枝團體正在進行 , 一、兩項項目只有在坦尚尼亞、肯亞、南非、剛果、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆 , 和其他團體 。 如我所說 , 它在世界上97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種樹 , 種有機蔬菜
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營裡工作 , 帶著雞肉 , 為了一點錢賣雞蛋 , 或只是用牠們來餵飽家人 , 感受到自豪和賦予自豪感 , 因為牠們不再無助 , 取決於他人 , 用牠們的蔬菜和雞肉 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理上的幫助 , 給予那些出類拔萃的士兵 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做這樣的計畫 , 就是把他們從自己身上帶出來 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會中有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們也在監獄裡有這個程式 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在已經沒有更多根與芽的時間了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的重要要素 , 老年的孩子和年輕的孩子談話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而無需懷孕之類的年輕人會從其他年輕人聽得更好 , 而不是成人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看過黑猩猩數量從本世紀的一百萬人下降到現在的十五萬人數 , 和其他許多動物都一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失 , 曾經有森林的沙漠
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 可以嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是這個驚人的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想這些技術 ,
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後 , 我很興奮 , 終於來到大家談堆肥式廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	它是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只要把這些水沖到梯底下 , 真是太糟糕了 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	然後談到再生能源迫切重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否在乎我們的孩子的星球 ?
