how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有孩子或孫子、姪兒、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們在乎他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們 , 身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們就能做點什麼 。 我們能做出選擇 , 做為我們每天的生活方式 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買的東西 。 我們穿的是什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	而選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	他或她長大後會如何影響我孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 或其他的 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 和人類的心情結合 , 我們在世界各地加入雙手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這正是ted對我們的幫助 , 谷歌幫助了我們 , esri也在幫我們繪製gombe國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們可以使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 它已經開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你們已經聽說過了 , 已經開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 要看到我們必須要有的改變 , 如果我們在乎未來 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	而希望自然的下一個理由是驚人的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以拿一個完全被摧毀的區域 , 只要時間和一些協助 , 就能讓它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	舉個例子 , 就是tacare計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴各位 , 看似死掉的樹木 , 如果你停止砍伐它們 , 你不需要因為你有很多木頭 , 那麼在五年內 , 你就可以有一棵三十英呎的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在滅絕的邊緣 , 可以得到第二次機會 。 那是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這真是令人鼓舞人心 。 這也讓我帶到我最後一類的希望 , 我們在過去兩天中聽過這一點:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種不屈不撓的人類精神的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 讓那些你認為會被貧窮、疾病、或其他類型的人 , 可以把自己從中拉出來 , 有時 , 用協助他們在社會中 , 帶領他們的一部分 , 帶領他們參與改變世界的一部分 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想在非洲中有一兩個人 , 他們真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出一張很長的清單 , 但很明顯的 , 納爾遜•曼德拉 , 從十七年的艱難體驗勞工 , 23年的監禁 , 有著這驚人的寬恕 , 讓他能帶領他的國家走出種族隔離的惡行政權 , 卻沒有血腥洗澡 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	kensarowiwa , 在奈及利亞 , 拿了巨型石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人都試過他們最好的 , 但卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是如此鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 是年輕非洲人需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 我今天也聽過其中的一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我真的很感激這個機會再次與ted的所有人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人能聚在一起 , 談論其中的一些事情 , 特別是根與芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後 , 那個正在經營這整個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天遇到了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她非常興奮 , 有了她的認證 。 她是根與芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在達爾斯薩拉姆的領導階層
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說是幫助她去做她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 我非常興奮 , 去見她 , 看看年輕人如何被賦予權力 , 有機會採取行動 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們對明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家diannacohen分享一些艱難的真相 , 關於海洋中的塑膠污染 , 以及我們生命中的一些想法 , 關於如何將我們從塑膠漩渦中解放出來 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、使命藍、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	diannacohen:關於塑膠污染的艱難真相
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在和塑膠袋一起工作 , 我把塑膠袋剪下來 , 縫合起來成為我過去二十年來的藝術品的主要材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二維立體的片段 , 雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	在與塑膠合作的過程中 , 在大約八年後 , 我的一些作品開始裂開 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	和我們一樣 , 簡直是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在我進一步教育我自己 , 關於塑膠 , 我其實意識到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分解成較小的部分 , 因為塑膠總是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多都在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	在過去的幾年裡 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾場和健身房 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是--我認為這是很多人最初學習的反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得去那裡清理這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我真的開發了一個提案 , 用一艘貨船出去 , 和兩艘被分解的漁船拖網 , 一台起重機 , 一台壓碎機 , 和一台冷冰機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是 , 去健身房 , 提高對這個議題的認知 , 並開始拿起塑膠 , 將它變成一點點 , 冰冷的模塊 , 可以用來當作在開發社區裡建材的磚塊 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和那些真的去過健身房的人談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 這麼做時 , 我了解到 , 清理它會是一滴很小的滴水 , 相對於全世界每天都產生了多少東西 , 我得要回頭看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的照片是:我們需要找到一個方法來關掉水龍頭 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要用單一用途和丟棄的塑膠來切片這些塑膠每天進入海洋環境以全球性的規模 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著那個 , 我也意識到我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠 , 你還在想在太平洋的中央 , 我發現現在世界上有11個塑膠垃圾 , 世界上有5個主要海洋 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不只是我關心的塑膠垃圾漩渦 , 而是超市裡的塑膠 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 我所有的食物都是用塑膠包裝 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都用塑膠包裝 , 甚至在健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我關心從塑膠進入我們體內的塑膠和毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以 , 我和一群其他人一起 , 他們都在看這個議題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多我們正在努力的倡議 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	其一是:如果我們在海洋中發現的海洋碎片中有80%到90%是塑膠 , 那我們為什麼不把它稱為它 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	把所有人都回收起來 , 用回收的概念來結束他們的書 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放進一個桶子裡 , 不用再想一想 。
what is the reality of that ?	究竟是什麼樣的現實 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 只有不到7%的塑膠被回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的深入探究 , 尤其是當涉及到塑膠瓶時 , 大部分只會被降級回收 , 或被打開 , 或是被運到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降級 , 轉變為較少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶又可以是玻璃瓶 , 或可以再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會是塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們正在看著並要求大家思考的事是 , 我們在 「 減量、再利用、回收 」 前面加了一個第四個r , 也就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	不論何時 , 都拒絕使用單一和丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些則是非常古老的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我自己現在正在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 用這些而不是玻璃和tupperware的容器來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和我的家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易拿起一瓶不銹鋼瓶或玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行 , 且你忘了帶你的不銹鋼瓶 , 填滿水或過濾水 , 和購買塑膠瓶的水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想對在座的各位說的是 , 我知道在座的各位都知道這個議題 , 就是海洋中有個很大的問題 , 但這是個我們身為消費者、我們可以解決的問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以透過提高對議題的認知 , 來解決這個問題 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 不論何時 , 若要選擇針對單一使用塑膠的替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這條幹道綁在我們的海洋中 , 如此一來 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這個從麻省理工學院的pattiemaes的實驗室做示範 , 由pranjestry所做的 , 是ted的buz 。 它是一個可穿戴的裝置 , 上面有一台投影機 , 為我們環境帶來深刻的互動 。 想像一下 「 少數民族報告 」 , 接著有一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、介面設計、科技、
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派蒂•梅斯和帕拉夫•福瑞示範第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很感興趣 , 關於我們是否可以演化或發展出第六感 , 一種使我們無縫地接觸和容易取得的元素或資訊 , 這種資訊可能和我們有關 , 來協助我們做出對的決定 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	在座有些人可能會爭論 , 嗯 , 今天的手機不早就這麼做了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted這裡遇見一個人 , 當然 , 這是最頂尖的網絡場所 , 你不會握某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能在我拿出手機和谷歌搜尋你的時候緊握住一會兒嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者 , 當你到超市站在那裏 , 你不會拿出你的手機 , 打開一個瀏覽器 , 去一個網站 , 試著決定這些不同的衛生紙是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們其實並不容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 只能協助我們做出最佳的決策 , 關於接下來要做什麼 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以 , 我在媒體實驗室的研究小組一直在開發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能用一種簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 而不需要使用者改變任何他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭露我們最新的努力 , 目前為止 , 最成功的努力 , 這在過程中仍然是一項工作 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在戴著這個裝置 , 我們已經把它拼湊起來 , 用那些從架子上脫下來的零件 , 順便說一下 , 在這個時候 , 只需花350美金 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式、電池驅動的投影系統 , 用一個小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在我的口袋裡傳達給我的手機 , 用來當作溝通和計算設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕拉夫•福瑞 , 他真的是那個一直在實施和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統如何讓他走到任何表面 , 開始用他的手去和前面投射的資訊進行互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統會追蹤四隻顯著的手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個案例中 , 他戴著你可能認得的簡單標記帽子 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個比較時髦的版本 , 你也可以用不同顏色來畫指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	相機基本上會追蹤這四隻手指 , 辨認出他做出的任何姿勢 , 讓他可以去 , 例如 , 一張長灘的長灘地圖 , 放大 , 等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出有代表性的手勢 , 例如 「 拍照 」 手勢 , 然後拍下你面前的任何東西 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以直接走到任何一面牆上 , 投射所有他拍攝的圖片 , 將它們整理起來 , 然後再次使用所有自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 你們其中一些人很可能在兩年前 , 看到了jeffhan , 或有些人可能會想: 「 嗯 , 這看起來不像微軟的表面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別在於 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面上 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以用 , 和這個投射資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜式的 , 而且可以是...
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 其中一個重要的差異是 , 它完全是行動了 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的不同點在於 , 在質量生產上 , 明天它的成本不會比現在的手機還高 , 實際上 , 並不是一個更大的包裝 , 看起來比我在脖子上穿的這個版本還要多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但除了讓你們其中一些人在《少數報告》中看起來像湯姆•克魯斯的幻想之外 , 我們之所以對這個裝置感到很興奮 , 是因為它真的可以作為這六分之一的裝置 , 給你相關的資訊 , 讓你知道你面前的是什麼 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到pranav進入超市 , 他正在購物一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起產品時 , 這個系統可以辨認出他所撿到的產品 , 使用圖像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠光或橘光 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以尋求額外的資訊
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個特別的選擇是特別好的選擇 , 因為他個人的標準 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	在座有些人可能想要馬桶紙 , 裡面有最多的白化紙 , 而不是最環保責任的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿出一本書 , 他可以拿到亞馬遜的評價 , 就直接投射在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的講者 , 順便說一下 , 在亞馬遜 , 得到很棒的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納把書的頁面轉過來 , 接著 , 可以看到關於書本讀者評論的額外資訊 , 也許是他最喜歡的評論家等等的資訊 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉向某個特定的頁面 , 他會發現我們朋友的註解 , 可能會給他一點額外的資訊 , 關於那個頁面上的東西 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀它從來不需要過時的報紙 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以拿到關於你所讀到的事件的影片註冊 , 可以得到最新的體育分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是一個更有爭議的
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted和某人互動時 , 也許你能看到標籤的字雲 , 和那個人在部落格和個人網頁中相關的字詞 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你你的飛行被延遲 , 登機門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道現在的時機是什麼 , 就如同在你的手臂上畫一支手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前所處的第六感 , 給予我們無縫的資訊 , 關於我們可能遇到的事物 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕拉夫 , 他真的 , 就像我說的 , 這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確值得很大的鼓掌 , 因為我不認為他在過去的三個月裡睡得太多 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友也可能對他也不太高興 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但現在還不完美 , 進步非常多 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 也許在另一十年內 , 我們會來到這裡 , 最後的第六感大腦植入 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里格斯和艾卡•艾瓦菲 , 有個強而有力的友誼 , 出生在不可思議的損失 。 羅德里格斯的兒子在2001年9月11日被殺害 ; 2001年9月11日 , 艾瓦菲的兒子祖拉斯被定罪於那些攻擊中所扮演的角色 。 希望找到一個和平的和平 , 這兩個媽媽已經開始彼此了解並尊重 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	九一一一治癒:那些發現寬恕、友情的母親、
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲利斯•羅德里格斯:我們今天在這裡 , 是因為我們有大多數人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	但現在 , 我們卻覺得很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次了解到 , 我兒子在世貿中心 , 在2001年9月11日的早晨 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他有沒有死 , 直到36小時後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們國家要用我們兒子的名字來做什麼──我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它 , 但 , 透過震驚 , 可怕的震驚 , 以及我們生命中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們沒有報復 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個星期後 , 當zacariasmoussaoui被指定為有六數個陰謀 , 來犯下恐怖主義 , 而美國政府呼籲他死刑 , 如果定罪了 , 我和我的丈夫 , 公開場合 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過那和透過人權團體 , 我們和其他幾個受害者的家人在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 在她的兒子被指控的時候 , 我心想: 「 真是個勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天我想要見到那個女人 , 當我更堅強的時候 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲痛中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或者我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我馬上得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她兒子被指控的是什麼時 , 她沒有得到那樣的同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難等同於我的
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以 , 我們在2002年11月見面 , 現在 , aicha會告訴你這是怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmooussaoui之母 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我要求人權組織把我和受害者的父母親接觸 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們向我介紹了五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	然後我看到了生理 , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是團體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姊妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	我身為母親所受的許多苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我14歲時就結婚了 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 第二個孩子 , 在我十六歲時 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以 , zacarias的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	而我仍然受苦 , 因為我的兒子就像是他活著地埋葬著 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她的兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 。 我不知道他是否受到折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	所以 , 這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 讓我的苦難對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對於所有的女性 , 所有賦予生命的母親 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	要靠我們女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定要親手幫忙 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女性 , 而是為了我們 , 對我們女人 , 對我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我對抗暴力、對抗恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校和年輕的穆斯林女孩談話 , 這樣她們才不會接受嫁給她們的意願很年輕 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 並盡量避免她們結婚和受苦 , 這就好到不行了 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我會站在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說 , 我從aicha開始 , 從那天開始 , 我們第一次和其他家族成員會面──那是非常私密的會議 , 因為那是2002年11月的事 , 而且 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕那個時代的超級報復主義──那些我們家族成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都這麼緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼想見我們 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	接著 , 她很緊張 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 我們為什麼想見她 ? 」

then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們坐在一個有支援、有協助的圈子裡 , 來自這種和解的人們 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha開始了 , 她說: 「 我不知道我兒子是否有罪或無辜 , 但我想告訴你 , 我對你家人所發生的事有多麼的遺憾 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道痛苦是什麼 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該被公平地審判、懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她用那種方式向我們伸出手 , 我想說的是 , 這是個冰箱 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	後來發生的是 , 我們都說出我們的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分聯繫起來 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午結束時 , 午餐後約三小時 , 我們覺得好像我們永遠認識彼此一樣 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不只能在當下的情況下變得如此慷慨 , 及當時的狀況 , 以及她兒子的人生 , 還有她所擁有的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過有這麼辛苦人生的人 , 從我自己的文化和環境完全不同 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特別的連結 , 我非常重視 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我覺得這一切都在害怕對方 , 但要踏出那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這實在不是那麼難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還有誰能見到我不知道 , 或說我和誰有這麼大的不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字要做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	艾瑞克:我想說 , 我們得試著認識其他人 , 另一個人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須要大方 , 你的心一定要大方 , 你的心智一定要大方 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定要被容忍 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。

this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多人無法取得乾淨的飲用水 。 工程師麥可•普立奇做了點什麼 , 發明了可攜式的lifesaver濾水器 , 可以在幾秒鐘內讓最多人飲用水 。 一個來自tedglobal2009年的驚人展示 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業 , 設計 , 設計 , 全球議題 , 發明 , 科技 , 水源 , 水資源 ,
michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	michaelpritchard的水過濾器把骯髒的水變成可飲用的水 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談幾件事情
the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都在享受過去幾天來這裡提供的水 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得它是來自一個安全源頭 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是這樣呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果是從這樣的源頭來的呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	然後統計數字會說 , 你們當中有一半的人現在都在受痢疾所苦 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	過去我談了很多關於統計 , 提供所有人安全飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎沒有經歷過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經知道為什麼了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	這是因為 , 使用目前的思維 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法思考解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就切掉了:我們 , 政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	嗯 , 今天 , 我想向各位說明 , 透過不同的思考方式 , 問題已經解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順帶一提 , 自從我一直在說話以來 , 世界上另外一萬三千人現在正遭受著痢疾問題 。
and four children have just died .	而四個孩子剛剛過世 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和在座的各位一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節後的那天 , 當時我正在看亞洲海嘯的消息 , 一邊捲進來 , 一邊在電視上演 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的日子和數週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下受污染的水 , 或面臨死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	那真的困住了我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風陷入美國的側邊 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這裡有一個第一世界國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你們知道要花五天才能把水送到超級dome嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相射殺電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我決定要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 在接下來的幾週、幾個月 , 同時在我廚房裡 , 讓我太太感到不滿 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 在幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想到了這個 , 命運瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好 , 現在 , 科學方面來說 ,
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifsaver之前 , 最好的手過濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒 , 大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以這絕對會穿過那200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	lifesaver濾水孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有什麼是穿過的 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我要給你們一點示範 。
would you like to see that ?	你們想看一下嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了所有時間設定這些 , 所以我猜我應該
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們在牛津的精緻城市裡 ,
so someone's done that up .	所以有人這麼做了 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	牛津良好的城市 , 所以我做的是從河流中取得一些水 , 河流的泰姆斯 , 流過這裡 。 這就是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我在想 , 你知道 , 如果我們在孟加拉的洪水區中間 , 水就不會長這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以我就去找了一些東西來加進去 。
and this is from my pond .	而這是從我的池塘出來的 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	有一個氣味 , 攝影師先生 。
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們只會把它倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	michaelprichard:好的 。 我們有一些從污水工廠來的 。
so i'm just going to put that in there .	所以我就把它放進去吧 。
put that in there . there we go .	放進去吧 。 開始吧 。
and some other bits and pieces , chuck that in there .	還有一些其他的位元和碎片 , 把裡面的部份切下來 。
and i've got a gift here from a friend of mine's rabbit .	而我這裡有一位朋友的兔子的禮物 。
so we're just going to put that in there as well .	所以 , 我們也要把它放進去 。
the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	lifsaver濾水瓶真的很簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水往上放 ,
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一個標籤來向你們展示 。 讓你們看一下 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	那還不夠髒 。 讓我們稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好吧 , 我現在要拿這個真的骯髒的水 , 把它放進這裡 。 你還想喝嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好吧 。 開始吧 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它幾個泵 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這都是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一滴滴水 , 無菌的飲用水就會出現 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我得快點 。 好 , 準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	來吧 。 請注意電流 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全的 , 無菌的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	去了克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	它的味道是什麼 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看克里斯在整個節目的其他節目 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好 。 lifesaver濾水瓶是全世界數千人使用的 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它會持續六千公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它過期時 , 使用失敗的技術 , 系統會關掉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把卡特里打出來 , 再打個新進來 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	它對另外六千公升有益 。
so let's look at the applications .	所以 , 我們來看看應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	然後 , 在幾週後 , 我們設立營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	而人們被迫走進難民營 , 以取得他們安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在一個營中 , 會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病散播開來 。 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題就在於自我延續 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但藉由不同的思維 , 並且運送這些 , 人們可以保持著 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌的飲用水 , 開始重建家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	現在 , 這並不需要天然災害才能成功 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	使用舊思維 , 國家基礎設施和管道工作 , 實在太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上執行數字時 , 你就快用完了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這是 「 換個角度思考 」 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水 , 用人造製程序來做 , 讓我們用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從上面撿起水 , 淡化它 , 免費運送到那邊 , 將它丟到山上 , 河流 , 和溪流 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水源 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們所要做的就是讓它變成 「 生病 」 。 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以用lifsaver濾水瓶 。
or we could use one of these .	或者我們可以用其中一種
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的科技 , 在一個jerry罐子裡 ,
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這將會處理兩萬五千公升的水 ; 這對四個家庭來說就夠好了 , 三年 。
and how much does it cost ?	又要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天約半分錢來跑 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 透過不同的思維 , 並且在使用時處理水源 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天走四小時的路 , 來收集他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的源頭取得 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	只要八十億美金 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 目的是要在無法取得安全飲用水的情況下減少人數 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	若要將此情境化 , 英國政府每年花費約一百二十億英鎊在外國援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停下來 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	只要兩百億美金 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	因此 , 每年有三十五億人受苦 , 而每年死亡的兩百萬個孩子 , 將會活下去 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashdown宣稱我們正處在歷史上的一刻 , 權力正在改變 , 以從未有的方式改變 。 在tedxbrussel的一場演講中 , 他指出他所看到的三大全球轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 世界文化
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashdown:全球力量轉移
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩是由一位非常有名的英文詩人寫的 , 在十九世紀末 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	被說在1930年代 , 在邱吉爾的腦中迴音 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是: 「 在夏天的一座山丘上 , 懶惰地流著溪流 , 哈克聽到一支遙遠的鼓手 , 鼓得像夢中的聲音 , 遠處和低處 , 越來越大聲 , 在地球的道路上 , 親愛的朋友和食物給粉末 , 士兵遊行 , 很快就死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩有興趣的人 , 這首詩是 " 一名購物人員 " , 由a.e.豪斯曼寫的 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但豪斯曼所理解的 , 你也在尼爾森的交響曲中聽到的 , 就是十九世紀穩定的長長、炎熱、矽的夏天 , 我們即將邁向一個可怕的歷史時期 , 當權力改變時 , 我們即將邁入歷史的其中一個階段 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些時期 , 各位先生女士 , 伴隨著亂流 , 太常被血液吸引 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我對你們的信息是 , 我相信我們被譴責 , 如果你們願意 , 活在歷史上的一刻 , 當建立權力的基礎開始改變 , 世界的新觀點 , 開始形成 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些是--而且我們今天看得很清楚--幾乎總是高度動亂的時代 , 高度困難的時代 , 而且太常有血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順帶一提 , 每一世紀發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會主張 , 上次它發生的時候 , 而這就是豪斯曼所感受到的 , 以及邱吉爾所感受到的 , 當權力從舊國傳下來時 , 歐洲的舊勢力 , 橫跨大西洋到美國的新興勢力 , 即是美國的初始時代 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在真空中 , 以前 , 太歐洲的權力在上個世紀扮演兩場血腥的大災難 , 第一部分和第二部分:兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經稱他們為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是更準確的形容他們的方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在其中一個時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 今天我想談談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 前兩種 , 重點是權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二種是關於我想要參考的新維度 , 這在現在發生的過程中從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但 , 讓我們來談談發生在全世界的權力轉移 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的狀況是 , 在某種意義上 , 令人害怕的是 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們看到了權力的轉變 , 希臘的力量傳遞給羅馬 , 以及歐洲文明發生的權力轉變 , 但我們看到了稍微不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	對於權力 , 不僅是後來從國家移到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	同時垂直移動
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	今天發生的狀況是 , 被包裝起來的力量 , 被責任歸屬於法律 , 在國家國家的制度中 , 現在遷移到全球的階段 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談到全球化的權力全球化 , 但事實上是真正力量的全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國際舞台上 , 權力被責任歸屬於法律 , 不在國際舞台上 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台 , 現在的權力是:網路的權力 , 衛星廣播者的權力 , 金錢改變者的權力 , 這個巨大的金錢交易所 , 現在它所需的金錢總共有32倍 , 它應該要去資助金改變金 , 如果你喜歡 , 那些金融推測者 , 最近引進我們膝關節的力量 , 跨國企業的力量 , 現在常常常常比中等大的國家還要多 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個很大程度上是不受規範的全球空間 , 不受法律規則的影響 , 人們可能不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在這將是強而有力的時刻
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些擁有最有權力的人在不受限制的空間中運作 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 早期或晚期 , 不受法律規範的空間變得更加正常 , 不只靠你想要的國際貿易、網路等等 。 也有你不想要國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義的東西 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的啟示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些住在太空的人 , 甚至會在你最明亮的九月早晨攻擊你的人 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約有60%被帶到資助911事件資助的400萬美金中 , 實際上通過了雙子星大樓的機構 , 911摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	要知道 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間──大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播 , 來抵擋他們的毒藥 , 也就是要破壞我們的系統和方法 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	更早或更晚 , 歷史的規則是 , 權力必須遵守統治 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	若是如此 , 正如我相信的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是全球化的權力 , 那麼我們這個時代的挑戰之一就是將統治者帶到全球 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信在我們之中 , 數十年前的我們將會有更大、更小的擾動 , 以至於我們能夠達成目標:把統治權帶到全球的空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	現在請注意 , 我不是在說政府
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要設立一些全球民主制度
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順道一提 , 我自己的看法是 , 女士們先生們 , 不太可能透過產出更多的聯合國機構來實行 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種手段 , 可以合法化的國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但 , 談到全球空間的統治時 , 我的猜測是 , 這不會透過更多聯合國機構的創立來實現 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它會發生在強大的團結中 , 並建立以條約為基礎的系統 , 以條約為基礎的協議 , 來統治全球的空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎 , 然而 , 強大到足以維持最強大的美國 , 足以承擔必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都:努力創造一個以條約為基礎的組織的開端 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們現在知道 , 我們必須組成一個機構 , 它能夠將管理帶到金融空間給金融推測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而g20就是這樣一個以條約為基礎的機構
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們會在一分鐘內回到它 , 那就是 , 如果你把最有權力的團結起來 , 以條約為基礎的機構來制定規則 , 來填補那個統治空間 , 那麼接下來會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們等一下會再回到這裡 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個信息是 , 如果你要通過這些亂流 , 或多或少的亂流 , 那麼我們的成功就要在大規模的衡量方式上 , 要仰賴我們的能力 , 才能將合理的治理範圍帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這一切開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和這樣的觀眾對話 , 但權力不只是垂直的轉變 , 也是橫向的轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會主張 , 文明的歷史 , 一直以來 , 文明都聚集在海上 , 和地中海的第一位 , 比較近代 , 在大西洋西部權力的後代 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到的是權力的根本轉變 , 廣泛來說 , 遠離大西洋公共空間的國家聚集在太平洋中 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	從經濟實力開始 , 但這就是開始的方式 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外國政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 發生在世界上其他種植權力的人身上 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這其實不是西方轉變到東方的轉變 ; 不一樣的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 對於這值得的 , 美國將在未來的十年保持地球上最強的國家 , 十五年 , 但她掌握權力的背景現在已經徹底改變了 ; 它徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們從50年來 , 最不尋常的幾年來 , 歷史上我們有著完全獨立的世界 , 每根針都必須由華盛頓的位置來參考 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的案例 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在新興的是更正常的歷史案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多極的世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	直到現在 , 美國一直都是我們世界的主導特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保持最有權力的國家 , 但他們將成為一個越來越多層面的世界中最有權力的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你開始看到中國的替代能源中心 , 當然 , 雖然我自己的猜測是 , 中國的優勢並不是光滑的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	當中國開始在自由化她的經濟之後 , 將她的社會民主化 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是不同的討論的主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	看到印度 , 看到巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 現在世界看起來 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 看起來更像19世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲:一個很棒的英國外交秘書 , 坎寧神 , 曾經形容它是 「 歐洲的權力音樂會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	當時有一個平衡 , 一個五度的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是對平衡打扮 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林結合 , 英國和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來提供平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	現在請注意 , 在一個被獨立世界支配的時期 , 你已經固定了北約 , 華沙制度的聯盟 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的權力對立意味著固定結盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但多種權力的對立意謂著轉變和改變聯盟 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	那就是我們進入的世界 , 我們會越來越能看到我們的聯盟並沒有固定下來 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	坎寧 , 偉大的英國外交秘書長曾說: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會看到越來越多的情況 , 即使我們在西方國家也會伸出手 , 必須伸出手 , 超越大西洋力量的舒適圈 , 才能和他人結盟 , 只要我們想要把事情做好 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	請注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方國家不夠好 , 我們不得不帶其他人進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們得把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方國家試圖自己做這件事的最後一次 , 我們還沒有成功過 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們正到達四百年底的開端 , 我說四百年來 , 因為它是西方權力、西方機構和西方價值觀的終點 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家團結起來 , 它可以在世界上的每個角落提出和解開 。
but that's no longer true .	但這不再是真的 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後的最後一次金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方世界銀行、國際貨幣基金組織結合了布雷頓森林機構、世界銀行、國際貨幣基金組織──問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須打電話給其他人 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為你做個預測 , 這可能更令人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經到了四百年的終點 , 當時西方的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會自己涉及到調停、多邊的調停 , 世界各地都有 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔 , 是嗎 ? 為什麼不 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色的貝雷特底下服務 , 在藍色旗幟下服務 , 今天在聯合國指令下服務 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11個 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	什麼是最大規模的海軍內容處理索馬里海盜議題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是默克爾主義者國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	想要讓海底車道保持開放 ,
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和我們不認同價值觀的人做生意 , 而在於 , 在此刻 , 我們共享共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	用全新的角度來看世界 , 現在正在興起 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天在我們的現代世界 , 由於網際網路 , 由於人們在這裡所談論的各種事物 , 一切都和一切都息息相關 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在是被封鎖的 , 作為國家 , 作為個人 , 以一個從未被實行過的方式 , 從未被實行過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	各國的相互關聯性 , 嗯 , 它總是存在的 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是為了管理國家的相互關聯性 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密切地鎖在一起了 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你得到了墨西哥的豬流感 , 這是24小時後查爾斯戴高爾機場的問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降 , 整個瓦解
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	在俄羅斯的步道上有火災 , 非洲的食物暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都很深、很深、很深的相互連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家獨立行動的想法 , 與他人無關 , 不再與他人合作 , 也不再是可行的提議 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為國家國家的行動與其本身都不相干 , 也不足以控制國家本身的領土 , 因為國家之外的影響現在已經開始影響他們內在的狀況 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國最後一場小型帝國戰爭的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時候 , 我國家的防禦是關於一件事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 以及我們的盟軍有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那時候敵人就在牆外 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人就在牆內 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想談談我的國家的防禦 , 我得要向健康部長說話 , 因為流行病是對我的安全威脅 , 我得要向農業部長說話 , 因為糧食安全是對我的安全造成威脅 , 我得要向產業部長說話 , 因為我們的隱私基礎設施的脆弱 , 現在是對我們的敵人的攻擊點 , 正如我們從網路戰爭中看到的威脅 , 我得要向網路戰爭部長說話 , 因為食物安全是對我國家的威脅 , 因為在我國內發生在我國內的影響 , 因為在我們國家的影響中 , 即將發生在我們的社區中 , 發生在我國內部部部部部部部部部門 , 即將發生在那國家 , 即是有所造成的影響 , 因為在我們的社區內部門 , 即將發生在我們的敵人 , 因為當時 , 即將發生在我國內部部部部部部部部部部部部部部部部門 , 正如同等 , 即將發生在我們的敵人的影響 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是如此 , 一個國家的安全性就只是對它的士兵和它的國防部而言而已 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	是它有能力將其機構集合起來 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直構建 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式縱向階層 , 專門完成任務 , 指令結構完全符合了錯誤的結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在企業裡你知道我們時代的典範結構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	是你有能力在政府內部及外部都很重要的網絡 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	所以 , 這裡是ashdown的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順帶一提 , 不要問我第一個定律和第二定律 , 因為我還沒發明出那些 ; 如果有第三定律 , 聽起來總是比較好 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdown的第三定律是 , 在現代的時代 , 一切都和一切連結在一起 , 最重要的是 , 你能用他人的方式來做些什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構最重要的一點 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍事登記者 , 不論你是生意上的一員 , 你的交互控制者 , 你的能力 , 都可以和他人聯絡 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你了解在工業界 , 政府不會 。
but now one final thing .	但現在是最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣的情況 , 各位先生女士 , 我們現在被鎖在以前從未有過相同的情況下 , 那也是我們彼此共同的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	忽然間 , 這是第一次 , 集體防禦 , 主導我們這個國家的概念 , 已經不再足夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前的情況是 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 我的聯盟 , 像北約 , 比他們的盟國更強大 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是如此 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互關聯的進步和大規模破壞的武器的進步 , 意味著 , 漸漸地 , 我和敵人分享了一個命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我是一位外交官 , 在1970年代與日內瓦的蘇聯協商時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和他們共享了命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平已經來到北愛爾蘭是因為雙方意識到零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們與敵人共享一個命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平的一個大障礙是 , 兩邊都是以色列 , 也是巴勒斯坦人 , 不了解他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 突然間 , 女士們先生們 , 正是遠見主義者和詩人的提議 , 變成我們必須認真看待公共政策的問題 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐恩的偉大詩歌 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 送不給誰鈴鈴 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是一座孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它會說: 「 每個男人的死亡都影響著我 , 因為我參與了人類 , 送出去 , 不要向誰尋求鈴聲 , 它會幫我打 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰唐尼來說 , 這是道德的推薦 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 作為我們生存方程式的一部分 ,
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽生命和健康的途徑 , 丹•伯特納和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區塊 」 , 他們的長輩與vim及vigor同住 , 以記錄年齡 。 在tedxtc , 他分享了9種常見的飲食和生活方式習慣 , 讓他們能在100歲以上過日子 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到一百個+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥雙胞胎研究發現 , 在某些生物限制下 , 一般人平均壽命只有10% , 是由我們的基因所主導的 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十是由我們的生活方式所主導 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍色區塊的前提是:如果我們能找到最佳的生活方式 , 我們可以想出一個以長壽為基礎的方程式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們大概不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘飲食 , 或者說是墨水飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	擁有美國食品食物金字塔
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是 ,
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們 ,
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正能幫助我們活得更久的東西 , 有很多困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	應該吃有機肉還是吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到補給品的時候 , 你應該拿它們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙或復原器呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是否扮演其中的角色 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 那我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	嗯 , 我們找到長壽的方法是和國家地理雜誌聯手 , 和國家老化研究院 , 找出四個人口分佈在地理位置上確認的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 帶一組專家到那裡 , 用方法來檢視這些人的做法 , 來分辨出跨文化的擾動 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後 , 我要告訴各位 , 那個斷層是怎樣的 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我想揭露一些常見的迷思 , 談到長壽時 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你非常努力 , 可以活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國只有5000人中只有1人活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會很低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	儘管它是美國成長最快的人口統計數字 , 但很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們不是為了長壽而設計的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們是為了所謂的 「 繁衍成功 」 程式設計的 。
i love that word .	我很喜歡那個字 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它讓我想起我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 繁衍成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一個世代 , 當你的孩子有孩子時 , 那個年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那次演化的效果完全消失之後 ,
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或人類 , 在兩者之間 , 這是相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要達到100歲 , 你不僅需要有良好的生活方式 , 你還得要贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有些治療方法可以幫助緩慢、反轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞就死了 , 它們就永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太辛苦了 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 毀了你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用斑塊纏起來 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 數兆個有 「 t 」 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年一次轉變一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己轉到那邊時 , 都會受到一些損害 。 而那損害就會形成 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並以指數型態成長 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像我們都有披頭四的專輯或鷹專輯 , 我們會在錄音帶上做複製 , 讓朋友複製那個錄音帶 , 很快地 , 成功的世代代聽起來像垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	嗯 , 同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化的速度比一個125歲的人快125倍
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有你能做的事來減緩老化或阻止老化 , 我在這裡幹什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實是 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約九十年 , 更多給女性 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 沿著線的某處 , 我們在桌子上留下了大約12年的好年份 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年是我們可以得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 他們將多年免於慢性病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些失蹤年齡最好的方法就是去看世界各地的文化 , 真正體驗到它們的文化 , 人們活到比我們活到100歲的年齡 , 比我們多出10倍的地方 , 平均壽命多了十幾年 , 中年的死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸的沙丁尼亞島找到了我們的第一條藍色區域大約125英哩 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 一個叫nuoro省的區域 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡有男性壽命最長的區域 , 百歲人瑞比美國人多出10倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只能達到100歲 , 還能有非凡的活力 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	102歲的老年人仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 雜碎木頭 , 可以打敗比他們年輕六十年的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上可以追溯到關於基督的時期 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是被隔離的青銅時代文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為這片土地是如此的有推斷性 , 它們大多是牧羊人 , 它會發生在一般、低密度的身體活動上 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎 , 以他們能帶到田裡的食物為主 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一塊未發酵的全麥麵包 , 名為 「 drum小麥做成的卡塔樂譜 」 , 一種乳酪是從牧草的動物製作出來的 , 所以乳酪在omega-3脂肪酸中 , 而不是玉米酸的omega-6脂肪酸 , 一種葡萄酒含量比世界上任何一個已知的酒含量高三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會中最可口的元素之一就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有注意到在美國這裡 , 社會平等似乎在大約二十四歲時會達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看一下廣告 ,
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 年紀越大 , 你得到的智慧就越多 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你進到薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 與其看到運動插圖的游泳日曆 , 看到月曆的百歲人瑞 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不僅對你老化的父母有好處 , 讓他們能保持親近的家庭 , 大約四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示 , 這對那些家庭的孩子也有好處 , 他們的死亡率較低 , 疾病的比率較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	也就是所謂的祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一端發現了我們的第二個藍色區域 , 位在東京南方約800英里處 , 位在琉球的智庫拉哥 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主要島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的基地 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是發現最古老的母族群 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	在這個地方 , 人們有世上最長的殘疾預期壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活得很久 , 往往在睡眠中死去 , 很快地 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性行為之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多活七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	五倍於美國的百歲人瑞 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	結腸癌和乳癌的比率是五分之一 , 在美國這裡的大型殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	而心血管疾病的比例只有六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	而這個文化所產生的事實 , 顯示他們有很強的教導我們的東西 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 一個以植物為基礎的飲食 , 滿是蔬菜 , 裡面有許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了大約八倍的豆腐 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們所吃的東西更顯著 , 就是他們如何吃它 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略 , 不停止過量 , 如你所知 , 在美國是大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的幾個策略:它們用較小的盤子來吃 , 所以它們在每個坐著的卡路里都比較少吃 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其服用家庭風格 , 你可以隨心所欲地在說話時隨心所欲地吃東西 , 他們在櫃台服務 , 把食物放走 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有3000歲的年紀 , 我認為這是有史以來最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	由混淆所發明 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	而那種飲食就是所謂的 「 哈拉 」 、 「 哈特奇 」 、 「 野餐 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在吃飯前說 , 提醒他們 , 當他們的肚子滿到80%時 , 停止吃東西 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	感覺從你的肚子傳到你的大腦大概需要一個半小時 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住要停止80% , 它會幫助你不去做那件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有幾個社會建構 , 我們可以將長壽聯想起來 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道隔離會致命 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經降到1.5歲了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運出生在琉球 , 你出生的系統就會自動有五十個朋友 , 和你在人生中旅行 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai 。 如果你在一個你預期會共享彈跳的人 , 如果你碰到運氣 , 如果事情惡化了 , 孩子生病了 , 父母死了 , 你總是會有你背後的人 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個特別的moai , 這五位女士已經在一起97年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人的生命分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	這是我們的工作生活 , 生產力的地方 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著退休到簡單的椅子上 , 或下到亞利桑那州去打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan語中 , 甚至沒有退休這個詞 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 一生中有一個詞是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	而且 , 大約是翻譯 , 意思是 「 早上醒來的理由 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位102歲的karate大師而言 , 他的ikigai正在攜帶著這場火星藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位百歲的漁夫來說 , 持續捕捉他的家人每週三次的魚 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究院實際上給了我們一個問卷 , 給這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們非常文化上的直覺 , 那些放了問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上醒來 ,
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位102歲的老婦人而言 , 她的ikigai簡直是她的曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲半前分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 抱著曾曾曾孫女的感覺是什麼樣的 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺就像跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我以為那是個很棒的思想 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理雜誌的編輯希望我找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們看著明尼蘇達的草原 , 那裡有非常高比例的百歲人瑞 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向了數據 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的族群 , 七天的冒犯者集中在加州羅馬林達市 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	傳統主義者是保守主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五日出日落時慶祝他們的休假 , 星期六到日落 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	一個 " 24小時的庇護所 " , 他們稱之為
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 傳達給他們非比尋常的長壽 , 相較於說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位冒犯者來說 , 他們的預期壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差異更大 , 男性中有更多的發音 , 他們預期的壽命會比他們的美國人多11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這是一個跟著約七萬人的研究 , 已經有三十年了 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 而且我認為它最高度地說明了這個藍色區域計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異性戀的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 他們一輩子都遵循儀式的習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	直接從聖經中取用他們的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	gensis:第一章 , 第三章 , 第三章 , 上帝談到法律和種子 , 再來是關於綠色植物的斯坦札特 , 很可能遺漏的是肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們認真看待這個聖所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週有24小時 , 不論他們有多忙 , 他們在工作上有多壓力 , 孩子們需要開車 , 他們停止一切 , 專注在他們的神 , 他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 在宗教裡 , 堅強地走著大自然 。
