and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這其中的力量並不是偶爾完成的 , 電力是每週都在完成一生的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	都不難 , 不需要花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒犯者也傾向與其他的冒犯者一起出去 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個基督徒的派對 , 你不會看到有人在瑞典的吉姆樑柱或滾動關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	取而代之的是他們在談論下一次的大自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以深刻且可測量的方式互相影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化產生了埃爾斯•沃爾斯•哈雷罕 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellswhareham已經97歲了
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是個數百萬富翁 , 但當一位承包商想要六千美元來建造隱私柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了那種錢 , 我會自己做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以在接下來的三天 , 他出了水泥 , 四處拖著竿子 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預料地 , 也許在他最後手術室的第四天 ,
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是桌子上的那個人 ; 做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他每個月要做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•拉福斯 , 現在103歲 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 早上開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡放置板子 , 丟出屋頂尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在這裡的雙胞胎城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天從抬起重量開始 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她進到她的根部 , 上了1994年的卡迪拉克賽維爾 , 在聖伯納迪諾高速公路上 , 在那裡 , 她仍然為七個不同的組織當志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經在十九次硬體探險中
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是你遇到的唯一一個人 , 騎著他的腳踏車穿過撒哈拉沙漠 , 沒有防曬霜 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何冒險比騎馬爾•德頓騎車更嚴厲 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒見過面的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中 , 共通點是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都做的事是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功把它歸納為九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自此之後 , 我們再做兩個藍色區域探險 , 這些常見的決議者是真的 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一 , 我即將要說出一個瘋子 , 沒有一個會運動 , 至少我們會想到運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之 , 他們設立了自己的生命 , 使他們不斷地被推向身體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球婦女正從地面上起落 , 她們每天坐在地板上 , 每天30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每趟旅行到商店 , 或去教堂 , 或去朋友家裡偶爾會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有按鈕可以推廣去做院子工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們就用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	跑步機燃燒的熱量和跑步機一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們確實進行有意的身體活動時 , 這是他們所享受的東西 。 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一證實的方式就是脫離認知的衰退 , 他們都傾向於有一個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式來建立自己的人生 , 所以他們有正確的外觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間轉移 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的冒犯者祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有這種祖先的調查 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在急促或感到壓力時 , 會觸發一種叫 「 發炎反應 」 的東西 , 它會和從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病的一切有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天慢下來十五分鐘 , 你將那個炎熱的狀態轉變為更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有用字彙來感知目的、ikigai , 就像okinawans一樣 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 以及你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的感他們活躍於生活中那值得七年的預期壽命
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝一點點 , 而不是賣給美國人口的難度 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	牠們傾向於以植物為基礎的飲食
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	而且他們有策略可以持續不受過度濫用 , 那些在對的時間將他們推離桌子的小東西 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接著 , 所有這一切的基礎是他們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們先把家人放第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和老父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向於屬於一個信仰型的社群 , 平均每月四到十四年的預期壽命是值得的 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最大的是他們也屬於合適的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們要麼出生 , 要麼就很積極地把自己和對的人圍在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗明罕研究中得知 , 如果你三個最要好的朋友都過胖 , 有50%的機率會過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人一起出去 , 那會隨著時間產生可衡量的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你朋友對休閒的想法是身體活動 , 保齡球 , 或玩曲棍球 , 腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點 , 但不太多 , 他們吃得對 , 他們也很投入 , 他們信任和值得信任 , 這會隨著時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食沒有用 。 在世界歷史上 , 沒有任何飲食能為超過百分之二的人口工作 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常是從一月開始的 ; 通常是十月才會完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到長壽的時候 , 藥丸或其他東西都沒有短期藥方 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做的最重要的事 , 來為你的生活加上更多年 , 及生活在你的生活中 。 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水指揮了電力 ; 一扇窗子 , 從清晰轉換到不透光 , 轉換開關 ; 製造音樂的水母 。 所有這些東西都存在 。 卡塔琳娜•莫塔塔說:該是玩它的時候了 。 莫塔帶領我們踏上驚喜和酷酷炫的新材料 , 並建議我們找出它們有益處的方式 , 就是去實驗 , 去玩笑 。
creativity , design , technology	創意、設計、科技、
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩智慧材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機建造了一輛車 , 讓他能運送家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他負擔不起汽車 , 也因為他知道如何建造一輛車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有一段時間 , 我們了解事情是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 , 這樣我們才能建立、修復 , 或在最不知情的決定下 , 決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這些自閉症的做法 , 在二十世紀的後半就迷失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 自造者社群和開放資源的模式正在將這種知識帶入我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層級 , 到組成的部分 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的時候 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是由什麼組成的 , 以及它們是如何產生的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有這些令人驚奇、自發的複合體 , 會改變形狀 , 會導電的顏料 , 會改變顏色 , 會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電墨水可以讓我們繪製電路 , 而不是用傳統印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在這個我拿著的小例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感應器 , 藉由打開這小小的光線來對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家的導電墨水已經被使用了 , 但近期的發展指出 , 我們很快就能在雷射印表機和筆中使用 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張照片是用無色的光傳導粒子注射的 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然普通的丙烯醇只會在邊緣散射光線 , 但這一顆在我打開燈時會照亮整個表面 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這材料的兩個已知應用程式包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而熱色素會在特定溫度下改變顏色
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我會把這個放在一個熱板上 , 設定在一個溫度上 , 只會稍微高於環境 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的其中一個原則是 , 在其他東西當中 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它指出 , 當內容夠酷到可以喝的時候 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	所以這些只是一些普遍被稱為智慧材料的東西 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	在幾年內 , 它們會在許多我們日常使用的物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行車--科幻小說中承諾的我們 , 但是我們可以有一些牆 , 會根據溫度而改變顏色 , 鍵盤會捲起來 , 窗戶會在開關上發出不透明的聲音 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是社會科學家 , 為什麼我今天要來這裡談智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 , 也因為我相信我們應該對構成我們世界的元件有更深入的了解 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技組合的未來還不夠了解 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料在小量中很難取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	對於如何使用它們 , 幾乎沒有任何資訊可用 , 很少有人說它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 他們主要存在於這個貿易秘密和專利的領域中 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	所以 , 大約三年前 , kirsty男孩和我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為開放材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是一個我們網站 , 任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人在任何時候都可以貢獻 , 並且集合資源 , 例如研究論文和教導其他自造者 , 像我們自己一樣的製造者 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個大型、集體的資料庫 , 由智慧型材料提供的資訊 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要在乎智慧型材料如何運作 , 以及它們是由什麼組成的呢 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的事物 , 而我們不了解的事物 , 最後使用的卻是塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康 , 以及生活品質有著深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要活在一個由智慧材料組成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	其次 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是被修補 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 一直是發明家和改善者 , 從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但這並不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	兩位伊利諾大學的科學家在伊利諾州大學發表了一篇論文 , 用比較簡單的方法製造導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	約旦bunker , 他以前完全沒有化學經驗 , 直到那時 , 讀這篇論文 , 並在他的自造者空間中進行實驗 , 只用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用了烤麵包機 , 甚至做出了他自己的vorex混合器 , 基於另一位科學家/製造商的課程 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬丹接著在網路上發表了他的成果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過且沒用的東西 , 所以其他人可以研究並繁殖它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 喬丹主要的創新形式是 , 在一所大學裡 , 用便宜的材料和工具做實驗 , 在芝加哥的車庫中重現 , 只用他自己做的便宜材料和工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這項工作 , 其他人可以在他離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子 , 我想提一下她的專案計畫的目標是要強調材料的表現品質 , 同時把焦點放在建造者的創意和技能上 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備在教導我們事情是如何運作的 , 但他們設計的限制影響了我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以 , 漢娜的手法 , 另一方面 , 是要推動一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 讓我們免於預先設定的限制 , 做法是教導我們材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以 , 在漢娜許多令人印象深刻的實驗當中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面有一些銅製膠帶在上面連接mp3播放器和磁鐵
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以根據麻省理工的marcelocoelho的研究漢娜創建了一系列的紙喇叭從簡單的銅膠帶到導電布料
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造者一樣 , 漢娜出版了她的食譜 , 讓任何人都能複製和繁殖 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子產品是最有前景的材料科學的分支之一 , 讓我們能創造出更便宜且有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的手工藝作品 , 和她分享她的發現的事實 , 將門打開給一系列新的可能性 , 這兩種都具有美學上的吸引力和創新性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的地方在於 , 我們用熱情和好奇心創造出來 , 我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從不規則的角度來處理問題 , 在過程中 , 最後發現了替代方案 , 甚至是更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 用材料做實驗的人越多 , 研究者就願意分享他們的研究 , 製造商他們的知識 , 我們就有更好的機會 , 創造出能真正服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我覺得有點像tednelson , 在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型主體 , 只有科學家在乎 , 甚至沒有人在家裡夢想過 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡 , 說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得關於新興技術的先入為主的知識是最好的辦法 , 確保我們在未來能有所說的話 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 把門鎖起來 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛來引導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前面的幾個車子和後面的那幾個車子 。 但如果車子能互相分享它們的位置和速度 , 用預測模型來計算路上每個人最安全的路線 ? 珍妮佛.喜利耶 , 想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛.喜利:如果汽車可以說話 , 意外可能是可以避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	咱們面對現實吧:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去思考的一件事 , 但宗教象徵和好運的魅力 , 出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們所知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是造成16至19歲人死亡的主要原因 , 在美國 , 導致死亡 , 其中百分之七十五的意外與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	當時我是年輕的司機出門在高速公路上 , 車子在我面前 , 我看到煞車燈熄滅 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停下來 , 停下來 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	剛好是65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我滑到煞車上 ,
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺到abs會踢進去 , 車子還會去 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空中袋子部署 , 車子已經完整了 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車子在停下來 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以藉由讓我們的車子彼此交談來轉變開車的體驗 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只希望各位稍微想想開車的體驗是怎樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車裡 。 關上門 。 你在一個玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	無法直接感知你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它導入部分地點的道路 , 在其他的金屬巨人之間 , 在超人的速度之中 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 而且你只需要指導你是你的兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所擁有的 , 眼睛不是真的為了這個任務而設計的 , 但接著 , 人們要求你做的事情像是 , 你想做一個車道改變 , 他們首先問你做的事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上拿下來 。 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再去看你要往哪裡去 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 並且在路上開車 , 不去看你要往哪裡去 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是駕駛的安全方法 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須 , 我們必須做一個選擇 , 我看這裡還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做很棒的工作挑選 , 選擇我們在路上參加的 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過什麼 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感受到錯誤或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒有看到它來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這一點 。 我相信這一點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但科技現在已經存在 , 可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了汽車互相交換資料 , 我們將能看到不只是前面三輛車 , 後面有三輛車 , 右邊和左邊 , 都是鳥的眼睛觀看 , 我們真的能看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看那傢伙要走得多快或停下來 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙下降到零 , 我會知道 ,
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們將能夠看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你如何能預測未來 ? 那真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 沒有 。 有了汽車 , 根本不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是立體的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們沿著道路往下走 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在預先出版的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要做出合理的預測 , 在不久的將來 , 汽車會在哪裡並不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在你的車裡 , 有些摩托車騎士來了 ! 每小時85英里 , 車道滑落 , 我知道你有過這個經驗 , 那傢伙沒有 「 剛出去 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙在路上大概已經走了半個小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英里後 , 有人看到了那傢伙 , 只要一輛車看到那傢伙 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他就在地圖位置 , 速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英里的速度持續下去 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你們會知道 , 因為你們的車會知道 , 因為其他車會在他耳邊低語 , 像是: 「 順便說一下 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 注意看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	可以合理的預測汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓物品 。
that's very nice about them .	對他們來說 , 那是很棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何達到目的 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的東西開始 , 就像分享我們車子間的位置資料一樣簡單 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我車子裡有gps和攝影機 , 我有一個很精確的概念 , 可以說明我在哪裡 , 以及我要走多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 有點像 , 還有它們要往哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車子也是一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道自己所在的位置 , 有點像是對其他車子的模糊概念 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛汽車共享那些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以準確的告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 當毛茸茸的估算結合時 , 甚至在輕型交通中 , 當車子只分享gps數據時 , 我們把這個研究從電腦模擬中移出 , 轉到機器人測試床 , 現在在這些機器人上有實際的感應器:stereo攝影機、gps , 和2d雷射鏡頭等級的發現者 , 都是在後備系統中常見的 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還會附著一個短距的溝通收音機 , 機器人彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人互相接觸時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 並且能互相避免 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你弄太多聊天時 , 要處理所有的包裝很難 , 所以你必須優先順序 , 那就是預測模型能協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子都在追蹤預測的軌跡 , 你不會對那些包包裝太多注意 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你優先考慮一個人 , 看來有點離譜 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	而且可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他是怎麼走的 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而你知道你需要警告哪些駕駛才能走出路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼樣才能警告每個人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼能低語說: 「 你需要出路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:一、車的能力 , 以及駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有個傢伙有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 你知道 , 做點什麼 , 他們可能不在緊急狀況的最佳位置 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一系列研究 , 進行駕駛狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用一系列三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測 , 如果一個駕駛者在向前看 , 向下看 , 在電話上 , 或者喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測事故 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪個車子 , 在最佳的位置上 , 可以移動到最好的位置 , 為每個人計算最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	從根本上來說 , 這些技術存在於現今 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願去分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個令人不安的概念 , 這個想法 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 談到我們和其他車子 , 我們會在八卦的大海上下道路 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用一種保護我們的隱私的方式來實現 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我真的不知道你怎麼想 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看一下你的車牌牌號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而我認為這會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位考慮一下 , 如果你真的不希望背後的青少年感到分心 , 知道你在煞車 , 你要來一個死者站 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由我們願意分享我們的資料 , 我們可以為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的汽車八卦有關你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	會讓道路更安全許多 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人peterdiamandis談到他如何幫助stephenhawking實現他的夢想藉由一起飛入上層大氣層並體驗到0g的無重力
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短的演講、太空、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得.戴曼迪斯是史蒂芬.霍金在零g-gro的霍金
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	在座認識我的人都知道我有多熱衷於打開太空前線 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界重力專家們體驗無重力的體驗時 , 真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次透過archonxprize來認識他 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們拿著的一個競賽 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一個團隊在10天內完成100個人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的 「 基因組一百個個個體 」 ──我們將其定序為其中的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特那次事件的主席 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇見了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是去太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裏 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力進入零 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 唯一能體驗0g的方法 , 其實是用降落傘飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	搭飛機 , 飛過頂端 , 體重不重25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 重達兩倍之多 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再 , 再而三地
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到八、十分鐘的無重力 , nasa如何訓練他們的太空人這麼久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始這樣做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣布要飛史蒂芬.霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一個政府機關 , 一個公司飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這麼做 , 你要殺那個傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	而他想去
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 ,
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了一次媒體大會 , 我們宣佈我們的目的是要做一個零邊拋物線 , 給他25秒的零點 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切順利的話 , 我們可能會做三個拋物面鏡 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼他要去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	而他所說的 , 對我來說 , 是非常動人的 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命在不斷增加的風險 , 可能因為災難而被消滅......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 人類的種族沒有未來 , 如果它沒有進入太空 ,
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此 , 我想要鼓勵公共利益在太空中 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在太空總署的內部 , 進入零號飛機的後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐款我們募集了15萬美元捐款給和我們一起飛的兒童慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個ted成員 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了一整個er 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生和兩位護士登上飛機 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監視他血液的po2 , 他的心跳 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	天知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施起飛 , 太空梭在那裡起飛 , 降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我的夥伴ronlichtenberg和我小心地把他暫停為零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力的真正樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在那第一個拋物面鏡之後 , 你知道的 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 我們說去 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們其實在牛頓爵士面上漂浮了一顆蘋果 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋有同樣的椅子 , 艾薩克•牛頓也做到了 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 第五個和第六個 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	和第七個和第八個
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	而這位男子看起來不像個65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們正生活在珍貴的珠寶上 , 正是在我們這星球上移動的有生之年 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入這場史詩般的探險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫師davidbolinsky所呈現的驚人動畫 , 顯示一個細胞內的忙碌生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化、
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插畫家 , 我來自一個稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在看 , 自從我長大以來 , 藝術、真理和美麗的表達 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩者都是很棒的 , 兩者都有很棒的東西 , 能讓它們成為真相和美麗的理想 , 能被科學和數學研究的理想 , 幾乎就像是科學家想要約會的理想雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真相是令人敬畏的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是有力的理想 , 不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 。 它們有時是有用的 , 常常是長久以來 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	現在你可以把一些圖片捲起來 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美是那些往往不在科學界的人所不透明的事物 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用一種形容美的方式來描述美的事物 , 通常只有在你了解語言和語義 , 才能夠取得的事物 , 才會在研究主題時 , 表達出真與美的事物 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看一下數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看一下宇宙常數 , 那裡有一個人類的理想 , 你看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數字進化--這些是非常難理解的事物 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導為醫學插圖師以來 , 我試著做的是 , 我父親是雕塑家和視覺導師 , 我想找出一種方法 , 來幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美 , 透過動畫、透過圖片、訴說故事 , 以致人們不見得是明顯的 , 可以被教導 , 可以被教導 , 並且可以被了解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常會沉浸在一個環境中 , 在那裡 , 他們所學到的主題是 , 有真相和美的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式是互相比較的 , 它會被吸引到一個不見得是事實和美麗的地方 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	這就像是雞湯的老食譜 , 在那裡煮雞肉 , 直到味道不見了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我有一支來自哈佛大學羅伯特•路德的電話 , 在分子和細胞生物學系 , 幾年前 。 他問我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意真正改變哈佛的醫療和科學教育方式 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	因此 , 我們開始進行一個計畫 , 探究細胞在分子和細胞生物學中的真與美 , 以便讓學生能夠了解更大的圖片 , 讓他們可以把這些事實掛起來 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能有一個關於細胞的心智圖像 , 是一個大型、非常複雜的城市 , 被微機械佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 正是世界各地奈米科技人士的羨慕 , 會自我導向、強大、精確、精確的裝置 , 是由胺基酸弦所製成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械能驅動細胞如何移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能驅動一個細胞如何複製 。 它們能支撐我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們能供給我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的是 , 找出我們如何將這個故事變成一個動畫 , 它會是哈佛生物視覺的中心角色 , 它是哈佛大學的一個網站 , 它是為了它的分子和細胞生物學的學生 , 它除了所有的文字資訊 , 除了把所有的知識放在一起 , 以外 , 讓這些學生對於它的真相和美有了內化的看法 , 並且能夠研究這個觀點 , 讓他們的想像力 , 如此一來 , 他們的腦海裡才會被激發出來 , 並將這些視覺化 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 就是 , 你有巨噬細胞在微血管上流下 , 它們在觸碰微血管壁表面 , 它們從微血管壁上的細胞取得資訊 , 它們得到了這些資訊 , 外面有發炎的地方 , 看不見和感覺不到的地方 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到導致它們停止的資訊 , 導致它們內化 , 認為它們需要製造出所有會造成它們改變形狀的各個部分 , 並試著脫離這個微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以 , 這些分子馬達我們必須和哈佛科學家和資料庫模型合作 , 在原子上準確的分子模型 , 找出它們是如何移動的 , 找出它們是如何移動的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想辦法用真理的方式來實現這件事 , 讓細胞中的同步群眾無法預防視野發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是三分鐘內讀者的消化版本 , 我們製作的這部電影的第一個面向 。 這是一個持續的項目 , 將會持續四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請大家看看這個 , 看看細胞製造這些小步行機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為 「 卡因 」 , 將這些巨大的負荷量 , 以相對的尺寸挑戰一隻螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	去執行電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能支撐細胞內部的機器真的很了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	將資訊傳遞給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成細胞內不同的事情發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造果蠅所需的部件 , 從細胞核的資訊中 , 由閱讀基因的分子所產生 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每一個人 , 若沒有這些小小的微機械 , 就有可能實現 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯 , 真的很激動人心 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做kin , 他拉著一個滿是全新的製造蛋白質的袋子 , 到細胞中所需的位置 , 不論是到細胞膜 , 不管是用來做器官 , 不管是用來建造東西或是修復某樣東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人都有大約十萬個這種東西跑來跑去 , 現在 , 在你的每一百兆個細胞裡面 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你並不是在本質上什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 我希望你們回家時 , 想想看我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	再想想一些我們正在學習關於細胞力學的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們想通了這一切 , 相信我 , 我們就知道幾乎百分之一的狀況 , 一旦我們想通了到底發生了什麼事 , 我們就真的能夠對我們的健康有很大的控制權 , 和我們未來世代所做的事 , 以及我們將活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這個來發現更多的真相 , 和更多的美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 真的是非常了不起 , 已經意識到它們所需的細胞 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	他們一起工作 , 讓細胞做該做的事
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起合作 , 協助我們的身體──巨大的實體──他們永遠無法妥善看到功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受其餘的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓計劃在她的旅行車裡住了一年 , 看看這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症設定進去時 , 她的露營旅程變成了無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她成為美國無家可歸者的經驗 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、社會、說故事、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:那一年我是無家可歸者 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是個瘋狂的好奇人 , 所以身為記者的22年裡 , 我學會了如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的一件事就是變成隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為工作無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭職擔任報社編輯的工作 , 在我父親在同年二月去世後 , 決定要去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死神撞上了我相當困難 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我做這件事時 , 有很多事我想要去感受和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一輩子都在露營 。 我決定住在一輛旅行車裡待了一年 , 這樣做會像是一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包了我的貓 , 我的轉子威爾和我的露營裝備 , 進入1975年雪佛蘭的休旅車 , 開進日落 , 完全沒能意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	一:那個社會等於生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至是一個購物 , 身為一個人 , 擁有價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到他人的負面感知有多快就能影響我們的現實 , 只要我們讓它發生 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我無法意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在廂型車裡很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 定期吃飯 ,
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	而我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但 , 接著 , 關於我父親死後的憤怒和沮喪就出現了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 而我必須得到全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	剛剛溫和的春天 , 變成了一個令人難以置信的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	到處都無法停車 , 不用很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 經過一扇在廂型車上的開窗 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗走進了狗的日子照護 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	不論何時 , 我都會在辦公大樓裡用員工洗澡 , 以及卡車停下來 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或者 , 我在公共場所清洗 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間車廂的溫度很少降到華氏80度以下讓難以入眠
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱氣中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰在我的冰胸裡融化了幾個小時 , 相當悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起找公寓 , 或負擔不起的公寓 , 可以讓我擁有轉輪和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在旅行車裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱氣使我無法走過五十英呎的大眾廁所 , 晚上我用一個桶子和一個垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天天氣落下 , 溫度降低在冷凍狀態下 。 然後他們就停留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	而我面臨了一整套全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上停車位不同的地方 , 所以我會避免被警察察察察覺 , 並且被警察抓走 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得自己無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道它是何時或如何發生的 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 轉變成一個無家可歸的女性 , 住在旅行車裡 , 帶著我的呼吸 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒變 。 我的智商沒降到 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華 , 我的完整性 , 我的價值觀 , 關於我的一切 , 都保持著同樣的觀念 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我旋轉得越來越深 , 陷入憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我去了 。 我在三天內就沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的任何人一樣有氣味和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我就是沒喝醉酒或很高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當有幾個無家可歸的男人意識到 , 包括一個前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的 。 你為什麼真正在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人沒有把我視為無家可歸的人 , 但我真的做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的一種藥物的反應──憂鬱症讓我離開了我自殺 。 我記得我在想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友告訴我 , 在那之後沒多久 , 她聽說提姆•羅夏特 , 一個全國知名的記者 , 一直在談論我在國立電視台 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫過一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他去世前的那一年 , 在提姆的新書上 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他正在做演說節目迴路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到提姆•羅塞特 , 《見媒體》的前主持人 , 在談論我的寫作 , 在我住在沃爾瑪的停車場 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為那時候我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我進了書店 。 我找到提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重播我的論文 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後沒多久 , 我搬回了田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在旅行車裡 , 和沙發上衝浪 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	到隔年的夏天 , 我是一位工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得了獎項 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	成千上萬的人全職工作兼職 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化和犯罪化生活在你的車輛或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸、無家可歸的工作 , 主要還是隱形的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你曾經遇過一個 , 讓他們參與 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何事情 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來做無家可歸者的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵各位 , 把錢交給下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在哪裡、睡哪裡 , 或任何時候他們的人生狀況 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在一輛廂型車裡 , 住在沃爾瑪的停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 永遠找到一種方式 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 中 , chaiviravaidya , 走過我們國家的大膽計劃 , 以提高其生活水準 , 從七零年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著許多法蘭克、好笑且非常有效的談到保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	梅契•維拉迪亞: 「 保險套先生如何讓泰國變得更美好 。 」
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有許多貧窮的人住在貧窮中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 或貧窮減少計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭規劃計畫開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕產婦健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存 , 沒有人會接受家庭計劃 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步是:去找孩子 , 去找母親 , 然後跟著做家庭計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是孩童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回顧一下為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有7個孩子 , 成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女人說: 「 我們同意 。 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 我們有非常非常少數的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有得到答案 , 我們沒有被當成一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找護士 , 同時也是婦女 , 做了一份很棒的工作 , 解釋如何使用藥丸 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那實在是太棒了 , 但它只涵蓋了全國的20% 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們該怎麼做才能讓80%的人獨自說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去找你看到的普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那黃色的標誌下面我希望他們沒有把這些都擦掉 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂還大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的人是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們自己練習家庭計劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地提供藥丸和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們就在那裡 。 我們去找被視為問題的成因 , 來當解決方案 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論有哪些人 , 和婦女一起看船 , 在這裡賣浮動市場賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 也有避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國哪裡 , 都會找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 何不來宗教因為在菲律賓 , 天主教教會相當強烈 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那裏是藍色的 , 不是黃色的 , 拿著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶在藥丸和保險套上灑上聖水 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	而這張照片被送到全國各地 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以村裡的一些僧侶自己也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	已經被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的認知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每一個人都參與 , 試著提供任何能讓人類更美好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師們 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過四分之一的家庭計劃有關於家庭計劃有新的字母a、b、b、c、保險套、iud、v等字母 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有了一條蛇和梯子遊戲 , 在那裡你丟了骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你在任何事上都很有規劃性地降落 , 你就往前邁進 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	像是: 「 媽媽每天晚上吃藥 ,
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 走到前面 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買了一套保險套 。 非常好 , 叔叔 。 繼續前進 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉了 , 不用保險套 。 回來 , 又重新開始 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣的 , 教育 , 階級娛樂 ,
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校裡做 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套有重組比賽 , 我們有孩子的保險套冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久前 , 保險套就被稱為女孩最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會讓它變成這樣 , 保險套就是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年引進了我們第一個微型貸款計畫 , 組織它的女性說: 「 我們只想借錢給實行家庭計劃的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧自己的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上取出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是由他們來的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年後 , 還在持續下去 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 但它是基金的微型貸款 。

and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能看不到泰國男子 , 總是女人、女人、女人 。

so just don't leave it to the specialists and doctors and nurses .	所以 , 不要讓它留給專家、醫生和護士 。
we all need to help .	我們都需要幫助 。
and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要協助大家脫離貧窮 , 現在 , 我們得到了愛滋病 , 有點像是這次 , 不是單單和政府合作 , 而是和商業界合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為貧窮的人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 取得信貸 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些是由商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳企業家 , 小型商人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法就是透過企業企業
so , that was done .	所以 , 這件事完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	錢從公司到村莊 , 通過樹木培育 。
it's not a free gift .	而不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 錢進到他們的小額貸款基金 , 我們稱之為村落發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都會加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進去 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	而在你可以借錢之前 , 你需要受過訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	而我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮中的人 , 信用度一定是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用必須是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠無法脫離貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	然後在拿到貸款之前 , 你一定要接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	這裡我們稱之為 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣一來 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就成功了 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這些是一些生意:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、樹、水果 , 這是非常有趣的nike冰淇淋和nike餅乾 ; 這是一個由nike贊助的村莊 。
they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止製作鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	把這些做得更好 , 因為我們負擔得起 。 」
and then we have silk , thai silk .	然後我們有絲 , 泰國絲 ,
now we're making scottish tartans , as you can see on the left , to sell to all people of scottish ancestors .	現在我們在做蘇格蘭的塔坦人 , 如你在左邊可以看到的 , 賣給所有蘇格蘭祖先的人 。
so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以任何人坐著看電視 , 都跟我聯絡 。
and then this is our answer to starbucks in thailand " coffee and condoms . "	接著 , 這是我們在泰國的星巴克的答案 「 咖啡和保險套 」 。
see , starbucks you awake , we keep you awake and alive .	看 , 星巴克你醒來 , 我們讓你保持清醒和活著 。
can you imagine , at every starbucks that you can also get condoms ?	你能想像 , 在每一個星巴克 , 你還能拿到保險套嗎 ?
you can order your condoms with your with your cappuccino .	您可以用您的卡普奇諾命令您的保險套
and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	現在 , 終於在教育界 , 我們想要改變學校 , 把學校用在一個地方 , 在那裡 , 它是每個人終身學習中心的地方 。
we call this our schoolbased integrated rural development .	我們稱之為以學校為基礎的鄉村發展 。
and it's a center , a focal point for economic and social development .	而它是經濟和社會發展的焦點 。
redo the school , make it serve the community needs .	改善學校 , 讓社區的需求
and here is a bamboo building all of them are bamboo .	這是一棟竹子建築 , 全部都是竹子 。
this is a geodesic dome made of bamboo .	這是用竹子做成的地質圓頂 。
and i'm sure buckminster fuller would be very , very proud to see a bamboo geodesic dome .	我相信巴克敏斯特•富勒會非常驕傲地看到一個竹子的地質圓頂 。
and we use vegetables around the school ground , so they raise their own vegetables .	而我們在學校附近使用蔬菜 , 所以他們提高他們自己的蔬菜 。
and then , finally , i firmly believe , if we want the mdgs to work the millennium development goals we need to add family planning to it .	然後 , 最後 , 我堅信 , 如果我們希望mdgs能在千禧年發展目標上實現 , 我們需要將家庭計畫加入 。
of course , child mortality first and then family planning everyone needs family planning service it's underutilized .	當然 , 兒童死亡率先 , 接著是家庭規劃 , 每個人需要家庭規劃服務──它被削弱了 。

and we also ask the next olympics to be involved in saving lives .	我們也要求下一屆的奧運能夠參與拯救生命 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能感覺像是朋友 , 但真正的朋友會在一陣子內給你微笑 。 在ted2013年 , kellerrinaudomomomos , 智慧手機驅動的迷你機器人 , 他可以在步行時和你一起運動 , 滑過桌子上的一杯咖啡 , 用可程序的表情來對你做出反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個由你的手機供電的迷你機器人 。

that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在romotive想解決的問題我和其他二十個在romotive的怪胎都執著於解決問題
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要建造一個任何人都可以用的機器人 , 不論你是八、八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個很困難的問題 , 因為你得要建造一個很小、很可攜式的機器人 , 它不只能負擔得起 , 它還得要是大家真的想要帶回家 , 圍繞他們的孩子 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能是令人毛骨悚然或不可思議的 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個機器人 , 它用你已經知道且喜愛你的iphone當作他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone的處理器的力量 , 我們可以創造出一個機器人 , 無線網路讓電腦視覺化 , 可供150美元使用 , 這大約是過去這類機器人的成本的百分之一 。

so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他其實是在用儀器上的錄影機來跟著我的臉 。

he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很疑惑 , 所以他會一直盯著我看 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來到這裡 , 他會轉身跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來到這裡 , 他很聰明 。

that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 送一封電子郵件給祖母 , 住在國家的另一邊 。
