but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想用我們未來正在努力的事情來做結尾 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們其中一位工程師 , dom , 在一個週末打造出來的東西 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	建在google開放架構的頂端 , 叫做 「 街區 」 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這讓你可以拖曳 , 丟下這些數碼的積木 , 為你想要的這個機器人創造任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何為romo設計一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你實際上可以在瀏覽器中模擬這種行為 , 這是你在左邊看到romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行 , 在現實生活中執行程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有讓你驕傲的事情 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些無線網路的機器人 , 實際上都能彼此學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以如此專注於建造機器人 , 讓每個人都能訓練 , 是因為我們認為 , 在個人機器人方面 , 最引人入勝的使用案例是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人變為人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以我們認為 , 如果你家裡有機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己的想像力的表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人學的未來會是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我完全不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是十年或一百億美金 , 或一個大型的人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將仰賴小型、敏捷的機器人 , 如romo , 以及像你自己一樣的人的創意 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及要讓你們全部的機器人 , 我們等不及要看你建造什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和行動主義者伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 在這場演講中充滿熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女人、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝•阿言德講述著熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你 。 非常可怕 , 能來到最聰明的人當中 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴各位幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有位猶太人說我很愛 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真相更真實 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是說故事的人 。 我想傳達一件比我們共同的人性更真實的事 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都對我感興趣 , 有些則困擾我 , 直到我最後寫完它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們身邊的謎團 , 所以我寫關於巧合、事前、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔術 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年中 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我已經匿名 , 直到2006年二月 , 我在義大利的冬天奧運帶著奧運旗幟 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為名人 。 現在人們在macy's中認出我 , 我的孫子們認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我來告訴你們我的四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧運會典禮的組織者之一 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為旗幟大師之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回覆說 , 這肯定是錯誤的身分認同 , 因為我是你能從運動員那裡得到的 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	其實 , 我甚至不確定我可以在體育館四處走動 , 不用走廊 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是什麼笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性 , 代表五大洲 , 以及三位奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一套制服 , 她說 , 並要求我的衡量標準 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對我自己有遠見 , 看來就像米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我發現自己在土耳其 , 在那裡 , 熱情的群眾在八十個奧運隊伍中的任何一個人都在街上歡呼 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了所有在遊戲中競爭的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得獲勝 , 但有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一支雪花 , 一吋的冰 , 風力的力量 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的比訓練或運氣更重要 , 就是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	重點是熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	杜林的街道被紅色海報覆蓋 , 宣佈奧運會的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 。 這不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅動著我們 , 決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中的角色所需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks , 異議者 , 冒險家 , 外人和叛逆者 , 他們會問問題 , 彎曲規則 , 冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的人 , 不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	只會做出好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育館的綠色房間裡 , 我遇到了其他的旗幟熊:三位運動員 , 還有演員susansarandon和蘇菲亞羅倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	另外 , 兩個有著熱情心的女性:wangarimaathai , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種了三千萬棵樹 。 藉由這麼做 , 她改變了土壤 , 天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然還有許多村莊的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	索瑪莉•瑪姆 , 一位柬埔寨激進份子 , 他熱切地對抗兒童妓女 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她14歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣到一間妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 他們相信和很小的處女做愛 , 會治癒愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	還有妓院 , 在那裡 , 兒童被迫每天收到5 , 15個客戶 , 如果他們反抗 , 用電力來折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在我收到的綠色房間裡 ,
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的那種衣服 , 但它離我所預期的米其林人套裝很遠 。 真的 , 不差 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但 , 大部分的旗幟也是如此 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 美麗和熱情的普遍象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很渺小 , 又很高 , 有很深的坦率 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你怎麼能有深水池 , 沒有皺紋呢 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當在電視面試中被問到: 「 她怎麼能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直的 , 我不製造老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	這裡你有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有痛苦 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有輪子 , 沒有跟你自己說話 , 沒有摔角 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜附近的某個時點 , 我們被喚醒到體育館的翅膀 , 大聲說話者宣佈奧運旗幟 , 音樂從這裡開始 , 同樣的音樂 , 從這裡開始 , 艾迪亞遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高 , 不算大頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 就像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 肩上拿著旗子 。 我在我的尖端背上開車 , 手臂上拿著旗子 , 讓我的頭其實在該死的旗子下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都是在蘇菲雅 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	那對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也出現了 , 雖然在蘇菲雅的雙腿間 , 常常是如此 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大多數男人都樂意成為的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘是奧林匹克體育館裡的那些 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我的丈夫在我說這句話時被冒犯了 , 雖然我向他解釋過 , 我們私底下的做法通常只花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自承認 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有那四分鐘的按下按鈕 , 因為我不想忘記它們 , 當年老人破壞我的腦細胞時 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著奧運熱情的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	所以 , 以下是關於熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	年度是1998年 , 地點是剛果圖西難民的監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順帶一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是婦女和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以在剛果稱這個地方為死亡營 , 因為那些沒有被殺死的人 , 會死於疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 羅絲•馬丁多 , 和她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和寡婦
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵迫使她看她的丈夫被折磨和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她想辦法讓她七個孩子活著 , 幾個月後 , 她生下早產的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用一根棒子切斷了這根麻痺線 , 用自己的頭髮將它綁起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她把雙胞胎的名字命名為 「 難民營的指揮官 」 來獲得他們的贊助 , 用黑茶來餵飽他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵闖進牢房來強暴她最年長的女兒時 , 她會抓住她 , 拒絕放手 , 即使他們拿著一把槍到她的頭上 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知何故 , 家庭存活了16個月 , 接著 , 透過非凡的運氣 , 和一位年輕美國人的熱情心 , 薩夏.查諾夫 , 想辦法把她放進一個美國救援機、玫瑰、她的九個孩子 , 最後到達亞利桑那州的鳳凰城 , 在那裡 , 他們現在生活和蓬勃發展 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	mapendo , 在斯瓦希里語中 , 意味著很棒的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我的書裡的主角是強而有熱情的女性 , 如玫瑰般的女子 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不把它們組成 , 不需要這樣 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看得到他們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在和女性一起工作 。
i know them well .	我很清楚他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代 , 在世界末日 , 在父權天主教和保守派家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪 , 五歲時 , 我是個憤怒的女權主義者 , 雖然這個名詞還沒達到智利 , 所以還沒人知道我有什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 要為我的自由付出很高的代價 , 也要質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出代價 , 因為對我收到的每一擊 , 我都能夠遞送兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒寶拉在她二十幾歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會的 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有難忘的戰鬥 。 女權主義是約會的嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒一樣有特權的女性 , 今天在座的各位 , 但不是在世界上大部分的姊妹 , 仍然被強迫過早婚、妓女、強迫勞工──她們有孩子不想要或無法餵飽的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	無法控制自己的身體或生命 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、被毆打、有時被殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對現今大部分西方年輕女性來說 , 被稱為 「 女性主義者 」 是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有很性感 , 但讓我向你保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我也曾經因為缺乏男性而遭遇過 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義沒有死 , 沒有任何意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經演化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 為了女神的真理 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	叫它aphrodite , 或金星 , 或bimbo , 或你想要的東西 ; 名字不重要 , 只要我們了解它的內容 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	所以 , 這裡是另一種熱情的故事 , 這是悲傷的一個 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉村裡的一個小婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	一年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是年輕的美國牙醫衛生專家 , 在她的三週假期間 , 她去了診所當志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她已經準備好要清潔牙齒了 , 但當她到達那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一個滿滿是蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一行的女性 , 已經等了好幾個小時才被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人正處於令人痛苦的狀態 , 因為她有好幾個腐爛的臼齒 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮了解到 , 唯一的解決方案就是拔掉壞牙 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有被授權給這一點 ; 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒了很多風險 , 而且感到害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有合適的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她也帶來了一些不合適的樂器 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有個勇敢且充滿熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她謀殺了一名禱告 , 帶著手術走 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 解脫的病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生學家會抽出更多的牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一位病人正在和丈夫一起等待她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	這位女士的臉看起來像個西瓜 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它是如此的腫脹 , 以至於你根本看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫 , 憤怒 , 威脅要殺死美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她做過的事感到害怕 , 但後來翻譯解釋病人的狀況和手術沒什麼關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打她 , 因為她沒有時間為他準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性像這樣生活著 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人中最窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然世界上三分之二的勞動人口卻擁有少於百分之一的全球資產
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水比男性還少 , 如果他們付錢 , 他們仍然很脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 且他們不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	這是一個事實 , 給予女性教育、工作 , 控制自己收入、繼承和自身財產的能力 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予權力 , 她的孩子和家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai到肯亞的一個村莊
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女談話 , 解釋這塊土地是貧瘠的 , 因為她們已經割掉並賣掉樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女種植新的樹木並澆水 , 一滴一滴 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五、六年間 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤被豐富 , 村莊被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最倒退的社會總是把女性放下 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而 , 這個明顯的真相卻被政府忽視 , 也被慈善事業所忽視 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	給予女性計畫的每一塊錢 , 有二十塊美金 , 給男性計畫 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們能力 , 將改變一切 , 勝過科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性一起工作 , 連結、知情、教育 , 能將和平和繁榮帶給這個破碎的星球 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	今天在任何一場戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡者都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 她們是相對的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑遍世界 , 看看我們遇到的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大部份人在問的根本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	是否合理地參與既有的世界秩序 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個生命被保存的世界 , 生活品質被豐富到每個人身上 , 不僅是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月的一月 , 我看到了fernandobotero在加州大學柏克萊圖書館的畫展 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了帶著鮑特羅的作品之外 , 還敢展現畫作因為主題是阿布格拉伊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們是強烈的酷刑和權力濫用的畫作 , 用大量的波特羅風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法從腦海或心中得到那些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的 , 是有力量的 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖會定義現實 , 迫使包中的其他部分接受現實 , 並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時隨地改變 , 但他們總是受益於他們 , 在這個案例中 , 棘手的效應 , 這在經濟上行不通 , 運作得很完美 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待會從梯子的頂端到下方 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和小孩 , 尤其是窮人 , 都在底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最殘酷的男人 , 也有他們能虐待女人或小孩的人 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我用性別、收入、種族 , 及階級的少數運動能力來強化 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時代是要在我們的文明中做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 為了真正的改變 , 我們需要女性化的能源在全世界的管理上 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要關鍵數量的女性在權力的位置 , 我們需要培養男性中的女性能源 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的是有年輕心智的男人 , 當然 ,
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人是沒有希望的 ; 我們得等他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很樂意擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和傳奇性的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若有選擇 , 我寧願讓華加里•馬塔伊的戰士心 , 索瑪莉•瑪麗 , 珍妮和蘿絲•馬爾多 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得更好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 但要讓它變得更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 這是有可能的 。 看看在這個房間裡所有的這些知識 , 能源 , 人才和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們來脫掉我們的粉絲 , 捲起袖子 , 去工作 , 熱情地 , 在創造一個幾乎完美的世界中 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦這麼大的城市裡 , 有三千萬份餐點是被服務的 。 但所有的食物來自哪裡 ? 建築師卡洛林•史黛爾討論了日常飼養城市的奇蹟 , 並顯示古代食物路線如何塑造現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	carolynsteel:食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	如何養活一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的一個偉大的問題 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然 , 若我們進入一間商店或餐廳 , 或是在大約一小時內進入這個劇院的碼頭 , 將會有食物在那等待著我們 , 神奇地來自某處 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為每一天在倫敦這麼大的城市裡 , 足夠的食物必須被生產、運送、買、賣、煮、吃、丟棄 , 類似的東西每天都要發生 , 對於地球上的每一座城市來說 , 都很了不起 , 城市會被餵飽 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在像這樣的地方 , 彷彿他們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘了這一點 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃東西 , 我們其實和我們古老的祖先一樣依賴自然界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們更多人搬進城市 , 更多的自然世界被轉化為非凡的景色 , 就像我身後的景色一樣 , 它是巴西馬托格羅索的黃豆田 , 以便餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非比尋常的景觀 , 但是我們很少有機會看到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	漸漸地 , 這些景觀不僅僅是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們更多人搬進城市 , 我們當中有更多人在吃肉 , 所以全球有三分之一的穀物會被拿來餵動物 , 而不是我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物實際上要十倍的穀物來餵飽一個人如果它是透過動物先通過的話 , 那就不是很有效率的餵飽我們的方式 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	而且這也是個正在增加的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計我們的人數將會在城市中生活兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	同時也估計 , 肉類和乳類所消耗的兩倍之多 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和城市化手段都在上升 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	那將會是一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 餓了60億的食肉動物 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	那是個大問題 。 而且實際上如果我們繼續我們 , 這是我們非常不可能解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有十九百萬公頃的雨林流失 , 以創造新的耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時我們也失去了相當多的現有的可耕物來將鹽化和侵蝕掉 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望石化燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	大約需要十卡路里來生產我們在西方所消耗的每卡路里食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有很大的成本生產的食物 , 我們其實並不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國目前生產的食物有一半是丟棄的 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	要結束這一切 , 在這漫長的過程結束時 , 我們甚至還不能夠妥善地供應食物給地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人是肥胖的 , 而有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	都不太合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為全球百分之八十的糧食貿易現在只受五個跨國企業所控制 , 這是一張嚴峻的圖片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們進入城市 , 世界也在擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	而如果我們看看未來 , 這是種不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	那我們是怎麼走到這一步的呢 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答這個問題比較簡單 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 正是這個過程的開始 , 在古老的東方 , 也就是所謂的 「 肥沃 」 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近期的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	同時也是肥沃的 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前就在這裡 , 兩個非凡的發明 , 農業和都市主義 , 大約在同一個地方 , 同時發生 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市是互相限制的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先第一次發現穀物 , 製造出足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久居住地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看那些定居處是怎樣的 , 我們看到它們是相同的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被生產性農場的土地包圍 , 被大型寺廟複合 , 像在烏爾這一類 , 實際上 , 是精神化 , 中央食品分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是神殿組織了收穫 , 聚集在穀物裡 , 提供給眾神 , 然後提供了神的穀物 , 讓神不吃東西給人民 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活都被穀物和收穫所支配 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	而事實上 , 每個古老的城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有人都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	在西元前一世紀 , 羅馬約有一百萬的公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	那麼 , 像這樣的城市是如何飼養的呢 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古老的食物哩程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以取得海洋 , 這使得它能從很遠的地方進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代 , 唯一可以做到的方法 , 因為要把食物運送到馬路上是非常困難的 , 這很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬有效地在類似卡森林和埃及之類的地方發動戰爭 , 只為了取得它們的穀物保護區上的爪子 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張有點長 , 把軍事化購物的速度 , 真的很長 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到這個:羅馬其實是以前從倫敦來的牡蠣 , 在一個階段 , 我想那是非凡的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬透過它的胃口塑造了它的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事情也發生在工業前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物從泰晤士河流進來 , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 穀物市場到了城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	這條道路從他們身上向上邁進 , 那是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以知道300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	魚也是一樣的 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也來到河裡 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , billingsgate , 著名的是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期 , 一直到現在為止 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	真的 , 這麼說真的 , 真的 , 當你仔細想想 ,
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他所有人都用手機在遊蕩 , 看起來像磚塊 , 有點像在港口下的魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是關於城市的另一件事:一旦它的根部進入城市 , 它們就很少移動了 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是很不一樣的故事 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	很多倫敦的肉來自西北部 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它就進來了 , 抵達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常有名的肉品市場 , 位在那邊 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家長從東安格利亞來到東北部 , 到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我感覺有點像天氣女子在做這件事 。 不管怎樣 , 鳥兒們都帶著他們的腳來保護小畫布的鞋子 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們撞到便宜的東端時 , 這就是他們被賣的地方 , 這就是為什麼它被稱為 「 家族 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看任何城市的地圖 , 在工業時代之前 , 你可以追蹤食物來到那裡 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你實際上可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造的 , 兩者都通過閱讀街道的名字 , 這給了你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街上 , 在以前的人生中 , 就是你星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是食物唯一被買賣的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的照片 , 你可以看到 , 生活在這樣的城市中 , 很難知道你的食物來自何處 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在吃星期天午餐時 , 你的窗戶外面的機率大概有三天左右 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	然後十年後一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年偉大西方的圖像 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客都是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 ,
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被從視力和心靈中屠殺 , 在鄉下的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並藉由鐵路進入城市 ,
and this changes everything .	而這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 首次要發展城市 , 任何大小和形狀都有可能 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	以前 , 城市會受到地理的限制 ; 以前 , 它們得要透過很困難的實體手段取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 他們有效地從地理學中解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	從這些倫敦地圖上可以看到 , 在火車來臨後的90年裡 , 火車出現後的90年間 , 它從一個小小的斑點 , 很容易餵飽動物 , 以此類推 , 到一個大的海綿上 , 要餵飽任何人 , 要不就是動物 , 要不就是人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 在火車到來之後 , 火車結束了這個過程 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市最終的解放 , 來自任何與大自然的明顯關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是那種缺乏嗅覺、缺乏混亂的城市 , 肯定是缺乏人力的城市 , 因為沒有人會夢想在這樣的地景下走路 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了獲取食物 , 是在他們的車上 , 開車到外面的某個箱子 , 帶著一週的購物回來 , 想知道地球上有什麼可用 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這正是我們與食物和城市之間的關係時 , 改變的時刻 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡有食物 , 以前是市中心 , 邊界的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	曾經是社交活動 , 購買和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 ; 現在我們只會加水 , 或一點點卵 , 只要你在做蛋糕 , 或什麼 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們聞不出食物來看看吃是不是沒關係
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是把標籤的背面讀進包裝上 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不重視食物 , 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是去評估它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的最諷刺之一 , 就是他們已經做出了他們承諾要讓更困難的事 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓城市在任何地方或任何地方都可以建造 , 它們其實已經讓我們和我們最重要的關係距離了 , 那就是我們和自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	同時 , 它們也讓我們仰賴只能提供的系統 , 如我們所見 , 都是無法持續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯更問自己的事 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的前方 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	而那是一系列的半獨立城市 , 如果這聽起來遙不可及 , 一天的走路 , 每個人基本上都是農夫 , 在他們的後花園裡種蔬菜 , 一起吃溝通餐點 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的基本原則 , 即便從來沒有這麼框架過它 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另一個非常有名的 「 烏托邦 」 遠景 , 伊貝納霍華德 「 菜園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列的半獨立城市 , 一小塊大都市的東西 , 周圍有可耕地 , 透過鐵路加入彼此 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物可以被說是他視覺的秩序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建立起來了 , 但和默斯克韋茲擁有的這個遠景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是烏托邦的想法的問題 , 他們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是托馬斯•摩爾故意使用的一個詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	那是個笑話 , 因為它是從希臘來的雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能是指一個好地方 , 或不存在的地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想 。 這是個想像的東西 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 用來思考人類鑽研的深層問題 , 這讓它不太用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 就是西奧比亞 , 來自古希臘 , 「 西托斯 」 的 「 食物 」 , 以及 「 多巴斯 」 的 「 地點 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到這一點 , 我們可以用食物作為一個真正強大的工具 , 一個概念的工具 , 設計工具 , 來塑造世界的方式 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們要這樣做 , 衣索比亞可能長什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我認為它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我得用這張投影片 。 只是狗的臉上看了一看 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是生活中心的食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌、被享受 , 人們為此花時間 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是我們社會中食物應該在哪裡 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不可能有這樣的場景 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順帶一提 , 這些也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	是那些想到食物的人 , 想到領先的 , 誰計劃 , 誰能盯著一堆原生的蔬菜 , 並且真正認得它們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為若沒有這類人 , 我們就不可能有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我刻意選擇這個 , 因為它是一個人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但在當地種植食物的網絡、市場
it's common . it's fresh .	它很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	是城市社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為 , 若沒有這些 , 你就無法擁有這種地方 , 當地種植的食物 , 同時也是地景的一部分 , 而不只是在一些不見得見的地獄裡的零和商品 。
cows with a view .	帶著一個觀點的牛
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽堆積的嗡嗡嗡聲
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	基本上這就是把整件事集合起來 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區項目 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 孩子們對食物說的全部 , 種自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一株叫做凱文的植物 , 或者它屬於一個叫凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類計劃試圖與大自然重新連結 , 是極度重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 西托邦是種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 它是在認識到 , 到處都已經存在於小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅在於要加入他們 , 用食物作為一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這麼做 , 我們將不再將城市視為巨大、大都市、無生產力的團塊 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 成為有生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們是無可避免的 , 具有共生關係的一部分 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這也不是很棒的圖像 , 因為我們需要不要再製造這樣的食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更加考慮永續農業 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張影像為我總結了我們需要做的那種思考 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	是重新概念化食物形塑我們生活的方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像 , 是來自650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂的 「 好政府的寓言 」 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	關於城市與鄉間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這其中的訊息是非常清楚的 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧全國 , 國家會照顧該城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要我們問的是 , 阿姆布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂如果他今天畫了這張影像 , 會有什麼樣的畫 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好政府的寓言會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	它是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的就是
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要意識到 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採取這個想法 , 我們可以用食物作為強大的工具 , 來將世界形塑得更好 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	在21世紀 , 同情心推出的憲章幾週後 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯探討宗教的角色:它的教條會分裂我們嗎 ? 或者 , 它會讓我們團結起來嗎 ? 她會評論能驅動世界的信仰 , 來重新發現黃金法則的催化劑 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted大獎 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , tedglobal2009年 , 暴力事件
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重生黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直感到沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我變得敏銳地意識到在所有主要世界裡同情心的核心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個都演化出自己的版本 , 所謂的黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它會出現一個正面的版本: 「 總是在你想要被對待自己時對待所有人 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 , 「 不要對別人做你不喜歡他們對你做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看自己的心臟 , 發現是什麼讓你感到痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 去感染別人的痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	而人們強調同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來不錯 , 而是因為它有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施黃金法則時 , 如同蘇格魯斯所說的: 「 整天、每一天 , 」 不僅僅是為你做好事的一個問題 , 然後回到貪婪和自負的人生 , 日復一日 , 日復一日 , 你將自己從你的世界的中心 , 再把另一個放在那 , 超越你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它會帶你進入所謂的神、涅盤、拉瑪、泰歐的存在 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的自我存在的東西 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來都不知道 , 這對宗教生活來說是如此的核心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有幾個很棒的例外 , 很常見 , 當宗教人士聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 他們在爭論抽象的教條 , 或是說出仇恨的理事會 , 或對抗同性戀或類似的事情 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不真的想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和一群宗教人士談話時 , 有點像自閉症的表情 , 跨越他們的臉 , 因為人們常常會想要對 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	那當然會打敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我對ted這麼感激 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書線研究中帶我進入二十一世紀 , 讓我能和更廣的聽眾說話 , 比我想像中更廣泛 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不想辦法實行全球的黃金法則 , 以便我們對待所有人 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 都好像我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 把他們交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務之一 , 我們這個時代的一個偉大任務 , 就是建立一個全球社會 , 如我所說 , 在那裡 , 人們可以在和平共存下一起生活 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 反而被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種有想像力的同理心行為 , 把自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有一個選擇 , 對我來說 ,
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們要麼繼續下去 , 要麼強調我們信仰的教條和不寬容的面向 , 要麼我們能回到拉比.希爾 , 那個較年長的耶穌 , 當一個帕根教徒 , 他站在一條腿上時 , 說: 「 這對你來說是討厭的 , 不要對你的鄰居做事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這是托拉和其他一切 , 只有評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	還有教堂的早期父親和教會的拉比他說任何解讀都認為他們是不合法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要讓那精神重新復甦 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不僅會發生 , 因為愛情的精神將我們推倒 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切實現 , 用ted所引進的現代溝通方式來實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們所有伴侶的反應感到極大的鼓舞 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人 , 要用憲章來治癒分裂 , 最近在新加坡社會已經出現 , 國會的一些成員想要在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家將帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 向他們展示 , 同情心也在所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區都在舉辦活動和討論 , 討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰中的同情心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在那兒 。 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教義 , 這是我們出了錯的地方 , 只靠相信抽絲剝繭的教條來集中精神 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教導一定會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	而且我打算在這個直到我死去的日子裡工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想繼續跟伴侶們一起做兩件事教育並刺激同情心的思考
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們如此退出憐憫之心
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為這意味著對某人感到遺憾 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但 , 當然你並不了解同情心 , 如果你只是想一想 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須去做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能讓媒體參與其中 , 因為媒體是關鍵 , 協助解析我們對其他人的一些刻板印象觀點 , 也就是將我們從彼此分開 。
the same applies to educators .	教育工作者也同樣適用 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能感受到活力、充滿同情心的生活方式的動態和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到 , 它需要敏銳的智能 , 而不只是一種高奧妙的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想呼籲學者們 , 用他們自己和其他人的傳統來探索同情心主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許 , 最重要的是 , 鼓勵一種對於無情說話敏感度 , 以至於人們有這種憲章 , 不論他們的信念或缺乏它們 , 他們都覺得有能力挑戰不自在的言論 , 不自信他們的宗教領袖 , 政治領袖 , 來自產業的船長 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把憲章放在網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還困在舊世界裡 , 有一大堆的棺材坐在一間房間裡 , 還在發表另一篇論文 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	而ted也向我介紹了一種全新的思考方式和呈現想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為那是ted這麼美好的東西 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識 , 如果我們加入全部 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時看起來很不可思議 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我想引用一句話 , 結束前 , 提到一位英國作家 , 一位牛津作家 , 我不太常引用c.s.lewis 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一句話 , 自從我讀的時候 , 心裡想著一件事 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的書《四個愛人》中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他區別了愛情 , 當兩個人凝視 , 拼字 , 進入彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他比較了友情 , 當兩個人站在一旁 , 肩並肩 , 雙眼固定在共同目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不用愛上彼此 , 而是可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	而我深信
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我強烈地感受到 , 在我們在調查的小小考慮中 , 當各種不同的說服者聚集在一起 , 一同努力 , 共同的目標 , 差異會融化 。
and we learn amity .	而我們學會了 「 真誠 」 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會一起生活 , 了解彼此 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。

sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時候我會畫很多圖 , 仍然不明白我在畫什麼 。

everybody knows carletto , because he's in entertainment , actually ; he's in television .	大家都知道卡雷托 , 因為他在娛樂 , 其實他在電視裡 。
he's actually in television repair , which is why people know him .	他其實是在電視修復中 , 這就是為什麼人們會認識他 。

enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入庭院 , 和客服人員談話 , 他告訴他 , 在帕拉佐索發生了一場災難 ; 沒有人的電視節目工作 , 有一場大型足球比賽出現了 , 群眾越來越不安 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他下到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後逐漸地工作到建築物頂端 , 透過公寓 , 檢查每一台電視機 , 查詢每一個連結 , 希望能找出這個問題是什麼 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他往上走 , 終於 , 偉大的樓梯 , 然後一個更小的樓梯 , 直到他抵達閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 有張桌布包裹著建築物的電視天線 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除它 , 問題解決了 , 普拉佐的每個人都很開心 。

all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在只需要用一張完美的桌子 , 等著她到達 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但似乎不足以傳達我想要傳達的羅馬 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我就想 , 嗯 , 我來做個比亞zas , 我會進入下面 , 展示這些東西在成長 , 展示為什麼它們會被塑造成它們的樣子等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我會把我最喜歡的位元和碎片放進萬神殿裡 , 讓它保持尺度 , 所以你可以看到聖提歐的頂部 , 還有凱斯提烏斯的金字塔 , 以及布拉曼特的殿堂 , 放在這個令人驚奇的空間中 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	現在那是一張圖 , 所以我想也許是時候讓皮拉西認識escher了 。

there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條很薄的藍色精疲力竭線穿過這個東西 , 有點像是把所有東西都結合在一起的小徑 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不僅是一個整齊的收集和儲存資訊的方法 , 而是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層剝下來 ; 我們把它們看成是頁面 , 用某種方式來做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但 , 把它們想成是層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是層次的地層 , 垂直層次 , 我心想 , 如果我把一個頁面壓開 , 可以讓你用正確的角度來說明 , 可以讓我向你們展示層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大樓的牆壁上大部分的牆壁都覆蓋著疤痕 ; 數世紀來這些結構的疤痕已經適應而不是被撕毀 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個折疊頁 , 讓你將它展開 , 你可以看到它背後的意思是疤痕組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 做出較小的窗戶是很重要的 , 因為壞人來了或其他的 。

but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我也能給你們看 , 在那些壯麗的建築物的角落 , 上面有大量的石塊 , 或是用磚頭和黏土做的假石塊 , 比較常見的情況 。

" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進展 」 震撼了我 , 把我當成抓狂的頭銜 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果是一隻致敬的鴿子 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。

it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	是一隻坐在教堂頂上的鴿子 ,
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天去做正常鴿子的東西 。 回來 , 整個地方被支架和綠色網環覆蓋 , 沒有辦法讓鴿子回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是一隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 牠要找另一個地方住 , 這讓我可以通過我最愛的東西的目錄 , 我們從比較高的一開始 。

and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有個人應該以某種方式參與這件事 。

and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	最後他終於得到足夠的力量 , 爬上梯子到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 一個紅色的氣球 , 在那裡等著他 , 他們把他帶到城市的牆壁上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:每當他失去一隻鴿子時 , 他就會把那隻鴿子從城市的牆壁上取出 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在舊的羅馬習俗中 , 死者從來沒有被埋在牆壁裡 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我以為這是個很歡呼的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長的路 。

and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	鴿子飛到appian的上方 。

if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你看到的是鴿子的小徑 ; 如果你看不見紅線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時此刻 , 它變得有必要且可能性 , 試圖傳達那種飛越城市的感覺 , 不需要真正移動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了審核金字塔--這些看起來對你來說很熟悉 , 即使你最近還沒去過羅馬的門廊 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的東西 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件事情 , 大部分的鴿子都不會做的事:它需要一條風景路線 , 那是我覺得有必要的裝置 , 才能將這本書延伸到大約四頁的範圍之外 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞著羅馬競技場 , 穿過哥斯麥德林的聖塔瑪利亞教堂 , 以及海克力斯神廟 , 朝河流前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和帕拉佐佐族人物相撞 , 由米開朗基羅所設計的米開朗基羅 , 由羅馬競技場採用的石頭 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰campodefiori 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事 , 因為它是完全的基礎化 , 否認任何的觀點規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的觀點規則是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出消失點在哪裡 ; 一對夫妻在火星上 , 和其他幾個在克雷門拉 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但進到聖馬利亞的廣場前面的廣場 , 那裡無可避免地有足球比賽正在進行 , 我們被足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這張圖是被足球擊中可怕的插圖 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的碎片:有聖塔馬利亞.德拉的腳步 , 有足球 , 有一點鳥的翅膀沒有發生 , 所以我不得不重新思考它 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你真的想看聖母馬雅雅的步調 , 這些書真的很有彈性 , 極具互動性 , 只是把它轉過來 , 用另一種方式來看 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們可以看到它的影響在紅線內捕捉到 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥類會把自己拉過去 , 在這中世紀的高塔中 , 少數幾個中世紀的高塔之一 , 直到聖母堂的教堂 , 及圓頂上 , 向下看 , 向下看 , 我們已經提到、看過、飛過、飛過了幾次 ; 四條河流的山頂上有一座中世紀雕像 , 接著 , 穿過了美妙的聖母堂 , 停在萬神殿的直徑足以捕捉我們的呼吸 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們可以在裡面不斷轉換 , 因為我們在飛 , 我們真的不用擔心重力 , 在這個特定的時刻 , 這樣這幅畫可以在頁面上以任何方式引導 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會得到一個小小的自發性 , 並不讓人意外地模仿這個建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	穿過一面美麗的牆 , 充滿了我剛剛談到的混搭 ; 美麗的雕刻設置在 「 新月球 」 標誌上的牆壁上方 , 諸如此類 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最終 , 我們抵達了帕拉佐索的庭院 , 那是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓的一扇小窗戶 , 在那裡 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把訊息從鳥的腿上移開 ; 這是它所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著繪圖板 , 我們看到他正在努力的 , 事實上 , 是鴿子剛剛拍攝的旅程的地圖 , 紅線會延伸到所有的視線 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只需要閱讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院研究員天空兔會自行組合這個想法 , 與其建造一些東西 , 我們可以創造出能自行建造的材料 , 大多是一股dnazips本身的方式 。 這是早期階段的大概念 ; tibbits向我們展示了三項暗示未來可能的樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylartibbits:我們能做出製造自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向各位展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快我們的建築物和機器就會自行組合、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要向你們展示我相信的 , 是目前製造的狀態 , 然後將它和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在目前製造的狀態下 , 我們有摩天大樓2.5年的時間 , 50萬到100萬個零件 , 相當複雜 , 新的 , 令人興奮的科技 , 鋼筋水泥 , 玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年的時間 , 250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒內折疊 , 或有三十億個鹼基對的dna , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 在我們的自然系統中 , 所有這些複雜性 , 但它們極度有效率 , 遠比我們能建造的任何東西都更有效率 , 遠遠超過任何我們能建造的東西 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們的效率遠高很多 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以自己修復長壽命 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以自然系統有一些超有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以將之轉化為我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們建造東西的方式有一些令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的實體環境中自行組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 讓我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將之解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的零件 , 可以用它來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能讓它啟動的能量 , 讓我們的零件能夠從程式中折疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的錯誤矯正措施 , 來保證我們已經成功地建立我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看幾個項目 , 是我和我同事在麻省理工學院的同事正在致力於實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩個是macrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些計畫是大規模的可重組機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	嵌入機械裝置 , 感應器
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼了你想要折疊的是什麼 , 變成一連串的角度 , 負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120種類似的東西 ; 所以一連串的角度 , 或轉過來 , 將序列傳送到弦中 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都要收到它的訊息 , 負120個轉到那邊 , 檢查它是否到達那裡 , 然後再傳給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	所以這些是傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師 , 在這個項目上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想這真的能帶來光明:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美金 , 許多人小時製造出這個八呎高的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能擴大規模嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人技術嵌入每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 看看被動的自然 , 或被動地嘗試重新配置程式化 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 試圖有實際的計算能力 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它會把最基本的電腦構件 , 數位邏輯閘 , 直接嵌入你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是一個nandgate
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一顆四面體 , 就是那扇門 , 它會做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是使用者的輸入 , 如同你在建造你的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一個則是從之前的磚塊放置出來的 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要磚塊做的事上插上 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它運算出它之前所做的事 , 以及你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三度空間中移動 , 上下或下移動 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以 , 在左手邊 , [1 , 輸入等於0的輸出值 , 會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入是1個輸出值 , 會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	真正的意思是 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的東西的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有嵌入在他們身上的東西 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	所以這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個情況下 , 我稱它為自拍複製 , 因為你的結構包含了確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 可以取代一個部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都嵌入來告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以 , 你可以有東西爬上去 , 讀取它 , 可以在一比一的情況下輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外界指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	所以最後一個我要展示的項目叫做偏見鏈 , 它可能是最令人興奮的例子 , 就是我們現在擁有的被動自我組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它需要重組性和可程式性 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都完全相同 , 而且它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每條鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要向右轉或向左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上就是在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每個單位是否應該向右轉或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以 , 當你搖晃鏈時 , 它會折疊成任何你編寫的配置 , 在這個案例中 , 一個螺旋 , 或者在這個案例中 , 兩個立方體在彼此旁邊 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以把任何立體的形狀或立體的形狀編寫到這個鏈子上完全被動 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們關於未來的什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我想 , 這告訴我們 , 有新的可能性可以自行組合、複製、修復在我們的物理結構、建築物、機器上 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部分有新的可程控性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那之後 , 你就有了新的計算能力 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間運算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚頭都能實際計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的平行和分散式的運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以對此是令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我在這裡展示的這些項目只是朝向這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們為一個新的自我組裝世界實施這些新技術 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了非洲大陸 , 我們甚至去過海底最深處的兩次 。 下一代要探索的是什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家內森.沃夫菲提出了這個答案:幾乎所有的事情 。 我們都能開始 , 他說 , 海平面上空無一物的世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森.沃夫特:還有什麼可以探索的呢 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我拜訪了威斯康辛州的貝洛特市 ,
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡向一位偉大的20世紀探險家roychapmanandrews致敬 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , 安德魯斯領導了一系列的探險 , 去未知的地區 , 就像在戈壁沙漠這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	他後來 , 有人說 , 印第安那瓊斯角色的基礎是
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛特市時 , 我給一群中學學生做公開講座 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 如果在ted演講中有任何比這裡更令人生畏的東西 , 它會試圖把一群人的注意力放在45分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但在那之後 , 有一個問題真的困住了我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們應該在哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為有種感覺 , 許多人都有探索地球的偉大時代已經結束了 , 對於下一代 , 他們得要去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到很顯著的東西來探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	我們真的沒有什麼能讓我們在地球上探索的意義嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想一下生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是一名探險家martinusbeijerinck
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以beijerinck開始發現菸草鑲嵌病的成因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是 , 他從菸草植物中取出被感染的果汁 , 透過越來越小的過濾器過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達了一個點 , 認為那裡一定有比當時所知的細菌還小的生命形式 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他想出了一個他的神秘探員的名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 病毒拉丁文 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在發現病毒時 , beijerinck真的為我們打開了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道 , 病毒構成了我們星球上絕大多數的基因信息 , 比所有其他形式生命形式的基因信息加起來還多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很顯然 , 這種世界已經有極大的實際應用 , 例如天花的消滅 , 一種對抗子宮頸癌的疫苗 , 我們現在知道主要是由人類乳腺病毒造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這並不是五百年前發生的事情 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	早在一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們不知道我們星球上大部分基因資訊的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些了不起的工具 , 讓我們可以探索那些看不見的世界 , 例如深度定序 , 讓我們可以做得更多 , 不僅僅是從特定物種的表面 , 觀察各個基因組 , 而是觀察整段時間 , 微生物群落 , 在我們周圍 , 記錄所有這些物種的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技巧用在從土壤到皮膚的事物上 , 以及中間的所有東西上 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們會定期這麼做 , 找出造成疫情爆發的原因 , 恰恰是造成疫情的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上拿來了一支鼻子 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常做的事 , 來尋找像流感這種呼吸道病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們首先會看到的是大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 我們會發現很多人類的基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒資訊 , 大部分是從你鼻子內完全無害的事物中得到的 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了非常非常令人驚訝的事情 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現你鼻子裡大約百分之二十的基因信息並不符合我們以前看過的任何東西 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒 , 或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們根本不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	而對於我們這一小群真正研究這類資料的人 , 我們當中少數人開始稱之為資訊生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前看過的任何東西 , 有點像是我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡百分之二十的基因信息是很多生物暗物質如果我們看著你的腸道 , 高達百分之四十或五十的信息是生物暗物質
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	甚至在相對較為嚴重的血液中 , 大約百分之1到2的信息是暗物質無法被分類 , 無法和我們之前看過的任何東西打字或配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為或許這就是人造物 。
