these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序工具相對是新的 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得越來越準確時 , 我們已經判定這些資訊是一種生命形式 , 或至少有些是生命形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設 , 其實只有在它們的嬰兒時 , 存在著一種非常令人興奮的可能性:埋藏在這個生命中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 都是存在著尚未認知的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串a、t、c、g時 , 我們可能發現一種全新的生命 , 像是beijerinck , 會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	也許可以讓我們找出癌症的成因 , 會影響我們 , 或找出我們不熟悉的疫情來源 , 或在分子生物學中創造出新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興能宣布 , 和史丹佛大學、加州理工學院的同事們 , 我們目前正在開展一個計畫 , 來探索生物暗物質 , 為生命的新形式存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百多年前 , 人們不曾意識到病毒 , 組成我們星球上大部分基因資訊的生命形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能驚嘆到我們可能完全沒意識到一個新的生命階級就在我們的鼻子底下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能已經描繪了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能已經發現了所有存在的哺乳類動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的那種人為下一代的探險家提供了很重要的一課 , 像是來自威斯康辛州的貝洛特市的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為如果我們說出這門課 , 會是這樣的:不要假設我們目前認為的內容是完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	去追尋任何你選擇探索的領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊都有未知數 , 等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家daviddeutsch將理論物理置於後葬器上 , 討論一個更急迫的事情:我們物種的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	daviddeutsch在我們在宇宙中的位置
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出肢體 , 說出令人驚訝的事情 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以 , 我會試著這麼做 , 但我想從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	第一種 , 事實上 , 大部分都以歷史為名 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是 , 地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們所處的環境 , 都是獨一無二的適合維持我們的進化或創造 , 如同它曾經被思想和我們現在的存在 , 以及最重要的 , 我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	如今這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這個想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是不可或缺的 , 內部就是我們所擁有的 , 我們所依賴的 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只能得到一個機會:如果我們搞砸了太空船 , 我們就沒別的了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家都已經知道的是 , 和大部分人類歷史中所相信的相反 , 人類並不是 , 事實上 , 存在的樞紐 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬•霍金所說 , 我們只是一個典型的行星表面的化學污垢 , 繞著一個典型的恆星繞行 , 就是在一個典型的星系的外裙上 , 以此類推 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	現在所有人都知道的第一件事 , 有點像是在說我們處在一個很不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的服裝等等 , 第二件事是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你把這兩者視為是深刻的真理 , 來告知你的人生決策 , 那麼他們似乎有點像互相矛盾 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們兩者都完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是的 。 所以 , 讓我從第二個開始 。 嗯 , 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 讓我們看看四周 , 隨機看著一個方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學污垢 , 完全不典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所要做的就是往同一個方向走幾百英里 , 回頭看 , 你不會看到任何牆面或化學污垢 , 你看到的只是一個藍色的星球 。 如果你再進一步看 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系、太陽系、恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但那仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為星系裡有恆星 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	而宇宙中的大部分地方 , 一個典型的地方 , 在宇宙中 , 幾乎沒有任何一個銀河系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 我們再進一步探討 , 直到我們在外星系 , 再往回看 , 是的 , 有著巨大的銀河系 , 背著螺旋手臂躺在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	在這個時點 , 我們已經有十萬光年之久 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然在宇宙中典型的地方附近 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 要到達一個星系間空間的1000倍之多 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那這看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方看起來像什麼 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在巨大的花費中 , ted已經安排了一種高解析度沉浸在星系間空間中的虛擬實境呈現了從星系間空間的觀點 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能不能把燈關掉 , 拜託 , 我們能看到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	不太完美 , 不太完美 , 在星系間的星系間空間是完全黑暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你正看著最近的恆星向你看 , 那顆恆星正以超新星的形式爆炸 , 而當它的光線到達你時 , 你仍然無法看見即使是一顆超新星 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙有多大和多暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超級新星是如此的明亮 , 如此一來 , 它會殺死你數光年的石頭 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間來看 , 距離你甚至看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也非常寒冷 , 在絕對零度上不到三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而且它非常的空洞 。 真空的密度比地球最高的真空密度還要少一百萬倍 , 我們目前最好的科技能夠創造出來 。 所以這就是一個和這個地方的典型空間有多麼不同 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	而這就是這個地方的典型方式 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 請把燈光放回去嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	那麼 , 我們如何知道一個距離如此遙遠、如此不同、如此外星的環境呢 ? 從我們習以為常的任何事物中 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球我們的環境 , 以我們的形式在創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這意味著什麼呢 ? 嗯 , 比我們剛才所說的更進一步--我是說從這裡 , 用望遠鏡 , 然後你會看到看起來像星星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 quasars 」 。 quasars原本的意思是夸斯托爾物體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	意思就是 , 看起來像恆星的東西 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 數十億光年之遙 , 一個銀河中心的物質瓦解成一個超大質量的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場引導了那重力崩塌的一些能量 。 其中一些物質 , 以極大的噴射流束的形式 , 以我認為是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學幾乎不可能像這種噴射機的物理學 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法立即存活下來 。 語言破解了當試圖描述其中一架噴射流束會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這會有點像經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在時間範圍和數百萬年間 ,
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這種噴射流發生在數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述、模型 , 然後預測 , 然後解釋 , 以上總會有你的參考資料 , 在現實中發生了什麼事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	其中一個實體系統 , 大腦 , 包含另一個立方體的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是它的一個超級平面形象 , 它也包含了這個 , 一個解釋式的模型 , 體現了相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人的話 , 那個結構的信心會隨著時間而增加 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那些實體物體 , 儘可能與彼此不相像 , 不論如何 , 都能體現同樣的數學和因果結構 , 隨時間 , 都能做得越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是化學污渣是不同的 。 這種化學污垢是通用的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含了不斷的精準度 , 所有事物的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 是一個包含在自己內部的樞紐 , 包含了整個物理現實的結構和因果本質 。 到目前為止 , 物理定律允許這個 , 或甚至是強調 , 這是物理世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼 , 太陽系和我們的環境 , 以我們與宇宙其他地方的形式取得了這種特殊的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 關於史蒂芬•霍金的論點 , 我是說 , 這是真的 , 但這是錯誤的強調 。 一件事是真的 , 它沒有用任何特殊的物理來做 。 沒有特殊的解析度 , 沒有任何奇蹟 。 它只是用三樣東西來完成 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中之一是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 無從得知的製造電腦的方法 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能源來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體能夠有效地記錄我們發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	接著 , 第三點 , 比較不有形 , 但對於知識、解釋的開放式創造是很重要的 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好可以進行測試 , 比如說 , 牛頓的重力定律大約是300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但過去數十億年來 , 我們所做的證據都落在地球的每平方米上 , 在那之前 , 數十億年 , 將會持續下降 。 所有其他的科學也是一樣的 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真理的證據 , 僅僅是為了我們星球上的真理而已 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間裡 , 那些開放式創造知識的先例 , 最低的可能供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說 , 它是空的 ; 它是冷的 ; 它是暗的 。 還是它 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一個狹隘的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個立方體存在於星系間的空間裡 , 和我們的家園一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體是非常空的 , 但這仍然意味著它包含了超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	比方說 , 一百萬噸就足夠製造一個自給自足的太空站 , 裡面有一群科學家 , 致力於創造一個開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 科技超越了從星系間空間收集氫氣到其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果物理定律不被禁止的話 , 那麼 , 有什麼可能可以阻止我們去做 , 除非知道如何 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是關於知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們可以自動取得能源供應 , 因為交易會是核融合反應爐和證據呢 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 再說一次 , 它對人類的感官來說是黑暗的 。 但你只需要拿一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是現在的設計之一 , 向外看 , 你會看到和我們從這裡得到的一樣的銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	用更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將能看到恆星 , 和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將能夠進行天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡你可以在當地建立粒子加速器 , 並學習基本粒子物理 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最難的科學可能是生物學的實地考察之旅 , 因為要花上數億年才能到達最近的有生命的星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你們 , 很抱歉 , 理查德--但我從來沒有像生物學領域一樣--我想我們只要每幾億年就能完成一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間的確包含了所有開放式知識的先例 。 任何一個立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何一個角落 , 都有可能變成我們所在的樞紐 , 只要我們知道如何在那裏展現的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不是處在獨一無二的敵人之處 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間的空間有能力創造出一個開放式的解釋流 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境也是 。 所以地球也是一個受污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而有限的因素 , 在這裡和這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充足 , 但知識 , 卻很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個以宇宙知識為基礎的觀點 , 可以讓我們覺得非常特別 。 但這也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有必要的具體知識 , 就能撐過宇宙的挑戰 , 我們就不會撐過它們 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	它只需要一個超新星 , 才會消失幾光年 , 我們都會死掉 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁.雷斯最近寫了一本書 , 內容是關於我們對各種事物的脆弱 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出錯了 , 最重要的是 , 用大規模毀滅性武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明在這個世紀只有50%的機率存活下來 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他稍後會談到這點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為機率是正確的類別來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他所說的 , 我們可以生存 , 卻無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這取決於不是偶然 , 而是我們是否在時間內創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不是史無前例的 。 物種隨時都在滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明會結束 。 絕大多數的物種和所有曾經存在過的文明 , 現在都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想要成為例外 , 那麼我們唯一的希望就是用一個特點來區分我們人類的物種 , 和文明 , 即我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造出新解釋的能力 , 新的知識來當存在的樞紐 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我現在把它應用到目前的爭議當中 , 不是因為我想要倡導任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是說明我所指的那種東西 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	現在 , 我是物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 。 根據全球暖化 , 我只是一個層次而已 。 而對層次人來說 , 理性是認真看待先例的科學理論 。 根據那個理論 , 已經太遲無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們現在最好的選項就是用京都議定書來預防二氧化碳排放 , 加上對經濟活動的約束 , 以及它巨大的成本 , 花費數千億美元 , 不管是什麼 , 那就已經是任何合理的措施 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而那些被提倡的行動 , 甚至沒有被迫去解決問題 , 只是稍微貼上後面 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 可能已經太遲了 , 以致於任何人意識到危險之前就已經無法避免它 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代可能已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放量即將在數十億人將會消失的新冰河時期 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	現在這門課對我來說似乎很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼這不是公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們無法永遠知道 。 當我們知道一個即將發生的災難 , 以及如何用比災難本身少的代價來解決它 , 那麼真的不會有太多爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 可以避免我們尚未預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個解決問題的立場 , 而不僅僅是問題所在 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	事實是 , 一盎司的預防等於一磅的治癒 , 但只有在我們知道預防的情況下才會發生 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你已經在鼻子上被打 , 那麼醫學的科學並不會教你如何避免拳頭打 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學科學不再尋求解藥 , 只專注在預防上 , 那它也不會達到極少的成就 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	在當下 , 世界正在緩和 , 用計畫來迫使氣體排放 , 以各種成本來減少 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要用計畫來降低溫度 , 再加上計劃 , 計畫要在溫度更高的地方生活 , 不需要任何成本 , 但效率又廉價 。 這樣的計劃存在 , 像是太空中的一系列鏡子 , 來將陽光反射出來 , 鼓勵水生生物吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	在當下 , 這些東西是fringe的研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力面對這個問題的核心 , 也不是一般問題的核心 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們還沒意識到的問題 , 若要把正確的能力 , 不是無限大的避免運氣 , 就是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以拿兩個石器平板 , 然後刻在他們身上 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	在其中 , 刻上: 「 問題是足夠的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	而在另一張圖上: 「 問題是必然的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家如何能突破貧窮 , 如果它被困在一個不好的規則體系中 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默提出一個大膽的想法: 「 憲章城市 」 , 市政區被一個國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅•羅默的激進想法:查特城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看一下這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個非常引人注目的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的路燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有任何電力 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	現在 , 我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我遇過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠色上衣的那位 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢打賭尼爾森有一支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森有接觸到尖端科技 , 像是手機 , 但卻沒有辦法接觸到一百歲的科技 , 用來在家中產生電光 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	現在 , 用一個字來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以預防類似的雙贏解決方案 , 當人們可以把新科技帶進去 , 讓他們可以在像尼爾森這樣的人身上取得 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在規則下運作 , 說它必須以非常低、補貼的價格銷售電力事實上 , 一個價格低到幾乎低於它銷售的每個單位 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它沒有資源 , 也沒有誘因 , 讓許多使用者聯繫起來 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到 , 有可能有不同的規則 , 企業賺取小額利益的規則 , 所以他們有一份誘因 , 讓更多客戶簽名 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這就是手機公司nelson從操作中購買的那種規則 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統已經看過那些規則如何運作良好 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變用電價來定價的規則 , 但卻碰到一場抗議 , 來自企業和消費者想要保存現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他陷入了規則 , 阻止了他讓雙贏解決方案協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	而尼爾森則困在街燈下研究 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是 , 試著找出我們要如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	有一些我們可以發展的規則來改變規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想爭論的是 , 有一個普遍的抽象洞見 , 我們能做出實際的看法 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人更多的選擇 , 更多的選擇 , 給在許多國家的領導人 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 要呈現這兩者間的對立是很有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領導人的那種選擇 , 一個選擇 , 像是給總統選擇 , 提高電價 , 帶走經濟中人們想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇能夠持續補貼電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以 , 如果你只給一方或另一方 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到能給予兩者更多選擇的方法 , 那會給我們一組改變規則的規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , 尼爾森也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想要看到規則所造成的破壞效果 , 規則能讓人們保持在黑暗中 , 看看夜間從美國太空總署拍攝的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 線上這裡 , 和它的鄰居相比 , 這就像一個黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地知道北韓的規則會讓那裡的人保持在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是要了解 , 北韓和南韓開始時 , 有著一模一樣的規則 , 存在於法律和法規中 , 同時也是在更深層的理解、規範、文化、價值觀和信念上 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離時 , 他們做了選擇 , 導致了他們各式各樣的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以我們可以改變我們身為人類 , 可以改變我們用來彼此互動的規則 , 做得更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個區域 , 加勒比海地區 ,
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大到海地 , 線上這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 相較於這裡的鄰居多明尼加共和國 , 居民數量相同 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家相較於波多黎各有一半的居民是海地或多明尼加共和國
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是 , 規則可能會很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不單是規則不好 , 因為政府太強而壓迫 , 如同在北韓 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要創造出有好規則的環境 , 我們不能只撕下來 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也得找方法來建構 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大幅呈現出使用規則的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這張圖表上呈現的資料的開端 , 中國是世界高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人有先驅技術 , 像是鋼、列印、槍支 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則 , 來鼓勵那些想法的傳播 , 一種利潤動機 , 能鼓勵傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 減緩了創新 , 把中國從世界其他地方切掉 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界上其他國家的創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 也發展出更新的規則 , 中國人從那些進步中被切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入在那裡停滯不前 , 在世界其他地方放大時 , 還停滯不前 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表看得更近期的數據 ,
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它繪製了收入 , 中國的平均收入是美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到它大約在3%左右 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代末期發生了變化 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的成長起飛 。 中國人開始很快地趕上美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回到地圖上 , 你可以得到一個線索 , 引起中國在規則上劇烈的改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最明亮的地點 , 你可以看到在線的邊緣 , 是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的時候 , 都在一套截然不同的規則下運作 , 由當時的勞動市場經濟來複製 , 並且由英國執政 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 像是縫襯衫、製作玩具等工作 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了達到增加收入的過程 , 越來越多的技能 , 造成了非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個模式 , 像鄧小平這類的領導人可以複製 , 當他們決定把整個大陸移向市場模式時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但是 , 鄧小平直覺上明白了為他人民提供選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫中國的每個人立刻轉移到市場模式上 , 他們透過創造一些特殊的區塊 , 可以做到 , 在某種意義上 , 英國所做的:讓機會和市場規則合作 , 讓那些想要選的人都能參與 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近創建了四個特殊的經濟區塊:在那裡 , 中國可以來上班 , 都市長得很快 ; 同時 , 外國公司可以進來製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區 , 有一個城市叫做深圳 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有一間台灣的公司 , 讓在座許多人都擁有的iphone , 他們用中國的勞工從中國人搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特區之後 , 有十四個沿岸客群用同樣的方式打開 , 最後在這些地方 , 人們可以選擇的成功 , 他們會因為他們提供的優勢而被關起來 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	在那裡展示了成功的結果 , 導致了整個經濟體的市場模式的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在中國的例子顯示了好幾個點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	其一是:為人民保存選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	二:在正確的尺度上操作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村莊的規則 , 你可以這麼做 , 但是一個村落會變得太小 , 以至於如果有數百萬人都在好規則下工作 , 你就能得到的利益 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你就不能給一些人一個機會 , 看看事情會如何發展 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你這個機會 , 創造新的地方 , 有新的規則 , 讓人們可以選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	而它們的大小足以得到所有當數百萬人在好的規則下一起工作時所能帶來的益處 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提議是 , 我們對於所謂的 「 特區城市 」 概念的概念 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個憲章開始 , 指定所有規則 , 來吸引我們需要的人來建造這個城市 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引那些會建造電力系統、道路、港口機場、機場、建築物的投資者 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司 , 誰會先去雇用那裏搬來的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	而你需要吸引家人 , 那些將來會永久居住的居民 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 取得他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那張憲章 , 人們會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	而且我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再、再而三地
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它運作 , 我們需要良好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了這一點 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些在憲章中被捕捉到的
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型上 , 如果我們能夠在無人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從無人居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以生活在新憲章之下 , 但沒有人被迫住在它下面 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是對領導人的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們希望領導者的那種選擇 , 我們需要讓國家之間的合作的可能性:讓國家能一起合作 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式 , 首先 , 把市場模式放大 , 然後再擴大到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 無意中 , 透過它在香港的行動 , 比起上個世紀我們所建立的所有援助計畫 , 更能減少世界貧窮 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這種合作關係再次複製這一點 , 我們就能讓這類的利益擴展到全世界 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到負責任的權力 , 一個由一個國家的控制權 , 到另一個國家 , 來克服某些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我說這句話時 , 你們有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是回復殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是的 。 但很重要的一點是 , 當我們開始思考這些事情時 , 會出現的那種情緒 , 可以走在路上 , 可以讓我們拉回來 , 可以關閉我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義的不利之處在於我們的一些援助方案中 , 剩下的不利之處在於它涉及了強制和執行的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式都是關於選擇 , 不論是對領導者 , 或對將來居住在這些新地方的人來說 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	而且 , 選擇是強制執行和執行的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	所以 , 我們來談談這如何能在實踐中演出 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們以一個特別的領導人拉爾•卡斯楚為例他是古巴的領導人
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定發生過 , 他有機會為古巴做些 「 鄧小平 」 做的事 , 但他在古巴的島上沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他在南部有一點點光 , 那裡有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	那裡有一個區塊 , 在關塔那摩灣 , 在那裡 , 一條條約給美國一塊地的責任大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚去找加拿大總理 , 說: 「 看 , yankees有個很糟糕的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	你為什麼不 , 加拿大 , 接管呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立一個特殊的行政區
allow a new city to be built up there .	允許一個新城市在上面建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓附近的香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會抓住 。 但這將是將現代經濟和現代世界連結起來的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這模型還能在哪裡被試驗呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	其中許多人完全得到一個特殊區塊的概念 , 讓人們可以選擇成為一種規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	這是一種改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是創造新規則的一種方式 , 讓人們不受牽制 , 反對那些強制制制的反對者 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們能對長期投資者做出更有信心的承諾 , 那種會來到港口、建造道路的投資者 , 在一個新城市中 , 他們能做出更可信的承諾 , 如果他們能和一個夥伴國家一起做的話 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許就算是在一些安排中 , 有點像escrow帳戶 , 在那裡 , 你把土地放在伊斯蘭帳戶裡 , 同伴國也為此負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲也有許多土地 , 新的城市可以被建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我沿著海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的土地有著巨大的延伸 , 讓數以億計的人能夠居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們概括地思考 , 不只一個或兩個憲章風箏 , 而是數十個城市 , 來協助為數億人創造地方 , 也許數十億人搬到未來的城市 , 是否有足夠的土地供應給他們 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在整個世界 , 如果我們在夜間看亮燈 , 其中一件事就是 , 視覺上看來 , 世界上大部分都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我來告訴你為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把這代表全部的土地
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方塊 , 代表地球上所有可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表這個已經被三十億人口居住的城市所佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把圓點往下移到長方形的底部 , 你可以看到 , 現有的30億居民居住的城市佔地球上僅有3%的可耕地 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要為其他十億人口建造城市 , 他們會是這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們將從百分之三的可耕地 , 到百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大幅減少了地球上的人類足跡 , 藉由建造更多人們可以搬到的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是以良好規則管理的 , 他們可以是讓人民安全來自犯罪、疾病和不良衛生的城市 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到一份工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	可以取得像電力一樣基本的公用事業 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要建造第一座特許城市 , 要花什麼代價 , 才能建造更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	有助於手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們能做的是寫一些細節 , 可能會進入這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們跑城市 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者在野外發聲 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們思考一些問題 , 假設加拿大不只是和raulcastro做交易的 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西也是參與者 , 西班牙也一樣 。 也許古巴想要成為四向關閉風險的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫條約來這麼做 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	對此 , 前所未有的前兆 , 但很容易就能解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要怎麼資金 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港都是城市 , 在他們開始時所擁有的土地價值上取得巨大的收益 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用土地上的收益來支付像警察、法庭 , 但學校系統和健康照護體系 , 這也讓這個地方更有吸引力 , 讓這個地方的人有更高的收入 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 人們協助建構這個區塊的誘因 , 並設立基本規則 , 往正確的方向發展 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們如何能讓一開始工作的人低成本、負擔得起的建築物 , 像iphone一樣組裝 , 卻能讓那些建築物的能源效率提升 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會落在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節可以被找出來 , 但那些已經開始追求這些東西的人 , 已經可以知道 , 沒有道路、沒有障礙 , 除了沒有想像力的失敗 , 還能讓我們無法在真正的全球雙贏解決方案上實現 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來做結論 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能如此離譜 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為思想的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現它們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不像稀少物品 , 共享意味著我們每一個人都變少了 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那種方式思考想法時 , 通常我們會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:我們彼此互動的規則 ; 規則如 , 讓我們有一個支持一個研究大學的稅收系統 , 可以免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個系統 , 在那裡 , 我們擁有的土地在政府辦公室中被登記的土地 , 讓人們可以作為奴隸主 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能持續在我們規則的空間上創新特別是想出了改變規則的規則所以我們不會陷入不良的規則那麼我們就能不斷進步真正讓這個世界變得更美好讓像尼爾森和他的朋友不用再在街燈下研究的人們
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先驅克萊格•凡特從他史詩詩圓頂的探險中休息 , 來談談他團隊目前所發現的數百萬個基因 , 來繪製海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna , 生物圈 , 生物科技 , 企業家 , 基因 , 發明 , 海洋 , 科學 , 科技 ,
craig venter on dna and the sea	dna上的克萊格•凡特和海底 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我對老化論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	而這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解 , 樂觀主義者大過於悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我要告訴各位的是 , 在我18分鐘內 , 我們將如何從閱讀遺傳密碼轉換到開始寫程式碼的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	這個月僅僅是10年前當我們發表了第一組免費的有機體序列 , 由嗜血桿菌造成的流感 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	那花了一段長達13年的基因組計劃 , 到4個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以用兩到八小時的順序來完成同樣的基因計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以 , 在過去十年 , 大量的基因組被加入:大部分的人類病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲 , 以及數種哺乳類 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	大約十年前 , 基因組學在這個階段的思考階段是 , 到今年底 , 我們可能有三到五組基因組序列 ; 它的順序是幾百組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們今年剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金會得到了一個資金 , 將130個基因組排序 , 作為一個來自環境生物的副專案 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因編碼的比率已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎無法在這個星球上可取得的表面上找到了 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部份人都沒有意識到 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物構成了地球生物總共約一半的生物量 , 而所有的動物只佔所有生物總量的一分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人不太常做的事 , 但如果你曾經把它弄到海裡 , 吞下一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的海水中有大約一百萬個細菌 , 以及一千萬個病毒的順序 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前只有不到5000種微生物物種被視為特徵 , 所以我們決定對此做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了 「 蘇格爾二號探險 」 , 在那裡 , 我們和海洋探險一樣 , 試圖在200英里內取樣海洋 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始進行測試計畫 , 接著搬到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸工作 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿越加拉帕戈斯 , 穿越太平洋 , 現在我們正在穿越印度洋 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的職責 ; 我們在航海船上做這件事 , 部分是要協助興奮的年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只是拿海水來過濾它 , 我們在不同的過濾器上收集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們每24小時就能完成一億個字母的基因編碼 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉由這麼做 , 我們已經做出了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 有人認為我們眼中的視覺色素只有一、兩種有機體在環境中有著相同的色素
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎世界上溫暖區域的海洋上方的每一種物種都有同樣的感光受體 , 並將陽光當作它們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水 , 我們發現了130萬個新基因 , 和50 , 000個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經把這個延伸到空中 , 現在有了從史隆基金會得到的獎金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們在測量我們所有人每天都呼吸著多少病毒和細菌 , 特別是在飛機上 , 或是關閉式禮堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的儀器過濾 , 我們從紐約市的一棟建築物上收集到十億微生物的順序 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們正處於目前的測序過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	光是收集資料的一面 , 就在加拉巴哥群島的位置 , 我們發現幾乎每兩百英里 , 我們在海洋中的樣本中看到極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些是合理的 , 從不同溫度的梯度來看 ,
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 根據紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色是溫暖的 , 我們發現 , 溫暖的水樣本和冰冷的水樣本之間有極大的差別 , 以豐富的物種為例 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一個令我們驚訝的是這些感光受體會偵測不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些區塊有著巨大的變化 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不令人意外的是 , 在深海裡 , 那裡主要是藍色的 , 光感應器通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有很多葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們在極端的紅外線和紫外線也不同 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	只是為了試著得到一個評估我們的基因複製品 , 我們組裝了所有的資料 , 包括我們遠離探險的所有基因資料 , 它代表地球上一半以上的基因資料 , 總共大約有2900萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放進基因家庭 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們是否只是發現已知家庭的新成員 ? 還是發現新家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但是我們在環境中所採集的每個新樣本都在線性時尚上加入這些新家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	因此 , 我們正處於這個星球上最早發現基本基因、元件和生命的最早階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看著所謂的演化樹時 , 我們在右上角和動物在一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在那兩千九百萬個基因當中 , 我們的基因體中只有大約兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物都聚集起來 , 我們大概共有不到三萬人 , 可能有十幾個或上千個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我看這些基因現在不僅僅是演化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在一個以基因為中心的觀點中 , 或許可以回到理查德•道金斯的想法 , 比起基因組的觀點 , 這些基因組件的構造不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 已經改變了差不多在過去十年或二十年間 , dna序列的速度 , 越來越快 , 非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組學是在1995年我們將第二組基因組定序回到1995年時 , 由mycoplasma生殖器完成的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤衫 , 上面寫著: 「 我心臟的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800個基因
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們簡單地問這個問題 , 如果其中一個物種需要800 , 另外500種 , 是否有一組較小的基因 , 可能組成一個最小的作業系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始做跨性別突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	變體只是基因編碼中隨機插入的小dna片段 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	而如果他們在基因中間插入 , 就會擾亂它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以 , 我們做了一張地圖 , 描述了所有基因 , 可以接受轉化插入 , 我們稱之為 「 不存在的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常重要 , 你只能根據環境中的環境來定義一個必要或不必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試採用更直接的智慧方法 , 用13個相關有機體的基因組做比較 , 我們試圖比較這些 , 看看它們的共通點是什麼 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現只有173個基因 , 共有13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了其中一種細胞寄生蟲 , 它的範圍擴大了更多 , 當我們研究了大約310年左右的核心基因 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	因此 , 我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 取決於你的觀點 , 從500的最低點到400個基因組 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法是建構一個人造染色體 , 和那些基因在其中的基因 , 我們必須以一種基礎的方式來做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片段中合成精確的dna是極其困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆.史密斯和克萊德.哈特奇森 , 我在這方面的同事 , 開發出了一種令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週內合成一個五千個鹼基對的病毒 , 只能在兩週的時間內達到百分之百準確 , 就它的序列和其生物學而言 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	那是個相當令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna , 注射到細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的生產 , 然後轉身殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這並不是第一個合成病毒--一個小兒麻痺病毒在一年之前就被製造出來了 , 但它只有十分之一的活躍 , 花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174結構的漫畫 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是軟體現在用來建造自己的硬體的案例 , 這是我們和生物學有關的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上跳到關心生物戰的那一刻 , 我在參議院委員會前有最近的證詞 , 以及美國政府設立的一個特殊委員會 , 來審查這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要保持現實是很重要的 , 要和人們的想像力相比 , 要是保持現實是很重要的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何今天已經被定序的病毒 , 基因組可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚訝 , 但來自這個生物體的dna並沒有傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做了天花基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	安全部門真正關心的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	而且只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯有著重大的努力試圖創造生物戰事代理人
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那項研究真的是不連續的 , 未來應該要有很少活動 , 才能製造出設計師病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為 , 單細胞生物體在兩年內可能
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	很可能 , 我們所擁有的那些細胞 , 在十年內就有可能實現 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以 , 我們現在正在製造數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變進入這個人造染色體的種類和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 要怎麼把所有其他人
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 接著 , 我們有一個同源重組系統 , 將它們重新組合成一個染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體衍生出來的 , deinococcusradiodurans , 可以承受300萬的輻射 , 且不會被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆炸後 , 它會在12到24小時內重新組合 , 在它的染色體被拆開之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種有機體在地球上普及 , 或許現在就存在於外太空 , 由於我們在那裏的所有旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一個玻璃作者 , 經過約50萬個輻射之後 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 而坐在底部的微生物卻變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這張圖是實際發生的狀況:這張圖的上方顯示了一百七十萬種輻射後的基因體 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體真的被打破了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動重組 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真正令人驚訝的是 , 這些生物體可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千種 , 如果不是這個星球上有數萬種不同的物種 , 可以做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合完成後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	因此 , 我們認為合成細胞將會具有極大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 也為了希望環境和社會的議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們定序的第三個有機體 , 甲烷jannaschii──它住在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫氣 , 它所有的碳來自於環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道很多不同的途徑 , 現在有數千種不同的生物 , 活在二氧化碳以外 , 還能捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其用石油來製造合成過程的碳 , 我們有機會用碳來捕捉它 , 從大氣中捕捉回來 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物 , 住在一氧化碳之外 , 我們用它作為減少水分 , 來產生氫和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有無數的路徑 , 可以被改造成甲烷的新陳代謝 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一個重大的方案 , 在挪威有雕像 , 用來捕捉和從氣體中將甲烷轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短時間內 , 我認為將會有一個新領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因陣列複合體 , 以及同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 來製造出也許一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 就像所有的生物學一樣 , 透過篩選 , 不論是用來篩選氫化生產 , 或化學生產 , 或只是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因所扮演的角色將會很好的接觸到 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試圖修改光合作用 , 直接從陽光產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們有一種氧氣敏感的氫氣 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在將纖維素結合 , 將複雜糖分解的酵素分解成簡單糖和發酵在同一個細胞中為了產生乙醇
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在使用微生物的大型實驗室中進行 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	來自環境中的化合物的化學成分比我們最好的化學家所能產生的更加複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為 , 未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環保的補救措施 , 或許取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策的研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年 , 我們延遲了實驗的開始 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 我們是否該嘗試製造一個人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與了這一點 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是一項非常奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖都在用他們的經文作為法律書籍 , 他們找不到任何東西禁止製造生命 , 所以這一定是沒問題的 。 最終的擔憂是生物戰的方面 , 但給了我們這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在sloan基金會剛剛資助了一項關於這方面的多元體制研究 , 找出對社會的風險和利益是什麼 , 以及科學團隊的規則 , 例如我自己的團隊應該在這個領域中使用 , 我們試著在向前邁進時設立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的問題 , 以解決問題的方式 , 我們是否能設計東西來生產清潔能源 , 也許革命化發展中國家能做些什麼 , 並提供各種簡單的過程 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•津巴多說 , 快樂和成功是根深蒂固的 , 我們大多數人都不認同:我們對過去、現在和未來的方向的依據 。 他建議我們準時校正我們的出發點 , 以改善我們人生的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理學、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利普•津巴多開了一個健康的開場即將要花上時間 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和各位分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的想法 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始時鐘 。 30秒鐘的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 。 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	大概是時間了 , 終點序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、5、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普•津巴多:讓我們調整一下亞當的校長對話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來到亞當 , 不要這麼老實 。 去咬一口 。 」 「 我真的做到了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一咬一口 , 亞當 , 不要放棄伊娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 ,
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 。 一咬一口 , 到底是怎麼一回事 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生是誘惑的 。 一切都是為了產出 , 抗拒 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 過後 , 衝動 , 反思 , 現在的焦點和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾美德會對當下的熱情墜落獵物 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	十幾歲的青少女 , 認為性缺乏和處女 , 直到結婚──謝謝布希──大多數人──60%──在一年內都對性誘惑產生了性行為 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們大部分都這樣做 , 沒有使用節育控制 。
so much for promises .	對於承諾這麼多 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們誘惑四歲的孩子 , 給他們一個療程 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然它會付錢 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 去等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	發生的是三分之二的孩子給予誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們等不及 。 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 為了稍後延遲現在 ,
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特•密歇爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 回到14年後 , 試圖發現那些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 都存在著巨大的差異 , 那些反抗生育的孩子 , 在很多方面都一樣 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抵抗分數250分的孩子們 , 在sat上高出250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那很巨大 。 那就像一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上那麼多麻煩 , 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們很自信 , 且有決心 。 對我來說 , 今天的關鍵在於 , 他們是未來的目的 , 而非真實的 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間的觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個人、我們所有人 , 將你人類經驗的流動分為時間區或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而你會自動地、非意識地去做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	它們在文化、國家之間、個人之間、社會階級之間、教育程度之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們可能會變得偏見 , 因為你學會過度使用其中的一些 , 並造成其他的濫用 。
what determines any decision you make ?	什麼決定了你做出任何決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做一個決定 , 要做出一個行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在即時情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你感受到什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們用那種形式做出決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 簡化 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的樣子 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是關於 「 過去我經歷過什麼樣的情況 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會把這些人稱為 「 遺傳者 」 , 因為他們會把焦點放在原本的事物上 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 只和未來有關 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是關於預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們會稱他們為 「 未來優先 」 。 他們的焦點在於會是什麼 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想論一下 , 時間的悖論 , 是影響你所做的每一個決定 , 你完全沒有意識到的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	也就是說 , 到目前為止你有這種偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六種 , 有兩種方式可以呈現出來 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被遺傳 , 可以成為未來的兩種方式 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面 , 或者是負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是現任的 , 意思是 , 你把焦點放在生命的喜悅上 , 或現在的福利主義者──這無所謂 , 你的人生是被控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:即是 , 生命始於死後 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維的靈活性來轉移時間的觀點 , 取決於情況的需求 , 這就是你必須學會做的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時間表 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	很正面 。 很高的未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	和現代主義的調整 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	並且總是低於負面和當前的死亡主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的暫時性混合是你從過去得到的正向性給予你根源 。 你連結你的家人、身份 , 和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來你得到的就是翅膀 , 到新的目的地、新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義中得到的 , 是探索自己、地方、人、感官的能量 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過度看待過剩的時光 , 都有比正面更負面的看法 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來會為成功犧牲什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲了家庭時間 。 他們犧牲了朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲了好玩的時間 。 他們犧牲了個人的禮貌 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 。 而且犧牲了睡眠 。 所以這會影響到他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	並且為工作、成就和控制生活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信那會和一些ted成員產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	它對我產生共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯區貧窮的孩子長大 , 每個人都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來到這裡 , 身為一位未來優先的人 , 他們走過頂端 , 做所有這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那個棉花糖 , 因為如果你等一下你會拿到其中兩個 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加入了現在的自閉症 , 把焦點放在正面 , 所以 , 在七十六歲時 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 而且我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們正在應用在許多世界問題上:改變學校孩子的輟學率 , 結合成癮 , 增強青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻來治癒他們的創傷後壓力症候群 , 得到奇蹟的解藥 , 可以促進永續性和保育 , 減少身體復健的身體復健 , 讓自殺恐怖份子的比率下降了50% , 改善了自殺式恐怖份子 , 改善了家庭的自殺式恐怖份子 , 改善了當作是時間跨越過時區塊 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說的是 , 許多生命的謎題可以藉由了解你的時間觀和他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深刻 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今有多少標題會在一百年後才會發生呢 ? 1000年 ? 科克•克特朗的 「 長消息 」 專案計畫收集故事 , 不只今日重要 , 還會讓數十年甚至在ted2010年時 , 他還會提出近期的頭條 , 用潛力來塑造我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:而現在 , 真正的新聞
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞界淹沒 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社一年就播放了350萬則新聞 。
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:長期來看 , 有多少故事真的很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	它是現在長期基金會的一個計畫 , 由ted成立的 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華特品牌 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的 , 是新聞故事 , 可能在50、100、100 , 000年後仍然重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過那個過濾器看新聞時 , 許多地方都落在了旁邊 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	要從a.p.在去年 , 這將在十年內變成重要的事嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這會在50或100年內起到作用嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但 , 過去一年最頂尖的故事是經濟 , 我敢說 , 遲早 , 這個特殊的經濟衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	那麼 , 什麼樣的故事會為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 讓我們以科學為例 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血液 , 修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	有一天 , 如果你是老鼠的話 , 就已經在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	一些最近的故事:奈米小生物用真正的蜜蜂毒液來抽取腫瘤 ; 他們將基因送入大腦 ; 他們建造的一個機器人 , 可以透過人體爬行 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	那資源呢 ? 我們要如何供應九十億人口 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們現在有麻煩餵養六十億人 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人處於飢餓狀態 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國在沒有基因改造的農作物下會餓死 。
