bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲在 「 農業研究 」 上打了十億個 。
what about global politics ?	全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界會在什麼時候、如果中國設定了這個議程 , 他們會變得非常不同 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經把美國當成世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經把德國當作是最大的出口國 , 開始對孩子做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職業生涯 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們發現各式各樣的方法來推回我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些近期的發現:阿根廷有一隻螞蟻蟻群 , 現在已經散播到每個大陸但南極洲 ; 有一個自主的機器人科學家 , 很快就做出了一項發現 , 科學可能不再需要我們了 , 生命可能也不再需要我們了 ; 一個微生物在十二萬年後出現 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 或沒有我們 , 人生會持續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但是我在去年的長期新聞中挑出的 , 是這個:月球上找到的水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓上面的蜂群更容易 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署沒有做 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的某人可能會寫大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:在長期來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他人更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡羅林.普羅科所顯示的影像 , 從卡西尼航行到土星 , 專注在它最大的月球 , 泰坦 , 和冰凍的土衛六 , 似乎是射擊冰的噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 太空 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco讓我們飛去土星 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這趟旅程是你和我現在已經踏上多年的 , 五十年前 , 人類第一次踏出我們的星球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不僅僅是真的 , 在月球上擺了一腳 , 我們還把機器人的太空船和所有行星都拆開 , 我們登陸了小行星 , 登上了彗星 , 此時此刻 , 我們有一艘太空船 , 登上了冥王星之路 , 前所知的行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	而所有這些機器人的使命 , 都是人類旅程的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解某件事 , 去了解我們宇宙的地方 , 去了解我們的起源 , 以及地球 , 我們的生活 , 來到那裡 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	而在太陽系中 , 我們可能去找尋類似這樣的問題的所有地方 , 有土星 。 我們在1980年代初造訪土星之前 , 去過土星 , 但我們對土星的調查 , 從卡西尼號太空船開始 , 在七年間穿越星系間的太空旅行 , 滑行到土星軌道上 , 在2004年的夏天 , 成為了當時人類最遙遠的機器人發現 , 人類在太陽周圍有史以來最遠的發現 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是一個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的、科學的洞見 , 且顯然超越了比較 , 這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙接觸 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究光環 , 我們就能夠了解許多關於星星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張andromedanebula的美麗圖片 , 它是我們最接近、最大型的螺旋星系 , 到銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	接著 , 這裡是旋風銀河系的美麗成分 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程 , 真的是其中的一部分 , 也是人類航行的比喻 , 來了解我們周遭的一切 , 以及人類如何融入到那張圖片中 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	讓我很痛苦的是 , 我無法告訴各位 , 我們在卡西尼號身上學到的所有東西 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我不能給你們看過去兩年半我們拍的所有美麗圖片 , 因為我只是沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我將集中在兩個最令人興奮的故事中 , 出現在我們在土星周圍進行的重大探險旅程中 , 並在過去兩年半的時間裡進行 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星與月球的大型多樣化集合在一起 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的範圍從幾公里大小到像美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍過土星的大部分美麗圖片 , 事實上 , 用它的一些月球來呈現土星 。 這是土星和土星 , 然後 , 這是土星 , 邊緣是土星 , 邊緣是土星 , 邊緣是它的環形邊緣 , 向你展示它們有多薄 , 和月球土衛星土衛星有多薄 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47個衛星中有兩個是站立的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六和土衛六 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號到達那裡之前 , 最大規模的未被探索的地形 , 是我們太陽系中剩下的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這個身體有著長久以來的好奇心 , 觀看星球的人 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有一個很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像我們在地球上的環境 , 或者說 , 至少在過去 , 比太陽系中任何其他身體都要來的 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層大多是分子氮 , 就像你在這個房間裡呼吸一樣 , 只不過它的大氣層裡有簡單的有機物質 , 如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	而這些分子在土衛六的大氣層中升高 , 會被瓦解 , 它們的產品會結合在一起 , 製造出霧狀微粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這個霧狀物無所不在 。 它完全是全球化且包含了土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼你看不見我們眼睛的表面 , 在光譜的可見區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀粒子 , 被保存下來 , 在我們和卡西尼號一起到那裡之前 , 經過數十億年 , 溫柔地向下漂移到表面 , 將表面覆蓋在厚厚的有機液體中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以 , 就像相當 , 泰坦等於 , 焦油 , 或石油 , 或我們不知道的 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以在土衛六的表面溫度下成為液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是到土衛六去的 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	這在大氣層中是可以凝聚的 , 所以認知到這個環境帶給整個世界奇異的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在這些雲端上方有數百公里的霧狀物 , 可以防止任何陽光到達表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但 , 儘管冰冷 , 土衛六表面可能會有雨落下 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 雨會做的事:它會雕刻惡棍 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它能造出峽谷 ; 它能在大型盆地和隕石坑中池 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把泥巴從高山峰和山丘洗掉 , 下到低地 。 所以停下來想想一分鐘 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 土衛六上的高中 , 和地球上的深處一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	很冷 , 很生氣 , 很失誤 , 可能會下雨 , 你可能站在密西根湖邊 , 用油漆薄薄片來刺穿 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在和卡西尼號一起到那裡之前對土衛六的表面的看法 , 我可以告訴你 , 我們在土衛六上發現了什麼 , 不過細節不盡相同 , 都和那個故事一樣迷人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像是卡西尼號人 , 它就像是叢林的凡爾納探險 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有著濃厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是土衛六的照片 , 背著太陽 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	但 , 那裡的另一個月球 , 我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 它是一個非常廣大的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們有卡西尼號的儀器 , 可以透過大氣層看到下面的表面 , 我的攝影機系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	而你所看到的是明亮和黑暗的區域 , 差不多就跟我們一樣 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在是太神秘了:我們無法弄清楚我們在泰坦看到的景象 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你再仔細看這個區域 , 你會開始看到一些事情 , 像是連續頻道--我們不知道 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	這個 , 我們後來發現 , 事實上 , 一個隕石坑 , 但在土衛六表面很少有隕石坑 , 意思是它是非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來像地形 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來像是被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到行星上有任何線性的東西時 , 它就意味著有一個骨折 , 像是一個斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經被改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但 , 我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 發生了一場事件 , 很多人都認為是卡西尼號對土衛六的調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那是huygens探測器的部署 , 歐洲建設的huygens探測器 , 卡西尼號在太陽系內載了七年 。 我們將它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時 , 才降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調一下這個事件有多重大 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它首次在人類歷史上登陸太陽系 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	意義重大到 , 在我心目中 , 這種事件應該要在美國和歐洲的每個城市裡 , 用貼膠帶遊行來慶祝 , 可悲的是 , 這不是事實 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另一個原因的重要原因 。 這是個國際的使命 , 這場事件在歐洲 , 在德國 , 慶祝的簡報 , 在英語的口音 , 還有美國的口音 , 還有德語 , 法語 , 義大利語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是個移動式的展示 , 說明了 「 聯合國 」 應該要表達的意思:一個真正的聯合國 , 共同為善而努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個例子中 , 要探索一個星球是一項大規模的行星系統 , 要了解一個地球系統 , 對於所有人類歷史來說 , 一直是不可思議的 , 現在人類真的碰到了它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我是說 , 我只是在談它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極大的情感事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 你也不該忘記 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但無論如何 , 探測器在下面的路上對大氣層進行測量 , 同時也拍了全景圖片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴你 , 從探測器看出土衛六表面的第一張圖片是什麼樣子 。 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	那真是個震撼人心 , 因為那是我們希望那些從軌道拍到的其他照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是個很明顯的模式 , 地質圖案 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種垂直的排水模式 , 只能透過液體的流動而形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以跟著這些管道 , 看看它們是如何匯合的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	它們會匯集到這裡的通道 , 流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里處拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在八公里高的地方拍的 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大概是一架飛機高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機穿越美國 , 你就會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	所以 , 這是你在土衛六航空的窗口所擁有的圖片 , 飛過土衛六的航空 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器來到海面上休息 , 我要向各位展示 , 各位先生女士 , 第一張從外太陽系的星球表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	地平線是這樣 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水中的冰卵石 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 且它沒有從視線下沉 。 所以它並沒有被我們降落的流體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器基本上是等同於一個泥土平面的巨石 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是個不穩定的地面 , 和液態甲烷混合在一起 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	很可能這種情況是 , 這種材料已經清洗掉了土衛六的高地 , 透過我們看到的這些管道 , 流動了數十億年 , 來填滿低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯探測器登陸的原因 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 在我們的影像中 , 仍然沒有標誌 , 甚至在惠更斯的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體中都沒有 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 會變得更困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好的 , 這是我們拍的 , 泰坦的赤道區域 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘是100公尺高 , 被幾公里的距離隔開 , 持續了數英里和數英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	這裡有幾百個 , 高達一千或一百二百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 不然你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次 , 令人困惑的是 , 沒有體液的存在 , 直到最後 , 我們在極地地區看到湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	土衛六南極的南極地區有一個湖泊的場景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	差不多和安大略湖差不多大
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 僅僅一個星期半前 , 我們飛過北極 , 發現再一次 , 我們發現這裡有一個特徵 , 和卡斯皮亞海的大小一樣 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以看來 , 液體 , 基於某些我們不了解的原因 , 或至少在這個季節 , 在泰坦的極地位很明顯 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你們會同意我們發現土衛六是一個很了不起、神秘的地方 。 它很奇特 , 很奇特 , 但又像地球 , 又像地質的形成 , 又有著巨大的地理多樣性 , 一個令人著迷的世界 , 太陽系只為了複雜 , 豐富而對立的世界是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以 , 現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是一個小月球 , 它的尺寸大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它在英格蘭旁邊 , 只是要向你展示它的大小 。 這並不是一個威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二很白 , 很明亮 , 它的表面很明顯會被骨折折磨 。
it is a very geologically active body .	這是個地質非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但是 , 土衛二的發現之母在南極發現 , 我們在研究南極 , 這裡我們發現了這個裂痕系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	而它們是另一種顏色 , 因為它們是另一種組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是覆蓋的 。 這些裂痕是被有機物質所包裹的 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個區域 , 南極地區 , 已經增加了溫度 。 它是地球上最熱的地方 , 在身體上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	那就好比發現地球上的南極比熱帶還熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們拍攝額外的照片時 , 我們發現從這些裂縫中 , 正是清潔的噴射噴射流 , 冰粒將長達數百英里的太空 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們將這張圖畫上色 , 將微弱的光線帶出時 , 我們會看到這些噴射流射射線餵養一個多數 , 事實上 , 在其他影像中 , 我們會看到 , 在土衛二上方數千英里的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊檢查過像這樣的影像 , 就像這張 , 也考慮過卡西尼號的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是 , 這些噴射流有可能從土衛二表面下的液態水中噴發出來 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有 , 可能 , 液態水 , 有機物質 , 以及過度熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或是說 , 一個可能適合生命體的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	而且我不認為我需要告訴你們在我們太陽系裡其他地方的生命發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學涵義 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們可以證實 , 不只一次 , 而是獨立 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 那就表示 , 推斷 , 在整個宇宙中 , 它發生了很驚人的次數 , 以及它的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是我們所知的唯一行星仍然充滿生命 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 獨一無二 , 到目前為止 , 我們所知唯一的家園 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有人在1960年代時被警告及連貫 , 我們會原諒你們 , 如果你不是 , 好 , 你們會記得1968年阿波羅8號太空人拍的這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球是從太空拍攝出來的 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置產生了巨大的影響 , 以及我們對地球保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼號上 , 拍攝了相當於前所未見的圖片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是日全食 , 從土星的另一端看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張不可能的美麗圖片中 , 你看到太陽的主要光環 , 看到太陽的折射影像 , 看到這個光環 , 事實上 , 是由土衛二的引流所產生的 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 就好像這還不夠聰明 , 我們可以發現 , 在這個美麗的圖像中 , 看見我們自己的星球 , 爬到土星光環的手臂中 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 關於從遠處看我們自己有著深刻的動力 , 捕捉到我們在其他世界的小小藍色星球的景象 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而那 , 和我們從中獲得的自我的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這趟發現之旅中得到最好的獎賞 , 是在半個世紀前開始的 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	在2005年 , 全球只有15%被繪製出來 。 這種方式緩慢了救援的遞送 , 在災難發生後隱藏了未被使用的土地和未知道路的經濟潛力 。 在這個短短的演說中 , google的拉特加達的demos , 一個團體繪製的工具 , 讓全球的人用於繪製他們的世界地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	laliteshkatragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 旋轉納爾吉斯破壞了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人急需幫忙 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想趕人和供應到該地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有辦法協助到達居魯士的受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看一幅洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信 , 到2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地理位置相當的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國經營的頭燒 , 變成一個問題 , 世界上絕大多數的民粹臉孔:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但協助就要來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40個志願者用一個新的軟體來繪製出120 , 000公里的道路、3000個醫院、物流及緩解點的地圖 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一項科技 , 賦予我們每個人在地圖上繪製出我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這套軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從公路到河流、從學校到當地企業 , 及影片商店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎得主赫南多•德索托認定 , 對大部分發展中國家而言 , 經濟升空的關鍵在於要利用大量的無私土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	例如 , 一兆美金的房地產 , 單單在印度 , 仍然沒有被開銷 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 170個國家的數以千計的使用者就繪製了數以百萬計的資訊 , 並且創造了一張從來沒有想到可行的細節地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	而這是由各地熱情的使用者所造成的 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們來看看現在使用者所創造的一些地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 在我們說話的同時 , 在這個170個國家裡 , 人們正在繪製這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲剛剛繪製塞內加爾一條路的橋樑 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	而且 , 離家鄉 , chalua , 班加羅爾的一個n.g.道路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學的結果 , 手勢辨識 , 以及機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數千個用戶的勝利 , 在數百個城市 , 一個用戶 , 一次編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們百分之七十未開發的星球的邀請函 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落在布德魯斯登上了十個月的非暴力抗議活動 , 去阻止一座跨過他們的橄欖園的障礙 。 你聽說了嗎 ? 巴西的電影製作人朱利亞.巴哈 , 問我們為何只關注以色列國內衝突中的暴力事件 , 而不是有一天可能帶來和平的非暴力領導人 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:留意非暴力行為 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平手段來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是會出現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抵抗力 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	我聽到這個問題時所面臨的挑戰是 , 通常我剛從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花時間拍攝數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們使用非暴力來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和居民 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試圖鑄造一個龐大的國家非暴力運動來終結佔領 , 並在該地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 在座大多數人可能從來沒有聽說過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這個分裂在地面上發生的事和國外的感知是其中一個關鍵原因是我們目前尚未擁有的巴勒斯坦和平抗拒運動已經成功的原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以 , 我今天來到這裡 , 要談談注意力的力量 , 你的注意力的力量 , 以及非暴力運動的出現和發展 , 在西岸、加薩 , 及其他地方 , 但 , 現今 , 我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 要成長的主要缺乏非暴力 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力 , 而是要我們開始注意那些已經存在的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我用這點來說明一下 , 把你們帶到布德鲁斯村 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建立一個隔離屏障 , 而這個屏障的一部分會被建在村子上方 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地並被包圍 , 所以他們會失去西岸其他地方的自由取得 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導 , 他們發起了一場和平抗拒運動 , 來阻止這件事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你們對於在地面上實際的樣子有一種感覺 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女性:我們被告知牆壁會與以色列分離 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村 , 我們意識到牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男子:事實上 , 圍籬已經創造出了恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你受邀參加和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十位以色列兄弟姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列激進份子:沒有什麼比非暴力反對更嚇人軍隊 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但沒有一個人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須要把我們對傳統思維的思想給清除掉 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯派對成員:我們處在完全和諧的狀態 , 想要把它散播到所有巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	頻道:一個聯合國
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫 , 哈馬斯和受歡迎的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主播:在圍籬的旁邊會持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被送到散佈群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是活子子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	就像瓦魯賈 , 到處開槍 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列激進份子:我很確定我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊有其他人 , 甚至還沒有在煮飯 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:一個非暴力抗議不會阻止[不明] 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	蛋白質:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	頻道:我們能做到 ! 我們可以做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	juliabacha:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很驚訝 , 國際媒體沒有報導那些發生在七年前、2003年的非凡事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更讓人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功的事實 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民們 , 經過了10個月的和平抗爭 , 說服了以色列政府將障礙從他們的土地上移開 , 到綠線上 , 也就是國際認可以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗藥性自此蔓延到西岸的村落 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而 , 媒體仍然對這些故事保持沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會帶來深刻的後果 , 造成非暴力的可能性可能會成長 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦生存 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭共通點是非常重要的共通點 , 它們是劇場上的一種形式 , 尋求觀眾的目標 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一能持續得到封面的角色 , 並吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦議題 , 對非暴力領導人來說 , 這對他們的社區來說 , 公民不服從是可行的選項 , 來處理他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能對房間裡的父母來說是毫無意外的 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓你的孩子丟出越來越大聲的反羅姆斯 , 最好的方式就是給他注意 , 他第一次丟出一個符合你的孩子 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	反而會變成兒時心理學家所謂的 「 功能性行為 」 , 自從孩子得知他能得到父母親的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母只要給予孩子的注意力 , 就能激勵或激勵人心的行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為都能受到影響 , 取決於國際社群選擇集中注意力的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終結中東的衝突的核心 , 帶來和平 , 就是讓我們將非暴力行為轉變為功能性行為 , 做法是給予當今地面上的非暴力領導人更多的注意力 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在把我的電影帶到西岸的村落、加薩和東耶路撒冷的村落裡 , 我看過即使是一部紀錄片也能影響轉變的影響 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫瓦拉杰的村莊 , 坐落於非常接近耶路撒冷的村莊 , 社區面臨著和布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 沒有取得自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷都沒有 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力兩年了 , 自從沒人注意到 , 他們就被放棄了 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一個篩選器 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們舉辦了最有攻擊感和紀律的示威 , 到約會 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德鲁斯村的故事 , 在一部電影中 , 覺得確實有人在追隨他們所做的 , 有人在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列的這一邊 , 有一個新的和平運動 , 叫做 「 蘇里達里特 」 , 意思是希伯來語的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這個運動的領導人一直用布德鲁斯村作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導 , 以色列人從未積極活躍過 , 看電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰和團結運動的例子顯示 , 即使是小型的獨立電影也能扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力轉化為功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在想像一下 , 大媒體玩家可以擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週發生的非暴力示威事件 , 像是比爾辛、尼、瓦拉傑 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰里 , 像是謝赫•賈拉、西爾文──非暴力領導人 , 在他們的作品中變得更明顯、有價值、有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的事是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 就好像它們從來沒有發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我親眼見到如果我們有 , 他們會相乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們相乘 , 他們的影響力會在以色列巴勒斯坦的衝突中生長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力 , 終於可以解開局面 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人已經證明 , 非暴力在布德鲁斯村這樣的地方工作 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓他們注意 , 讓他們可以證明到處都行得通 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	賽蒙•史瓦克有一個簡單但強大的模型 , 可以激發領導力 , 都始於一個黃金圈 , 他的問題是 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果 , 馬丁•路德•金 , 還有萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導人 , 銷售 , 賣 , 成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	賽蒙•史瓦克:偉大領袖如何啟發行動 ?
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	要怎麼解釋當事情不如我們所假設的那樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的 , 你如何解釋當其他人能夠達成似乎全部的假設時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果電腦這麼創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 比他們所有的競爭都要創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的人才、相同的機構、相同的顧問、相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德金恩領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受苦的人 , 他肯定不是當時唯一偉大的演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出掌控權力、有權力的男人飛行 , 肯定還有其他團隊更有資格、更好的資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	而且他們沒有達到有權力的男人飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的玩意兒
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這項發現深刻地改變了我對世界運作的看法 , 它甚至深深地改變了我在其中運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果是 , 世界上所有偉大且鼓舞人心的領導者和組織 , 不論是蘋果 , 馬丁•路德•金恩 , 或他們都認為的萊特兄弟 , 採取行動 , 並以同樣的方式溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	和其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是把它編碼 , 這可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 如何 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠激勵別人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個術語 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每一個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道它們是怎麼做到的 , 不論你稱它為你所謂的 「 不同價值觀提案 」 , 或你的特性流程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但極少數人或組織知道他們為什麼要做的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	藉由 「 為什麼 」 , 我不是指 「 賺錢 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	那是結果 , 總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	藉由 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的成因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼早上要下床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	還有為什麼有人應該在乎呢 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果就是 , 我們的思考方式、行動的方式、溝通的方式 , 都來自於外在 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 。 我們從最清楚的東西到最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但鼓舞人心的領導者和鼓舞人心的組織 , 不論他們的大小 , 不論他們的產業都認為 , 行動 , 和向外溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果電腦 , 因為它們很容易理解 , 且大家都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 來自他們的行銷訊息可能會像這樣: 「 我們製造了很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們很漂亮地設計 , 簡單地使用和使用者友善地使用 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? " meh "
and that's how most of us communicate .	那就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷的方式 , 多數銷售都是如此 , 多數人之間的溝通方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們所做的事 , 我們說我們如何不同 , 或者我們如何更好 , 期待某種行為、購買、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師有最大的客戶 , 我們總是為客戶為我們做生意的客戶表演 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很好的氣體哩程數 , 它有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果是這樣溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓我們的產品設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用 , 且用戶友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是剛好製造了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不對 ? 你準備好向我買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是逆向資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明的是 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼要這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在場的每一個人都很舒服地從蘋果電腦購買電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很舒服地購買蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或蘋果電腦的電話 , 或是蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 正如我之前所說 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能區別他們和任何競爭者的結構性 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 蓋特way出了平面螢幕電視
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有資格製作平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	多年來他們都在做平面螢幕
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	dell帶著mp3播放器和pdas出去 , 他們會做出很棒的品質產品 , 可以做出非常好的設計產品 , 沒有人買一個 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦購買mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼要從電腦公司買mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標並不是要和每個需要你擁有的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我告訴你們的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都落在生物學的網狀物體中 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看一個人腦的橫切面 , 從上方看 , 你看到的是人腦其實是碎成三個主要元件 , 和黃金圈完美相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人大腦 , 我們的新皮質 , 和 「 什麼 」 的等級對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成了我們的邊緣大腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責我們所有的感受 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也要為所有人類行為負責 , 所有的決策 , 它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外界溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、利益、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它就是不驅使行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部傳達出去 , 我們就直接和控制行為的腦部交談 , 然後我們允許人們將它合理化 , 用我們所說及所做的有形的事情 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給某人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有的事實和細節都說什麼 , 但感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	我們為什麼要用那個動詞 , 它不會 「 感覺 」 對不對 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的大腦的部位無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們能追求的最好是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或有時你說你要帶著你的心 , 或是帶著你的靈魂領頭 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭把它分給你 , 那些不是其他身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	都發生在你的邊緣腦中 , 大腦控制決策的部分 , 而非語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你會做你該做的事 , 而人們會回應為什麼你會做你該做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們為你投票 , 或是向你買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 要忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是為了賣給需要你所擁有的人 ; 目標是要賣給相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你所相信的人們 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這樣說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用人們只是因為他們可以做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢而工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人們 , 他們會為你工作 , 帶著血汗和淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有其他地方比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人都不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初期 , 追求權力的人飛行就像是當時的網點com 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley曾經有過 , 我們假設 , 要成為成功的食譜 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或你的公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你同樣的三件事:不被鼓吹、不對勁、不對勁的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是一樣的三件事 , 所以讓我們去探索一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley得到了五萬美金 , 由戰爭部門找出這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	錢根本沒問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦了一個位子 , 在史密森尼亞工作 , 他非常有連結性 ; 他知道當時所有的大型思想 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的心智金錢 , 市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處走 , 每個人都在為langley而紮根 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	我們怎麼會從未聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里外的荷爾頓俄亥俄州 , 奧維爾和威爾伯萊特 , 他們都沒有我們認為的成就成功的配方 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們用自行車店的腳踏車來支付夢想 ; 萊特兄弟團隊中沒有一個人有大學教育 , 甚至沒有奧維爾或威爾堡 ; 紐約時報跟著他們到處走 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 奧維爾和威爾本被一個目標所驅使 , 由一個信念所驅動 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能弄清楚這台飛行機器 , 它會改變世界的過程 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 而且他想變得有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	再來 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟夢想的人和他們一起工作 , 帶著血汗和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只是為了付錢而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 每當萊特兄弟出去時 , 他們就得要拿五組零件 , 因為那是他們會在進來供應商之前墜毀的幾次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟飛行 , 甚至沒有人能體驗到 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們在幾天後發現
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	進一步證明langley的動機是錯的:萊特兄弟飛行的那天 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是個驚人的發現 , 各位 , 我會改進你的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他就辭掉了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但 , 為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂的 「 創新法則 」 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你肯定知道 「 創新法則 」 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前2.5%的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期的採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的多數 , 多數晚期 , 和你的落葉 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控式手機的唯一理由 , 是因為你不能再買轉動式手機 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在這個尺度的各個地方 , 但創新的傳播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功 , 或是大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你就無法擁有它 , 直到你達成這個臨界點 , 在15%到18%之間的市場滲透 , 然後系統就會轉折 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你對新生意的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡跟你說: 「 喔 , 大概是10% 。 」 很驕傲 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 可以超過百分之十的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約百分之十的 「 懂 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們形容他們的方式 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是那種直覺的感覺 , 「 喔 , 他們只能拿到 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何在和他們做生意之前 , 找到那些拿不到的人 , 和那些拿不到的人做生意 。
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 就是這個 , 這個你必須關閉的小缺口 , 就像傑佛瑞•摩爾所說的 , 「 穿越隔閡 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期 , 大部份不會在別人先試過 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 創新者和早期採用者 , 他們很自在地做出那些腸道決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更加自在地做出那些被他們所相信的世界所驅使的直覺決策 , 而不只是產品能取得的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊六小時來買iphone當他們第一次出門時 , 你可以在下個禮拜走進店裡買一個 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面螢幕電視上當他們第一次出來時 , 即使這項技術是後續的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順帶一提 , 他們並沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們為自己做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想要先
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 , 你做的只是證明你所相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	第一個人買iphone的原因在前六個小時內 , 排隊六個小時 , 是因為他們對這個世界的信念 , 以及他們希望所有人都能看到他們:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	所以 , 讓我給你一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 以及一個有名的成功的創新法則 。
first , the famous failure .	第一 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說 , 一秒鐘前 , 成功的食譜是金錢 , 是對的人民 , 以及對的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該有成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從八、九年前的tivo出發 , 到目前為止 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 雙手向下 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常有資金 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件非常棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我隨時都在我的垃圾時間華納的dvr上唱歌 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是商業上的失敗
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺過錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo時 , 他們的股票大約有30或40美元 , 然後跌倒 , 再也沒有超過10美元的交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它甚至是6歲以上交易的 , 除了幾個小突點以外 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品 , 可以暫停現場電視 , 跳過商業廣告 , 重寫現場電視 , 記下你的觀看習慣 , 甚至不問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	而憤世嫉俗的人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要 。 我們不喜歡 。
you're scaring us . "	你嚇到我們了 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 若你是那種喜歡完全控制你人生的每個面向的人 , 男孩 , 我們對你有產品嗎 ?
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視 , 跳過廣告 , 記憶你的視野習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 , 而你所做的事就只是證明你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你一個成功的例子 , 說明了創新法則的擴散 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的購物中心 , 來聽金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們送出去沒有邀請 , 也沒有網站來檢查日期 。
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 金恩博士並不是美國唯一一個很棒的演說家 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一一個受苦的人 , 他是美國人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟糕 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處走動 , 告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴別人 ,
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而相信他所相信的那些人把他的成果拿來做自己 , 告訴別人 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓這個詞對更多人來說更是如此 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	然後 , 25萬人出現在對的時間聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他出席 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出席 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們所相信的美國 , 讓他們在公車上旅行八小時 , 站在華盛頓的八月中央 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人對白:25%的觀眾都是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信這世界上有兩種定律:那些由更高的權威制定的 , 以及由人類所製造的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有由人類訂定的法律都與我們所居住的更高權威制定的法律一致 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好 , 民權運動是最完美的 , 能協助他將他的目標帶入人生中 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 的演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽政治人物 , 帶著他們全心全意的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有激勵任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導人 , 還有那些領先的人 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導人有權力或權威的立場 , 但那些領導的人卻鼓舞了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論他們是個人或組織 , 我們都跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	就是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 能夠激發他們周圍的人 , 或找到那些鼓舞他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你把你的車停在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你是否在正確的方向移動 ? 神經科學家尼爾•布洛吉斯研究那些繪製我們周圍空間的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結到記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neil埋怨:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個大型停車場時 , 我們怎麼記得我們停車的地方 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬面臨的問題是:
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	然後我們會試著去了解他的大腦裡發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	所以 , 我們先從海馬體開始 , 用黃色表示 , 就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你那裡有損傷 , 像在阿茲海默症 , 你記不住的東西包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它以拉丁文為名 , 以 「 海馬 」 來命名 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦其他部位一樣 , 是由神經元構成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人腦內大約有一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	而神經元彼此之間的溝通方式是透過互相連接來傳送小脈衝或刺激的電流
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞組成 , 非常密集的相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家們開始了解 , 空間記憶是如何運作的 , 透過從老鼠或老鼠的個別神經元中記錄下來的 , 或探索尋找食物的環境 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們會想像我們從一隻單個神經元在這隻老鼠的海馬體中記錄下來 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一個小小的電刺激時 , 會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到的是 , 這個神經元知道老鼠在環境中的某個特定位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	並藉由發送一個小小的電刺激訊號 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以把神經元的發射率當作動物位置的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中記錄下來 , 我們會發現 , 不同的神經元會在不同部分的環境中發射 , 就像在這個方形的盒子裡顯示的一樣 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們一起為大腦的其他部分建立了一張地圖 , 持續地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時會需要他們腦部監測的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	其中一些病人玩了一個電玩遊戲 , 他們在一個小鎮上開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	隨時開車穿過某個特定地點的細胞就會發出電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 一個位置細胞如何知道在其環境中的老鼠或人在哪裡 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界限特別重要
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	上面的這個 , 喜歡在他們老鼠在盒子裡的牆壁間開火 ,
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你把盒子擴大時 , 發射位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的那個則是 , 每當有一面牆靠近南方時 , 都會發火 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放進盒子裡 , 那麼細胞就在兩個地方 , 無論在哪裡都有一面牆 , 當動物在盒子裡四處探索時 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這預測了 , 在你周圍的建築物周圍的界線和方向 , 如此一來 , 對海馬體特別重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入情況下 , 細胞會發現哪些細胞進入海馬體 , 它的反應正是偵測邊界或邊緣 , 特定的距離和方向 , 從老鼠四處探索 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以 , 左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 它會發火 , 每當動物靠近一面牆壁 , 或向東邊的界線 , 不論是方形箱子的邊緣 , 或是圓形的牆壁 , 或甚至是桌子邊緣的一滴 , 動物會跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發出火線 , 不論是桌子邊緣的邊緣 , 或牆壁 , 甚至兩張桌子之間的缺口都被拉開 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以這是我們認為位置細胞在周圍探索時會決定動物的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物體的位置 , 像是這個目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或你的車會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看看他們必須記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們非常擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車子的位置上 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們在住宿細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那樣的情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變形狀和大小的功能 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 你可以看到 , 如果旗幟在一個小方形的環境中穿越 , 然後如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但你讓環境變大 , 他們認為旗幟已經被伸展到完全相同的地方 , 位置細胞發射的位置就會被伸展出來 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	就好像你還記得旗幟的位置 , 通過在那個位置定位的位置激發出的模式 , 然後你可以藉由四處移動 , 回到那個位置 , 這樣你最好配合你那個位置細胞的發射模式 , 用那個儲存的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過運動在哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 若我們採取一些外界的路徑 , 也許我們會停下來 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 我們可以整合這條路徑 , 大約會是前進的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從一個叫做網格細胞的細胞中得到這種通路的整合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在網格細胞被發現 , 同樣的 , 在海馬體的輸入上 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但 , 當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個細胞都在不同的位置上發射 , 會在一個非常規律的三角形網格中發射 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	若你從幾個網格細胞中記錄 , 這裡顯示的不同顏色 , 每一種都有類似網格的激發模式 , 每個細胞的網格激發模式都和其他細胞相對稍微相近 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的則是這張格子上的紅色 , 綠色的這張 , 藍色的這張 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 這就好像老鼠可以把一個虛擬的發射位置放到環境中 , 有點像你在地圖上找到的緯度和長度線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電流活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它的位置 , 讓它可以用自己的動作來知道它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	嗯 , 因為所有的網格激發模式都有相同的對稱性 , 相同的網格方向 , 在這裡顯示橘色 , 這意味著 , 在特定的網格細胞中所有網格細胞的淨活性 , 應該根據我們是否沿著這六個方向跑 , 或沿著六個方向跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進核磁共振掃描儀 , 讓他們像我剛剛給你們看的那個小遊戲 , 尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你確實在人類的大腦迴中看到的 , 和你在老鼠身上看到的網格細胞是一樣的 。
so back to homer .	所以 , 回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他大概會記得他車子的位置 , 就距離和方向而言 , 要在他停車的地方延伸建築物和界限 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會是由界線偵測細胞的發射所代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車公園取出的路徑 , 這會在網格細胞的發射中呈現 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞發電 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動 , 回到他停車的位置 , 找出哪裡是最好的位置 , 能符合目前他大腦中位置細胞位置的發射模式 , 和他停車的地方 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個位置 , 視覺提示的不尊重 , 像是他車子是否真的在那裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許已經過時了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去拿它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找這種網格狀的激發模式 , 我們會在一系列的位置中看到 , 當我們做各種自傳式記憶工作時 , 總是很活躍 , 比如 , 上次你去參加婚禮時 , 記得上次你去參加婚禮時 , 舉例來說 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 也許 , 代表我們周圍空間的神經機制 , 也被用來產生視覺圖像 , 這樣我們才能重現空間場景 , 至少 , 在我們想要想像它們時發生過的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞透過這些密集的相互連結開始活化對方 , 然後重新啟動界限細胞 , 創造出圍繞你的觀點的場景的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 頭部導向細胞 , 我還沒有提到 , 它們會像指南針一樣 , 根據你面臨的方向 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以用你想要的視覺影像來定義觀看方向 , 所以你可以想像當你在婚禮時發生了什麼事 , 舉例來說 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	所以 , 這只是一個新時代的一個例子 , 正是在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理過程 , 像是你如何記住、想像 , 甚至是以數十億個神經元構成我們大腦的行為來思考 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 在機構、政府、私人部門和大眾之間合作所驅動的全球安全性 。 這不僅是開放原始碼的粉絲們的遙遠希望 , 也是jamessteavridis的遠景 , 最高層的指揮官 , 他們分享了最近的軍事歷史中的生動時刻 , 來解釋未來的安全性 , 應該用橋樑來建造 , 而不是用牆壁來建造 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•斯塔維里迪斯:納托最高指揮官如何看待全球安全 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談一下開放資源的安全性 , 因為我們必須在21世紀變得更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說說 , 讓我們回顧二十世紀 , 稍微了解一下安全的風格如何為我們工作 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 法國的一個戰場 , 就在北方的比利時總部 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 超過300天的時期 , 有70萬人被殺害 , 所以一天大約2000人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你將它向前推進20世紀的安全 , 進入第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到史達林格的戰役 , 300天 , 2百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的壕溝戰爭 , 到第二次世界大戰的麥吉諾線 , 然後進入冷戰、鐵幕、柏林圍牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天為我們做的論點是 , 與其建造高牆來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲一座有名的橋 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是dina河流的橋樑 , 由ivoandrich所主題 , 它談到 , 在歐洲和巴爾幹半島的那一邊 , 經過一段時間 , 有著巨大的圍牆建築 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	更近期 , 在過去的十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫著 , 一起聚在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會主張 , 同樣地 , 開放資源的安全是將國際、跨國、私人連結起來 , 並將之與戰略溝通結合 , 主要是在社交網路中 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物在各種方面都在受到攻擊 , 沒有任何威脅到全球公有物的來源 , 都會透過築牆來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我是個水手 , 很顯然 ,
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一支線 , 翻過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張圖有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	沿著它的側邊有協奏曲線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	也就是防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜是現今全世界非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	piracy也非常活躍在馬拉卡的平面上
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	在幾內亞海灣裡活躍起來 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到的
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	在全球運輸系統中 , 花了10億美金的不連續性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 總共有20艘船 , 有500名馬林人質 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海域 , 網路海域 ,
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	目前 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們進行了一套信用卡詐欺 , 淨化了超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟中2兆美元的不連續性 。
two trillion a year .	每年有兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	那只是在英國的國內生產總值之下 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以 , 我們所知的這個網路大海 , 無止境地都是激進開放的基本開放 , 同時也受到威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	在全球公有物上 , 我擔心的另一件事是人口販賣所帶來的威脅 , 由毒品 , 鴉片類藥物 , 由阿富汗來到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心來自andeanridge北部的可卡因 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器和人口販賣的運動 , 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的成本 。
